For Azemena signifies a temporary bodily debility, such as deafness, blindness, loss of limbs, and other such things which a person will have as long as they live, unless miraculously healed. Therefore, if the Moon is in these degrees at the birth of a child, the aforesaid Azemena will befall him, according to the signification of the place and aspect or places of the planets. Azemena also signifies various things in different ways, as you will find in books of nativities. The Azemena degrees are those described in this table. Aries: 8, 6, 7, 8, 9, 10. Taurus: 1, 19, 29. Gemini: 1, 7, 8, 18, 19. Cancer: 9, 10, 11, 12, 13, 14, 15. Leo: 6, 20, 27, 28, 29. Virgo: 18, 19. Libra: 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6. Scorpio: 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6. Sagittarius: 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6. Capricorn: 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6. Aquarius: 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6. Pisces: 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6.

[On Degrees Increasing Fortune]
In this circle there are certain degrees which are said to increase fortune, which are described in this table. Aries: 8, 18, 27, 28. Taurus: 1, 2, 3, 15, 27. Gemini: 5, 13, 15. Cancer: 21. Leo: 7, 18, 20. Virgo: 13, 20. Libra: 19. Scorpio: 1, 2, 3, 4, 15. Sagittarius: 5, 7, 13, 14, 20. Capricorn: 12, 13, 14, 20. Aquarius: 7, 16, 17, 20. Pisces: 13, 20.

[On Compatible Degrees]
Two degrees which are of the same longitude from the beginning of the cardinal signs are called compatible, that is, of equal strength and consonant or participating in virtue. For example, the 20th degree of Capricorn or Cancer with the 10th degree of Sagittarius or Gemini; the 20th degree of Aries or Libra with the 10th degree of Pisces or Leo.

[On the Accidental Circle]
Having, with God's help, brought forth all that pertains to the essential circle of the signs, we now turn to the accidental. For the circle is figured at every hour in such a way that it is divided into four parts, which the circle of the hemisphere and the circle of the meridian (that is, the circle of the midheaven) divide, which makes the mid-day. And each of these parts is divided into three unequal parts according to the ascensions of the ascending signs. And in this way the circle is divided into twelve parts which are called houses, and are also named cusps and towers, the work of which is explained in the book of Ezibi, that is, in the book of the course of the stars. The beginning of the division is also the horoscope, that is, the ascendant, whose beginning is above the circle of the eastern hemisphere. Then the second house follows, and the third, and the rest of the houses up to the twelfth. The fourth part, which is from the ascendant to the midheaven, which is the twelfth, eleventh, and tenth house, is called the eastern masculine fourth part, and arriving, it signifies the beginning of life, and is called childish, sanguine, vernal. And the other part, which is from the midheaven to the degree of the western sign, that is, the seventh, which is above the circle of the western hemisphere, which is the ninth, eighth, and seventh house, and is meridian, feminine, receding, signifies middle age, and is called truly youthful, aestival, choleric. The third part, which is from the west to the degree of the fourth house, which is above the meridian circle under the earth, which is the sixth, fifth, and fourth house, is western, masculine, arriving, signifies the end of life, and is called autumnal, melancholic, and is senile and of middle age. The fourth part, which is from the fourth house to the ascendant, which is the third, second, and ascendant house, is northern, feminine, receding, signifies what happens to a person after his death and to what his body will come, or his disposition concerning the dismissed substance, or what will be said of him, namely whether he will be praised or blamed. This part is called senile, phlegmatic, defective, hibernal. And those two parts which are from the midheaven to the ascendant, and from the ascendant to the fourth house, this half is called the ascending half. And the remaining parts which are from the fourth house to the seventh, and thence to the midheaven, are called the descending half. And whatever is above the earth of the circle, that is, that upper part of the circle, is called the right. And what is under the earth, that is, that lower part, is called the left. And the ascendant, and the fourth, and the seventh, and the tenth are called Alamed, that is, what we call angles, so that it sounds more beautiful. And the second house, the eighth, the fifth, and the eleventh are called succedent to the angles. But the third, sixth, ninth, and twelfth are called cadent from the angles. Therefore, when a planet is in the angles or its succedents, it is said to be effective. And if it is in the cadent houses from the angles, it is said to be defective. And each of these houses signifies something concerning the existence of men.

[On the Houses and Their Significations]
The first house, whose beginning rises in the circle of the eastern hemisphere, is called Athale, that is, the ascendant. This signifies the body and life and the beginnings of actions in interrogations, and speech and rumor, and whatever the querent thinks in his mind. It signifies the beginnings of life. And Alendezgod said that in nativities, the lord of the first triplicity of the ascendant signifies the life and nature of the native or querent, and his delight and will, and what he loves, and what he hates, and what good or evil will befall him in the beginning of his life. And the second lord of the triplicity signifies life and body and virtue or strength and the middle of life. And the third lord of the triplicity signifies that which his companions have signified for him, and signifies the end of life in death. The second house is the house of substance and sustenance and ministers and helpers, and signifies the end of the years of life, that is, the end of youth. And Alendezgod said concerning the lords of the triplicity of this house, the first, second, and third, see which of them is stronger, and you will rightly make him the author and significator of acquisition, for if he is in the midheaven, he will find a king, and if he is in the house of faith or trust, it is better. Similarly, the first lord of the triplicity gives substance in the beginning of life, and the second in the middle of life, and the third at its end. The third house is of brothers and sisters and relatives and loved ones, of faith and religion, of commands and legates, of changes and minor journeys, and signifies the existence of life before death. Alendezgod said that the lord of the triplicity of the house of brothers, the first signifies older brothers, the second middle ones, the third younger ones, and their dignity and their existence according to their places. The fourth house is of fathers, inheritances, the end of things, treasures, and all hidden and secret things. It signifies the end of human life. Alendezgod said that the lord of the triplicity of the house of fathers, the first signifies fathers, the second cities and lands, the third the ends of things and prisons. The fifth house is of children and loves, of legates and gifts, and signifies what will be after death, namely praise and blame. Alendezgod said that the lord of the triplicity of the house of children, the first signifies children and life, the second love, the third legates. The sixth house is of infirmities and servants, and signifies the end of life and what will happen before old age. Alendezgod said that the lord of the triplicity of the house of infirmities, the first signifies infirmities and recovery from infirmities and from evils and deteriorations. The second signifies eyes and servants. The third signifies what will happen from them and their utility and works. And it is the significator of beasts and cattle, and all quadrupeds, of their strength and their multitude, and also their death in his hand or their departure from it, that is, from the hand, and also of prison and detention. The seventh house is of women, marriages, contentions, and partnerships and oppositions, and signifies the middle of the end of life towards old age. Alendezgod said that the lord of the triplicity of the seventh house, the first signifies women, the second contentions, the third mixtures and partnerships. The eighth house is of death. It signifies fear and death and Almauerith, that is, the substances or inheritances of the dead which the heirs ought to possess after their death, and it signifies the years of life if...

[Significations of Angular Lords]
through causes of medicine and astronomy, and through spiritual and similar works, and it signifies through its presence in the tenth house, through agreements and negotiations, and through wives, and through the king's causes. The presence of the lord of the fourth house signifies fortune from cultivation of the land and its fruit, through the causes of fathers and ancient things, and through its presence in the ascendant it signifies fortune from cultivation of the land and its fruit, through ingenuity and depth of counsel; and its presence in the tenth house signifies profit from cultivation of the land and its fruit, through the causes of the king and magistracies. And its presence in the seventh house signifies fortune from cultivation of the land and its fruit, through the causes of wives and fates, and through negotiations. These are signified by the lords of the angles through their presence in their angles. Similarly, therefore, you will do concerning the presence of the lords of the other houses; and therefore we have introduced only the lords of the angles so that it might be an example for the others.

[How to Know the Dominant Planet]
When you wish to know the planet that dominates a matter, look at which planet has the most authority in the house of the matter and the planet that signifies the nature of that matter, as we will say in the natures of the planets. Therefore, see which of the planets is stronger in the house of the matter and what part it has of the strengths we have mentioned, that is, from the number we mentioned when we discussed the strength and power of the planets, and whichever is strongest of all in the place of the matter, that will be its dominator. For example, if the question is about substance and you wish to know who its dominator is, and the second house, which signifies substance, is the fifth degree of the sign of Aries: because it is the house of Mars, Mars has five strengths in this place; the exaltation of the Sun is there, and it has four strengths in it. It is also the Sun's triplicity, and it has three strengths there. Therefore, the Sun has seven strengths there. And it is the term of Jupiter, and it has two strengths there. And it is also the face of Mars, and it has one strength there. Therefore, Mars has six strengths there: five from the house and one from the face; and the Sun has seven. And such a planet is called Almubta, that is, conquering. Therefore, the Sun takes precedence there, because it has seven strengths there, and it dominates there in the house of substance. Similarly, you will take into account the place of the part of substance and the part of fortune, and you will make Jupiter, who is naturally the significator of substance, a participant in them, and you will combine the testimonies of the parts and the planets; and you will do the same for all the houses to know their dominator.

[Accidental Powers of Planets]
Among the accidental powers of the planets is Albais, that is, similarity; and this is when a diurnal planet is above the earth by day and below the earth by night, and a nocturnal planet is above the earth by night and below the earth by day. And if this is a masculine planet in a masculine sign, and a feminine planet in a feminine sign, it is said to be in its similarity, that is, in its Albais. And its strength will be like the strength of a man in its perfect place of acquisition and fortune. The second difference in the natures of the seven planets, and what is proper to them, and what they signify concerning the essence of things. And since, with God's help, we have now completed what we proposed to discuss concerning the circle of the signs and its accidents, let us now pursue the intention of the seven planets and their natures, what they have in common, and what they signify.

[Nature and Significations of Saturn]
Saturn is masculine, malefic, diurnal, and is the significator of fathers if the child's nativity is at night; and it signifies ultimate old age if it is occidental; and the beginning of old age if it is oriental; and it signifies gravity, coldness, and dryness; and from the complexion of bodies, melancholic; and its increase and distillation. And perhaps it will sometimes be a cold, humid, ponderous, and fetid complexion; and much eating and true affection; and it signifies depth of counsel; and much silence; and from magistracies, ancient and precious things; and it signifies cultivation of fields and population of lands and rivers if it is fortunate; and vile and laborious things if it is malefic, such as friction in baths, fullers, and sailors. And if it is fortunate, it will be of true affection, spacious, and patient. And if it is malefic, it will be indiscreet, stable, sad, and sorrowful, of evil suspicion, very suspicious, and moving people to whisperings. And if it is fortunate, it signifies from substance ancient and durable things, and inheritances, and cultivation of land; if it is malefic, it signifies dirty waters and bad-tasting, old, and convertible things. And from infirmities, phlegmatic and melancholic and viscous and congealed acute diseases, such as leprosy, morphea, gout, and cancers and other such things; and it signifies long journeys, prisons, and bonds, also labor and slowness, and affliction, and almauerith, that is, the substances of the dead; also fathers and grandfathers and older brothers, eunuchs, servants, and vile men; and it signifies from works the works of skins if it is the sole significator without the complexion of any other planets. If Jupiter is conjoined with it, it signifies the work of parchment on which divine books are written. And if Mars is conjoined with it, it signifies shoe soles and their preparations. And if the Sun is conjoined with it, it signifies the work of shoemakers. And if Venus is conjoined with it, it signifies the work of skins from which drums and other instruments we use in games are made. And if Mercury is conjoined with it, it signifies the work of skins on which testaments and payrolls are written. And if the Moon is conjoined with it, it signifies the preparation of skins of wild animals and mountain animals and similar things; and it signifies from sects that which confesses unity if it is fortunate; if it is malefic, it signifies belief in unity with much hesitation, that is, doubt. And Messahala, whom God wished to exalt, who was an astrologer very clear in judgments, said: why is it said that it signifies the Jewish faith? Because it is among the most ancient, and all confess it, and it no other; thus Saturn, to whom all are joined, and he to none; it also signifies black garments. And some others said that Saturn signifies the inner parts of the ear and the spleen, and the stomach; and it has blackness from colors; and from tastes, astringent and sour. And from days, Saturday; and from nights, that which precedes Wednesday. And the quantity of its orb is nine degrees. And the years of its firdaria are eleven, the greatest 465, and the greater 57, and the middle 43 and a half, the lesser 30. Its strength in the regions of the circle is to the right of the north. And Messahala said that it signifies among human figures a man between black and yellow, who, when he walks, casts his eyes to the ground, ponderous in gait, joining his feet, and thin, stooped, having small eyes, and dry skin, veiny, having a sparse beard on his jaws, thick lips, cunning, ingenious, seducer, killer. And Dorotheus said that this signifies a very hairy man with joined eyebrows; and it has from regions Alcina and India and all the land of the blacks. And from parts, it has the part of strength and stability; and it signifies lands or things of lands and inheritances; and those who work in works and audacity and labor, ingenuity and causes of death; and it has from the parts of the world Achid and Alchint and their confines and the lands of the blacks and their mountains.

[Nature and Significations of Jupiter]
Jupiter is fortunate, masculine, diurnal; and it is the significator of substance and produces temperate heat and humidity, airy, sanguine; and from ages, it signifies youth up to the perfection of age; and from magistracies that pertain to law, such as judging just judgments, and bringing peace among men, and striving for good things; and it signifies abundance of substance; and from negotiations, those that are done without deception; and it signifies soul and life, joy and truth and religion and patience and every beautiful and precious precept and abundance of Venus; and from infirmities that arise from blood by an increase of quantity that is not superfluous beyond nature, nor from vitiated and convertible blood; and it is the planet of wisdom and intellect and use. To whom if Saturn is conjoined, it signifies necromancy and incantations and exorcisms. And if Mars is conjoined with it, it signifies the science of medicine. And if the Sun is conjoined with it, it signifies the science of sects and prudence in contentions and disputes. And if Venus is conjoined with it, it signifies the composition of sounds and other delightful sciences. And if Mercury is conjoined with it, it signifies the science of arithmetic and writing; also astronomy and philosophy and geometry. And if the Moon is conjoined with it, it signifies the science of disposition.

[Venus: Feminine, Nocturnal, Cold and Humid]
Venus, a feminine, nocturnal fortune, signifies women, wives, and mothers if the nativity is diurnal. She operates with temperate coldness and humidity. From age, she signifies youth or adolescence. From crafts, she signifies instruments of games, ornaments, beautiful figures, games of dice and chess, dances, idleness, fornication and fornicators, and children of fornication, and a multitude of coitus, and all kinds of luxury, and the composition and use of crowns, and beauty and cleanliness of clothing and ornaments. Gold and silver, affection, games, laughter and joy, and the use of ointments and various spices, drinks and intoxications. She believes in all those she gives generously to, and signifies affection, diligence, love, justice, and houses of prayer, which she holds faithfully. She signifies the mastery of all signs, such as music, etc. If Saturn aspects her, she signifies the sound of songs with which the dead are sometimes lamented, or which builders sing when they build edifices. And if Jupiter aspects her, she signifies the sound of readings or songs which the lords of sects use in their altars and places of prayer in praise of Almighty God. And if Mars signifies the sounds which secular people use, and vulgar songs in which there is mention of blasphemy or battles, or in which there is mention of prison or labor and similar things, such as a song in which there is mention of capture and binding and the striking of whips. If the Sun signifies the sound of wood with which one sings before kings and nobles. If Mercury, the sound that is exercised in the composition of verses. And if the Moon signifies the songs of sailors in ships. And from infirmities, she has cold and humid diseases which occur especially and often in the genital members. And from substance, that which is acquired for beauty, such as women's ornaments, and their clothes, pearls and paintings. And from the quality of the soul, sweetness and friendship, and eating and familiar things, and desires for drinking and eating and coitus. And from sects, the worship of idols, and those in whom eating and drinking are most practiced. And some have said that she signifies the hips and the spine, the back and sperm. And others have said that she signifies fat and fleshy parts in the vulva, uterus, belly, groin, and navel. And from colors, she has whiteness; and from tastes, oiliness. And the quantity of her orb is 7 degrees. And she has from days, the day of Venus; and from nights, the night of Mars. And the years of her firdaria are eight. And her greater years are 82, greatest 152, middle 45, but lesser 8. Her strength in the regions of the circle is to the right of the east. And Masha'allah said that she signifies, from the figures of men, a white man inclining to blackness, of beautiful body and hair, having a round face, and having a small jaw, beautiful eyes, and the blackness of her eyes is more than it should be. And Dorotheus said that she signifies a man with a beautiful face, beautiful eyes, and much hair, and more white, mixed with redness, fat, showing benevolence. And she has from parts, the part of desire, and signifies friendship and play and affection and patience and conjunctions of males. And she has from the parts of the world, Albiget and Aliemen and the lands of the Arabs.

[Mercury: Mixed, Masculine, Diurnal]
Mercury, mixed, masculine, diurnal, inclines by his nature to that which he aspects from the planets and from the signs. He signifies younger brothers, and signifies servants and the affection of concubines. He also signifies divinity and the oracles of prophets, and credulity, and work and honor or prayer. If he is in his own nature and no planet aspects him, he signifies earthly things and the augmentation of things by growth. And from age, youth, and perfection in it. And from works, works that generate knowledge, preaching, rhetoric, negotiations, estimation, and geometry, and the disposition of things, and philosophy, and auguries, and proverbs, and writing, and the science of versification, and especially the work of numbers. If Saturn aspects him, he signifies from the work of numbers, the work of measuring lands and inheritances, and the number of buildings and looms. If Jupiter, he signifies the number of prayers and the number of divine books. If Mars, he signifies the number that is in the gifts of armies and fighters, and the number of blows of whips and clubs. If the Sun, he signifies presiding over the number of kings and the substance of houses. If Venus, he signifies the number of strings of wood or citharas, the number of sounds and pipes. If the Moon, he signifies the number of dishes that are made for the meals of travelers outside the house. And he signifies from infirmities, spiritual infirmities of the soul, i.e., horrible thoughts, and restlessness of mind and doubts and other similar things. He also signifies the quality of the soul and similar things, his complexion and conjunction. When he is fortunate, there will be good things according to the kind of fortune that makes him fortunate, and according to the place in which Mercury is fortunate. And when he is unfortunate, there will be iniquities according to the evil that makes him unfortunate, and according to the place in which he became unfortunate. And he signifies from sects, the worship of unity and similar things, and this secretly with hypocrisy and simulation. And some have said that he signifies the thighs, navel, and groin, and legs, nerves, and veins. And from colors, he has every mixed and varied color, and the color of the wild lily flower. And from tastes, sourness. And the quantity of his orb is 7 degrees. And he has from days, the day of Mercury; and from nights, the night of Sunday. The years of his firdaria are 9. And his greater years are 76, greatest 460, middle 48, but lesser 20. His strength in the regions of the circle is in the north. And some have said that Mercury from the middle of his retrogradation until the second station signifies childhood; and from the second station until the conjunction of the Sun, youth; and from the conjunction of the Sun until the first station, middle age; and from his first station until the middle of retrogradation, he signifies old age and contrariety in his conjunction through direct motion until the first station, he signifies affection and friendship and imitations of love; and from his second station going to conjunction, he signifies the inquiry of affection and concord; and from his first station going again to retrogradation, he signifies the inquiry of contrariety and dissimulation, slowness and little shame, and occupation and stupor in things; and in the middle of retrogradation, he signifies temperate swiftness because of the weakness of ingenuity. And at the second station, he signifies stupor and occupation of ingenuity and slowness, and the egress from this, swiftness and the opening of ingeniousness.

[Mercury's Conjunctions and Figures]
His conjunction with the Sun through direct motion signifies the swiftness and passion of ingeniousness and their breadth or augmentation. Similarly, it happens to Venus in these places and to the higher planets. And Masha'allah said that Mercury signifies, from the figures of men, a man not very white nor black in color, having an elevated and long forehead, length in the face and a long nose, having a sparse beard on the jaws and beautiful eyes not entirely black, having long fingers. And from parts, he has the part of negotiation; he signifies fear, infestation, and war and enmities and seductions and contrarieties; he also signifies perfect mastery and subtlety in work and inquiry, and in other things that happen among men from deeds and contentions. And from lands, he has Adelech, Alquidem, and especially in the south, the lands of the Indians. The Moon, a feminine, nocturnal fortune, operates coldness and humidity. She is the significator of mothers if the nativity is nocturnal, and in her there is a false temperate quality, and she signifies childhood and the beginning of growth. And from works, she has embassies and messages, and works of waters and lands according to the quantity of fortune or misfortune or evil, so that if she is good, she signifies good, and vice versa. She also signifies principality if she presides or is the mistress of some things pertaining to the king, if she is fortunate with the Sun in a good aspect and in a good place. And from substance, she signifies silver and cultivated land if she has authority in the fourth house, and from faith, religion. And from infirmities, epilepsy, paralysis, gout, falling sickness, facial distortion, disarticulation of limbs, and commotion; and whatever is similar to coldness and humidity. And the quality of the soul, her conjunction with the planets. If she aspects

[Planetary States in Themselves and Mutually]
The third difference is in what happens to the seven planets in themselves and what happens to them mutually. Since, by the grace of God, we have already discussed the state of the planets in themselves and what they signify, let us proceed to narrate what happens to them in themselves and mutually, that is, from some to some. The signification of the planets in themselves is that if a planet is ascending in the circle of its apogee, it is lesser in light, magnitude, and speed, that is, when there are less than 90 degrees between it and its apogee, either before or after. If there are exactly 90 degrees between it and its apogee, it will be equal in light, magnitude, and speed. But if it is outside these two places, i.e., more than 90 degrees, it will be descending from the circle of the apogee and will appear greater in light and magnitude and swifter in speed. If its portion is equal to less than 180 degrees, it will be increasing in number. And if it is more, it will be decreasing in number. And if its portion is equal to 180 degrees or 360 degrees, it will neither increase nor decrease. And if the equation added to the mean course is called increasing the course or number, and if its equation is decreased, it is called decreasing the number. And when any of the three superior planets goes more than its mean course, it is said to increase the course; and if it goes less, it is said to decrease the course; and if it goes just as much, it is said to be equal in course. When any of the inferior planets goes more than the mean course of the Sun, it will be increasing the course. When it goes less, it is said to be decreasing the course; and when it goes just as much, it will be equal in course. The state of the luminaries in their course is like the state of the three superior planets. A planet is also northern when it crosses its genzabar, that is, when it crosses the path of the Sun going from south to north. That transit, that is, that intersection of circles, is called genzabar. Therefore, when a planet has crossed that intersection and there are less than 90 degrees between the planet and that intersection, the planet will be ascending northern. When it is from 90 to 180 degrees, it will be descending northern. When it has passed this number, that is, when it has more, going to 270 degrees, it will be descending southern. And when it has passed this number, going to 360 degrees, it will be ascending southern. This is the state of the planets in themselves. Let us now discuss the state of the planets mutually, that is, what happens to the five planets with respect to the luminaries. And we will say from this what Ptolemy said about almuten, that is, about seeing each other face to face. This is when it is between a planet and the Sun, while the planet is occidental, that is, while it follows the Sun, as much as is between the house of that planet and the house of the Sun in signs. Or when it is between that planet and the Moon, when it is oriental from the Moon, that is, while it succeeds the Moon, as much as is between the house of the planet and the house of the Moon in signs. That is, when the planet is as distant from the Sun as its house is distant from the Sun's house. Similarly, it is said of the Moon: when a planet succeeds the Sun and Saturn is 6 signs from the Sun, Jupiter 5, Mars 4, Venus 3, Mercury 2, then it is said to be in the almuten of the Sun. Similarly, when this number of signs for each planet is between any planet and the succeeding Moon, it is said to be in the almuten of the Moon. The security of a planet, that is, that a planet is in its hayz, that is, in its proper part and in one of the angles of the ascendant and one of the luminaries; similarly in a place similar to it in the quadrant, namely in an angle, so that the planet is oriental from the Sun by day, occidental from the Moon by night. And every planet is said to be in its security by some when there are 60 degrees between the oriental planet and the Sun. And every planet, from when it is covered by the Sun's rays until it appears from under the rays, is called combust. And when it begins to enter the rays, it is said to have begun to be combust. And when it is hidden under the rays and is near the Sun by 12 degrees, it is called oppressed. And when it is with the Sun in one degree, and there are 16 minutes or less between them, and its latitude is similar, it is called united. And when it has passed that union, seeking exit until it is seen, it is called escaped. And from when the three superior planets appear from under the rays and begin to rise, that is, appear in the morning before the Sun, this is when they are closer to the circle of the eastern hemisphere until they come to opposition, they are called oriental dextrous. And from when they have passed opposition until they conjunct the Sun again, they are called occidental sinister. Venus and Mercury, from when either of them separates from the degrees of the Sun in the middle of its retrogradation and appears until they are combust by the Sun in their direct motion, are called oriental. And from when they separate from the Sun in the middle of their direct motion until they are combust again in their retrogradation, they are called occidental. And when they are in their rising, that is, when they are oriental, they are called dextrous and direct masculine. And in their setting, that is, when they are occidental, they are called sinister and direct feminine. And then they are stronger. The three superior planets, after they emerge from under the Sun's rays, are called oriental and are said to increase in strength up to 30 degrees from the Sun. And after that, up to another 30 degrees, they are called strong or stronger oriental. And when they have passed the Sun by 60 degrees, they are called oriental planets going to debility until they come to retrogradation. Then they are called oriental retrograde until they are in opposition. And after this, they will be occidental retrograde when they have passed opposition until they come to direct motion. Then from direct motion up to 60 degrees after direct motion, until their longitude from the Sun is 30 degrees, they are called strong occidental. Then from a longitude of 60 degrees after direct motion, they are called occidental going to debility. Then they become weak occidental until they enter under the Sun's rays. The inferior planets, from when they separate from the Sun, and they are retrograde, are called weak oriental. They do not cease to be so until they come to their direct motion. And then they become strong oriental until their longitude from the Sun is like the Sun's longitude from them when they began to weaken going to retrogradation. Then they become weak oriental until they are under the Sun's rays. After this, they are conjunct. Then combust, going to appearance until they are seen. And from when they separate from the Sun in direct motion up to 60 degrees, they are stronger. And from 60 degrees up to the time of their retrogradation, they will be strong occidental. And as long as they are with the Sun, they will be weak. When a planet has emerged from under the Sun's rays and is not joined to any other planet, it is said to be in its own light. This is the state of the planets with the luminaries.

[Planetary Aspects and Conjunctions]
Regarding what happens to planets in relation to each other. Their relation to each other is conjunction, that is, when two planets are in two aspecting signs, and the lighter planet is in its sign with fewer degrees than the heavier planet in its sign, and there are 6 degrees or less between them, then it is said that the lighter planet goes to the conjunction of the heavier one. And when their degrees are equal, their conjunction is perfected. When it passes it, it will be separated from it. This conjunction is called a conjunction of longitude. A conjunction of latitude is when two planets are joined by latitude. And if there is an application of conjunction, their latitude must be equal in one part. And if there is a conjunction by opposition, their latitudes must be equal, so that the latitude of one is ascending in the north and the other descending in the north, or one ascending in the south and the other descending in the south. Or if there is an application from any other aspect, this means that the latitude of one is northern ascending and the other southern descending, and vice versa in the south. And this is the application of latitude that has been mentioned. And when one planet separates from another and is not joined to any other planet as long as it is in the same sign, it is called void of course. And when a planet is in a sign and no other planet aspects this sign, as long as it is in the same sign, it is called feral or wild. And when a lighter planet separates from a heavier planet and is joined to another, it transfers the nature of the first to the second. A planet also transfers nature in another way, that is, when a lighter planet joins a heavier planet, and that heavier planet in turn joins another heavier planet, then it better transfers the nature of the lighter to the heavier. If, however, one of these is not joined to the other, but each is joined to another, then if that third planet aspects any place in the circle, it returns their light to that place. This is called the return of light. Again, if one planet is not joined to another, but a third planet transfers light to both, then this conjunction is also called the return of light. Prohibition follows and occurs in two ways. One, namely, by conjunction, when there are three planets in one sign, but in different degrees, and the heavier one has more degrees, then the one in the middle prohibits the former, that is, the one with fewer degrees, from joining the heavier one until it passes it. In the second way, two planets are in one sign, and the lighter one joins the heavier one; another also joins the same heavier one by aspect. Therefore, the one who is with it in one sign prohibits the aspecting one from conjunction with the heavier one, if, however, the degrees of the one who joins and the one who aspects are equal, that is, of the same number. But if the one who aspects is closer to the degree of the heavier one, the conjunction will be of the aspecting one. And if a planet joins the lord of the sign in which it is, or the lord of exaltation, or the lord of other dignities in which it is, it is said to pulsate, that is, to send the nature of that planet, the lord, that is, of the same dignity, to it. And if a planet is in any of its dignities and is joined to another planet that also has a part of dignity in the same place, it also sends both its nature, namely, and that of the one to which it is joined. This entire sending is called alchobol, that is, reception.

[Return of Light and Refrenation]
Now follows the return, that is, when a planet joins another planet that is combust, that is, under the sun's rays, or is retrograde, it returns its virtue due to its weakness, which it cannot retain. Then, if both planets are in an angle or succeeding angles, the return will be with profit. Similarly, if the one joining it is only in an angle, and the one to whom it joins has received it. But if the planet joining is cadent from an angle, and the one to whom it joins is in an angle or in a succeeding angle, or if both are cadent, the return will be with detriment. Now follows almenē, that is, refrenation, which occurs when a planet wants to join another, but before it joins, retrogradation occurs, and thus its conjunction is destroyed.

[Alichorad and Alfazim]
Now follows alichorad, that is, accidental contrariety. This occurs when a lighter planet has many degrees in a sign, and another, heavier one, has fewer degrees, and a third, lighter than the first, wanting to join the heavier one, but before it joins it, that lighter one which has more degrees becomes retrograde and joins and applies to that heavier one. And passing it, it also joins another lighter planet, and thus the conjunction of the former with the heavier one is destroyed. Now follows alfazim, that is, frustration. This occurs when a planet seeks the conjunction of another planet, but before it reaches it, this one changes into another sign, and there will be some planet in few degrees aspecting that sign, and its rays will be at the beginning of the sign. When the succeeding planet leaves the first sign, it joins this aspecting one, and the conjunction it had with that one, that is, with the first, is annulled.

[Abscission of Light]
Now follows the abscission of light. This is when a planet seeks the conjunction of another, and is in the second sign from the sign of the one to which another planet joins, but before it joins it, the one in the second sign becomes retrograde. It joins it and cuts off its light from the planet that wanted to join it. Similarly, if a planet is going to the conjunction of another planet, and that other planet to which it wants to join seeks the conjunction of another planet heavier than itself, but before the lighter one reaches the degrees of the heavier one, the heavier one joins another heavier than itself, and cuts off its light from the first lighter planet.

[Fortunate and Unfortunate Places]
Regarding fortunate and unfortunate places. There are also places for these planets in which they are strengthened and in which they are weakened: places in which fortunes occur, and places in which misfortunes occur. But the places in which fortunes occur are these: that they are in good aspects, that is, in some useful aspect, that is, a sextile, or in a trine aspect, which by some is called hexagonal radiation and trigonal; and that the malefics are cadent from them, and are separated from misfortune, and joined to fortune; or are besieged by fortunes or their rays, that is, that they are between two fortunes or between the rays of fortunes. For this is obsession, that a planet has fortune or its rays.

[Planetary Fortification and Debilitation]
before it, or another benefic or its rays behind it. And some call this elevation, that is, veneration: or they are united with the Sun in one degree: or they are in its sextile aspect: or trine or similar aspect of the Moon, and the Moon is then fortunate: and they are swift in course, augmented in light and number: or they are in their dignities, as in their own terms, that is, in their own likeness, so that a masculine planet is in a masculine sign: and a feminine planet in a feminine sign, and a diurnal planet in the day above the earth and in the night below the earth, a nocturnal planet in the night above the earth and in the day below the earth, and the rest, and that they are in signs in which they have dignities or their powers: or in their joys, or in bright degrees received: and from their strength it is that they are ascending in the north: or they are northern: or they are ascending in the circle of their apogee: or in the second station, that is, those which are in the station where they are directed from retrogradation: or they are emerging from under the Sun's rays: or they are in an angle: or in its succedent: or they are three degrees higher and oriental from the Sun: if the Sun aspects them with a sextile: or trine aspect, this will be an increase of strength for them: or they are in masculine quarters and the Sun, when it is in those masculine quarters: or in masculine signs, it will also be strong unless it is in Libra: because there it falls. And from the strength of the three inferior planets it is that they are occidental from the Sun: or in feminine quarters, and from the strength of the Moon: that it is in the night above the earth and in the day below the earth in a feminine place; or in a feminine sign: and when it is in the exaltation of the Sun. Concerning the misfortune of the planets. Indeed, concerning the misfortune of the planets and their destruction, it is that they are in conjunction with malefics: or in opposition to them: or in their square: or trine: or sextile radiation: or if there is between them a malefic body or its rays less than the term of the planet: or they are in the terms of malefics: or their houses: or malefics are elevated above them from the 10th or 11th places, and much worse if they do not receive them. Or they are in conjunction with the Sun: or its opposition: or in square radiation: or it is in the heads of their genitures: or with their tails: or with the head of the Dragon or the tail, or there are between them and any of these, namely, places, 22 degrees or less: and especially if the Moon is in any of them: similarly, the Sun is then more hindered by them, that is, by the head or tail when they are between it and one of them, even 4 degrees before or behind: or the planets are besieged between two malefics: this is that the planet is in some sign and with it a malefic: or its rays before it, and a malefic or its rays behind it: or it is separated from a malefic by conjunction: or by aspect: and is joined in such a way to another malefic: or a malefic: or its rays are in the sign which is before it: that is, in the second from it: and in the sign which is after it: that is, in the 12th from it, there is another malefic: or its rays. Similarly, it is said of signs that they are besieged. But if a benefic or the Sun aspects the same besieged planet: or besieged sign from a trine: or from a sextile aspect, and there is between it and the conjunction less than seven degrees, that malice or siege is dissolved. And from this, that the planet is retrograde.

[Planetary Debilities and Affections]
or combust under the Sun's rays, or falling from the ascendant, or from their debility, so that they are slow in course, or in their first station, that is, when they stand still to become retrograde, or are in dark degrees, or are masculine in feminine signs and feminine degrees by day under the earth, and by night above the earth; or are feminine in masculine signs and masculine degrees by night under the earth, and by day above the earth; or are in opposition to their dignities or powers; or descending in the south or meridian; or falling from the angles, or from the succedent houses of the angles; or in cadent houses; or are in the via combusta, which is the last half of Libra and the first half of Scorpio; or are joined to a retrograde, impeded, or cadent planet; or are not received. Or if the three superior planets are occidental, or in feminine quarters. And the debility of the Sun is to be in feminine signs, or in feminine quarters, unless it is in the ninth house. And the debility of the three inferior planets is to be oriental, or in masculine quarters. Concerning the friendship and hatred of the planets. It is said among the planets that some of them love and hate each other. For concerning those who love, some of the ancients said that Jupiter loves all planets and is their friend, and they are his, except Mars. The friends of Venus are all planets, and all love her except Saturn. The friends of Saturn are Jupiter, Sun, and Moon, and his enemies are Mars and Venus, and she hates him more. And the friend of Mars is Venus, and the other planets hate him, and Jupiter and Sun more. The friends of the Sun are Jupiter and Venus, and his enemies are Mars, Mercury, and Moon. The friends of Mercury are Jupiter, Venus, and Saturn only, and his enemies are Sun, Moon, and Mars. The friends of the Moon are Jupiter, Venus, and Saturn, and her enemies are Mars and Mercury. The friends of the Dragon's Head are Jupiter and Venus, and his enemies are Saturn and Mars. The friends of the Tail are Saturn and Mars, and his enemies are Sun, Moon, Jupiter, and Venus. And there are other kinds of enmity: when two planets have their houses opposite, like Mars and Venus, and when they conjoin, it is called the opening of the gates. The third kind of enmity is when the exaltations of two planets are opposite. The stronger friendship of planets is when a planet agrees with another planet in nature, quality, substance, and power, just as Mars agrees with the Sun, because both agree in heat, dryness, sharpness, and swiftness; he is the lord of his exaltation in which his strength appears. And just as the Moon agrees with Venus in coldness and humidity, and she is the lady of her exaltation. But when two planets agree in nature and substance, like Jupiter and Venus, they are friends.

[Astrological Terms and Conjunctions]
Fourth difference in the exposition of astrological names. Let us now proceed with the exposition of astrological names. The beginning of these is the conjunctions signifying destructions or changes that occur in this world from conjunctions, the number of which is six. The greatest of all conjunctions is the conjunction of Saturn and Jupiter at the beginning of Aries, and this occurs every 960 years. The second conjunction of these is at the beginning of each triplicity, and this occurs every 240 years. For they conjoin twelve times in each triplicity, and perhaps they make 13 conjunctions in each triplicity; then their conjunction changes to the triplicity that succeeds this one. The third conjunction is of Saturn and Mars at the beginning of Cancer, which occurs every 30 years. The fourth is the conjunction of Jupiter and Saturn in each sign, which occurs every 20 years. The fifth is the descent of the greater luminary at the point of the vernal equinox, that is, the Sun's ingress into the head of Aries, which occurs every year. The sixth is the conjunction of the luminaries and their opposition, which occurs in the middle of each lunar month. And when the ascendant of the conjunction is mentioned, it means or signifies the ascendant of the world, that is, the sign that ascends at the hour of the Sun's entrance into the aforesaid point of the vernal equinox, at the beginning, that is, of that year in which the aforesaid conjunction is to occur. Concerning the investigation of the annimodar, that is, the degree of the ascendant of nativities. From this annimodar, which is the investigation of the degree of the ascendant of a nativity, many astrologers think that the same degree of the ascendant of someone's nativity is found by it, but this is false, and I have already revealed this in my book which I made on the annimodar. But it finds by it the most worthy of all degrees of the circle after the degree of the ascendant at the same hour according to the natural course, and it often agrees, that is, it sometimes happens that the degree of the ascendant is found by it. The knowledge of this is to consider the degree of the conjunction or the degree of the prevention that occurred before the nativity itself. And if the conjunction was prior to that nativity, the nativity itself is called conjunctional; if the prevention was prior to it, it is called preventional. That is, in whichever of them the nativity occurred, in conjunction, that is, or prevention, in the same way and name the aforesaid nativity is called. And because the degree of the conjunction is the same degree in which the luminaries conjoin, there is no inquiry, nor does it need exposition. But in prevention, because each of the luminaries is in its own degree, that is, in different degrees, it is necessary for us to know which of these degrees is to be understood as the degree of prevention. And Ptolemy has already said that the degree of that luminary which is above the earth is the degree of prevention. And some wise men have said that if it happens in prevention that one luminary is in the degree of the orient and the other in the degree of the occident, then the degree of the orient will be the degree of prevention. And Vettius said that the degree of prevention is the degree in which the fulfillment occurs, wishing to understand the degree of the Moon. But because this is the work of Ptolemy, we must return to his opinion in this. Therefore, when the degree of the conjunction or the degree of the prevention is most certainly known, you will establish the degree of the ascendant by an estimation of the hour of the nativity and the four angles and the remaining houses. Then you will look at the degree of the conjunction or the degree of prevention that occurred before the nativity, and which of the planets was more dignified or stronger in it at the same hour of the conjunction or prevention by the multitude of dignities or powers, that is, you will consider which of the planets has greater dominion in the same place. Then you will equate that planet to the estimated hour of the nativity. Then you will see whether the degree of that planet in the sign in which it is is closer to the tenth house or to the ascendant, and to whichever of these it is closer, you will make this angle according to the degree of the planet itself, and you will divide the twelve houses by it. Ptolemy said that if several planets agree in the dominion of the same place and are equal in strength, you will establish as lord of the place that one who is the lord of the hayz. If they also agree in this, you will establish the one who is more likely to change from his state to what is better, that is, the one who wishes to leave a sign in which he is and enter another in which he has more dignities; or if they are oriental from the Sun, you will choose the one who is closest to the Sun and is not under the rays. But if it is in an angle, the one who is closest to the degree of that angle is to be chosen, and understand this. And from this, the hyleg, that is, the place of life in nativities, the knowledge of which is: first, you look at the hour of the nativity. If it is by day, you take it from the Sun. If it is before the degree of the ascendant by 5 degrees or less, or if it is in the tenth or eleventh house, whether the sign itself is masculine or feminine, it will be apt to be the hyleg. But if it is in these three places, but in the seventh or eighth or ninth house in a masculine sign, it will not be apt to be the hyleg. But if it is in these three places in a feminine sign, it will not be apt to be the hyleg. Then looking at the Moon, if it is in the ascendant or in the second or third house, or in the seventh or eighth, it will be apt to be the hyleg, whether the sign is masculine or feminine. And if it is before the degree of the ascendant by 5 degrees or less, or if it is in the tenth or eleventh, or in the fourth or fifth, or in the seventh in a feminine sign, it is apt to be the hyleg. But if it is in any of these in a masculine sign, it will not be apt to be the hyleg if it is in the day of the nativity. But if the nativity is nocturnal, we begin with the Moon, which, if it is in any of the aforesaid places, according to what we have said, will be apt to be the hyleg. But if the Moon is not in them, after this, look at the Sun. If it is before the 7th degree by 5 degrees or less, or if it is in the 4th or 5th house, it will be apt to be the hyleg, whether the sign is masculine or feminine. If it is before the ascendant by 5 degrees or less, or

[Determining the Hyleg]
in the ascendant, or in the second sign, it will also be apt for the hyleg. But if it is in any of these places in a feminine sign, it will not be apt for the hyleg. If none of the luminaries are apt for the hyleg, then look at the nativity: whether it is conjunct or preventional, that is, whether it is after the conjunction or prevention. If the nativity is conjunct and the degree of conjunction is in any of the angles, or in a succedent house, it will be in a place apt for the hyleg. But if the aforesaid degree is cadent from these eight places, that is, from the angles and from the succedent houses, it will not be the hyleg. Then you will look at the degree of the Part of Fortune: if it is in any of the angles or in the succedent houses, it will be in a place apt for the hyleg. But if it is cadent from these eight places, you will then look at the degree of the ascendant and constitute it as the hyleg. If the nativity is preventional, you will begin from the degree of prevention. You will look at it as you did before with the degree of conjunction, and after that, the degree of the Part of Fortune, and after that, the degree of the ascendant, in the order we mentioned for the degree of conjunction. You will not care about the sex of the signs, that is, you will not look at whether those signs are masculine or feminine, except only in the luminaries. That is, in the degree of conjunction or prevention, and the ascendant, and the Part of Fortune, you do not consider whether they are in masculine or feminine signs, both in the angles and in the succedent houses. But these four will only be apt for the hyleg when they are in these eight places, that is, in the angles or their succedent houses. If they are in receding places, that is, cadent from the angles, they will not be apt for the hyleg. It appears that the Sun is apt for the hyleg by day and night, above the earth and below the earth, in 11 places: above the earth in 6 places, and below the earth in 5. The Moon will also be apt for the hyleg by day and night, above the earth and below the earth, similarly in 11 places: above the earth in 5, and below the earth in 6. And if the Moon is in these places under the Sun's rays, it will not be apt for the hyleg. You will look for the hyleg in the angles and their succedent houses according to how the 12 houses of the circle are equalized by the degrees of the ascendant's hours, according to how its work is explained in the canon of planets, that is, in the book of the courses of the planets. And when you have equalized the houses in this way, every planet that is before the degree of the ascendant sign or of any house by 5 degrees or less, its strength will be valid in the house that succeeds it. And every place among the places we mentioned is apt for the hyleg if any of its lords looks at it, who is the lord of the house, or the lord of exaltation, or the lord of the term, or of the triplicity, or the lord of the face. If not, it will not be apt for the hyleg. Concerning the Alcochoden. The text of the Alcochoden, who is the significator of life, that is, the lord of years or the giver of years, whom you wish to know, and you already know the hyleg in the order I predicted: you will look at the lord of the hyleg's house, or the lord of its exaltation, or the lord of its term, or the lord of its triplicity, or its face, whichever of these is stronger and more authoritative in the hyleg's place. And if it aspects the hyleg, it will be more worthy of being the Alcochoden. If it does not aspect the hyleg, and it has more authority, you will look at the one with less authority until you find one of them that aspects. If it does not aspect the hyleg, that place cannot be the hyleg. And then you will seek from another hyleg, and again you will seek from the same second hyleg the Alcochoden in the order we predicted. If two or three planets are equal in authority in the degree of the hyleg, and each aspects, the one who is stronger in place will be more worthy of being the Alcochoden. But if they are equal in strength of place, that is, where the planets themselves are, that one will be the Alcochoden who is closer to the degree of the hyleg. Some, however, thought it better to look at the lord of the house, whom if they saw aspecting the hyleg, they would make him the Alcochoden and not consider another. And if they did not find the lord of the house aspecting the hyleg, they would take the lord of exaltation, whom if they saw aspecting the hyleg, they would make him the Alcochoden and not consider another. They did similarly with the lord of the triplicity, term, and face in order. And Dorotheus preferred the lord of the term in this lord of the house. And some said that if two or three or more planets are equal in dignity and in proximity of aspect to the degree of the hyleg, that one will be the Alcochoden who is in a laudable place from the Sun, that is, who is with the Sun in one degree by 16 minutes or less, or closer to the degree of the angle, or at the beginning of its rising, that is, when it appears in the morning, or is in its second station, or is in some laudable place from the Sun as we said, he will be the Alcochoden. But if the degree of the Sun is the hyleg, and it is in Aries or Leo, the Sun will be the hyleg and Alcochoden simultaneously, and no other Alcochoden will be considered besides it. Similarly, if the degree of the Moon is the hyleg, and it is in Taurus or Cancer, you will take it as the hyleg and Alcochoden simultaneously, and you will not consider another Alcochoden besides it. The Almuten is the one who presides over the nativity; from him is signified the being of the native after the hyleg and Alcochoden. And this planet has more authority than the others: in the ascendant, and in the places of the luminaries, and in the place of the Part of Fortune, and also in the place of the conjunction or prevention that is before the nativity. If any planet presides over two, three, four, or more places due to the multitude of its power, it will be the Almuten, that is, the author and significator of life after the hyleg and Alcochoden, and through him is signified the being of the native. And some consider him the Alcochoden for giving life. Concerning the Profection of Signs. From this, the sign of profection in the years of nativities and of the world. For in the years of nativities, the knowledge is this: that you look at how many years have passed for the native from the perfect solar years. And you will look at one sign each year, and you will begin from the native's ascendant through the succession of signs until the number is finished. The sign that succeeds is the sign of profection from the ascendant, namely the sign of the entering year, which you have not included in this number. This will be in such a degree as it was in the ascendant of the nativity. And its lord is called the Alcochoden, whose interpretation is the lord of the year. Similarly, you will count from the sign of the Sun one sign for each year, and from this will come the sign of profection from the Sun. Similarly from the sign of the Moon and from the Midheaven, and from the Part of Fortune, in the likeness of the degree of the radix, that is, the point of nativity. An example of this is someone born with Capricorn rising, in its 3rd degree. The Sun was in Pisces, in its 15th degree. And the Midheaven was Scorpio, 8 degrees. And the Moon in Libra, 15 degrees. And the Part of Fortune in Leo, 17 degrees. Now three perfect years have passed for the native, and the fourth year arrives from the ascendant in Aries, which is the fourth from Capricorn, up to the 17th degree of the same Aries. And Mars will be the Alcochoden. And the place of the Sun arrives at Gemini up to the 15th degree of the same sign. And the Moon arrives at Capricorn, at 15 degrees. And the profection from the Midheaven arrives at the 8th degree of Aquarius. And the profection from the Part of Fortune arrives up to the 17th degree of Scorpio. And when the year arrives at the degree of profection, as to the 17th degree of Aries in this example, and between it and a similar degree of the succeeding sign to which the next year should arrive in the same house, there is a planet or its rays, and you want to know when the profection will arrive at that planet or its rays, you will look at the distance between the degree to which the year will arrive and the planets or rays in degrees and minutes. You will multiply that by 12, and a sixth of that number which you multiply, or in 12 degrees and 6 minutes of one degree. And whatever results will be the days from that year in which...

[Profection of the World's Years]
in which the profection will come from the degree in which the force begins to the degree to which you have numbered, then the profection of that planet will occur. The profection, however, from the years of the world, Alchindus said, is what was between the year of the conjunction that signified the sect of the Saracens and the year of Al-Biruni in which Muhammad first began to preach, which was the first year of the Arabs, 52 solar years and 57 days. And the ascendant of that year of the aforementioned conjunction of the sect was the sign of Gemini, and the profection of the same year came to Virgo. And between the first year of the Arabs and the first year of Yazdegerd, the king of the Persians, there were 3624 days, that is, complete. Therefore, when you wish to have knowledge of this matter, take the years of Yazdegerd and convert them into days, as has already been explained in the Azig, that is, in the book of planetary courses. And add to them the days that are between the first year of the Arabs and Yazdegerd, and divide this by 365 days and a quarter of a day. And as many divisions as come out, so many will be the solar years, and what remains of months and days will be from the imperfect year. When this has been collected from the years, these are the solar years from the beginning of the years of the Arabs. Therefore, project all years, one sign at a time, and begin from Virgo, and to whatever sign the number leads you, that will be the sign to which the year of the world comes from the ascendant of the conjunction of the aforementioned sect. Others, however, besides Alchindus, thought that they should add to the complete years of Yazdegerd 61 years, 2 months, 12 days, and 16 hours, from the years of the infidels, which are without fraction, that is, without a quarter of a day, and extend these years into days and convert the days into solar years as we have said, and begin to project from the beginning of Libra. If you want the profection from the sign of the conjunction of the sect, let the profection be from Scorpio. But if you want the profection from the ascendant of the kingdom, subtract from the years of Yazdegerd those 217 complete years and convert them into solar years as we have said, and begin to project from Virgo. Again, if you want the profection from the ascendant of the profection of the change of conjunction from the watery triplicity to the fiery triplicity, subtract from the complete years of Yazdegerd 176 years and convert those that remain into solar years, and begin to project from Leo, and wherever the number arrives in that sign, there will be the profection of each beginning of those things we have said. Concerning the direction of the significator. From this follows atazir, that is, direction: this is that you direct some significator to some unknown place and know what is between them from the degrees of direction, taking for each degree one year. Therefore, when you wish to know this, and that significator is in the ascendant, which you wish to direct to some part of the circle, subtract the ascensions of the degree in which the significator you wish to direct was, by the ascensions of the region from the ascensions of that degree to which you wish to direct it. And what remains will be the degree of direction. If the significator is in the seventh degree, you will subtract the ascensions of the nadir, that is, the opposite of the degree in which the significator is, from the ascensions of the nadir of that degree to which you wish to direct it in that region. But if the significator is in the midheaven or in the angle of the earth, you will subtract the ascensions of the degree of the significator from the ascensions of that degree to which you wish to direct it by the circle of direction, and what remains will be the degree of direction. But if that significator which you wish to direct is in some place outside the four angles, you will look at its longitude from one of these angles, which are the angle of the midheaven and the angle of the earth. This is that you look at the significator, which if it is between the ascendant and the midheaven, you subtract the ascensions of the degree of the midheaven by the direct circle from the ascensions of the degree of the significator. And if it is between the seventh and the midheaven, you subtract the ascensions of the degree of the significator from the ascensions of the degree of the midheaven by the direct circle. And what remains, from whichever of these places it is, you will divide by the parts of the hours of that day of the degree in which the significator is, and what comes out will be the hours of longitude from the angle. And if it is between the ascendant and the angle of the earth, you will subtract the ascensions of the degree of the significator by the direct circle from the ascensions of the degree of the angle of the earth. Again, if the significator is between the angle of the earth and the seventh, you will subtract the ascensions of the degree of the angle of the earth by the direct circle from the ascensions of the degree of the significator. And what remains from whichever of these places, you will divide by the times of the hours of the day of the nadir, that is, the opposite of the degree of the significator. And what comes out will be the hours of longitude from the angle. When you know the hours of longitude from the angle and you wish to direct the significator to some place of the circle of signs, and the significator is in the middle of the eastern circle, which is from the midheaven to the angle of the earth of those that succeed the ascendant, subtract the ascensions of that degree in which the significator was from the ascensions of that degree to which you wish to direct it by the direct circle, and what remains will be the significator of the direct circle; keep it. After this, you will subtract the ascensions of that degree in which the significator was by the ascensions of the region from the ascensions of that degree to which you wish to direct it, and what remains will be the significator of the region. After this, look at the remainder that is between the significator of the direct circle and the significator of the region; take its sixth part and multiply it by the hours of longitude from the angle; what results will be the equation. And if the significator of the direct circle is less than the significator of the region, you will add the equation to the significator of the direct circle. And if the significator of the direct circle is more, you will subtract the equation from it, and what remains will be the degree of direction. Likewise, if the significator which you wish to direct is in the middle of the western circle, which is from the angle of the earth to the midheaven of what succeeds the seventh, you will subtract the ascensions of the nadir of the degree of the significator which you wish to direct from the ascensions of the nadir of that degree to which you wish to direct it by the direct circle, and what remains will be the significator of the direct circle. After this, you will subtract the ascensions of the nadir of the degree of the significator by the ascensions of the region from the ascensions of the nadir of that degree to which you wish to direct it, and what remains will be the significator of the region. Then you will take the remainder that is between the significator of the direct circle and the significator of the region; take its sixth part and multiply it by the hours of longitude from the angle, and what results will be the equation. After this, you will look at the significator of the direct circle; if it is less than the significator of the region, you will add the equation to the significator of the direct circle. If the significator of the direct circle is more than the significator of the region, you will subtract the equation from the significator of the direct circle, and what comes out of it will be the degree of direction. If the significator is in another quadrant, and the place to which you direct it is in another quadrant, you will direct the significator to the angle that succeeds it, then you will direct from the angle to the place to which you wish to direct it.

[Decan and Novenary Lords]
which succeeds until you come to some novenary from which the degree is: and the planet will be the lord of that novenary: for example: if the sign from which that degree was, was from the triplicity of Aries: then the first novenary of that sign will be Mars, lord of Aries: the second novenary of the genus will be Venus, lady of Taurus: and the third novenary will be Mercury, lord of Gemini. Similarly up to the ninth novenary. If the sign was from the triplicity of Cancer, the first novenary will be the Moon: the second novenary will be the Sun, lord of Leo: and the third will be Mercury, lord of Virgo. And if the sign was from the triplicity of Libra, the first novenary will be Venus, lady of Libra: the second will be Mars, lord of Scorpio: and the third will be Jupiter, lord of Sagittarius. Similarly in the triplicity of Capricorn, its first novenary is Saturn, lord of Capricorn: and the second similarly Saturn, lord of Aquarius: and the third Jupiter, lord of Pisces. Then what follows according to the order of succession of the signs: for example: if a planet or some house from the houses, that is, was in the 19th degree of Aquarius, if the sign is divided into nine divisions, the 19th degree will be in the sixth division, and since the sign of Aquarius is in the triplicity of Libra, its first novenary is Venus, lady of Libra: the second Mars, lord of Scorpio: and the third Jupiter, lord of Sagittarius: the fourth Saturn, lord of Capricorn: and the fifth also Saturn, lord of Aquarius: and the sixth Jupiter, lord of Pisces: and thus the novenary of the 19th degree of Aquarius will be Jupiter. The method of finding the lord of the decan. From this, you will divide the ascendant into three parts, and each division will be 10 degrees: and you will give the first division to the lord of the ascendant, and the second to the lord of the fifth sign from it, and the third to the lord of the ninth: for the ascendant, the fifth, and the ninth are always one triplicity: for example: from the beginning of Aries up to its tenth degree, the decan is Mars. And if it is from the 10th degree up to the 20th degree, its decan will be the Sun, lord of Leo. And if it is from the 20th up to its end, its decan will be Jupiter, lord of Sagittarius. From this, the lord of the orb in nativities, that is, you will look at the lord of the hour in which the native is born, and you will give the ascendant and the lord of the hour in the first year of his nativity, and by him, that is, the lord of the hour, will be signified the health or illness of the native's body, just as it is signified by the lord of the radical ascendant, that is, of the nativity: and you will give the lord of the second hour from it to the second house from the ascendant in the second year, and by him will be signified his being in that year, the being of substance, etc., just as it is signified by the being of the lord of the house of substance: and you will give the lord of the third hour from it to the third house from the ascendant in the third year, and by the being of that one in that year will be signified the being of brothers and sisters and others, just as it will be signified by the being of the lord of the third house. And you will give the lord of the fourth hour to the fourth house from the ascendant in the fourth year: and by his being in that year will be signified the being of fathers and those who are signified by the fourth house. Similarly, you will do with the lords of the hours by succession, that is, you will give the lord of each hour to the radical house, and the lord of the 12th hour from the hour of nativity will be the 12th house from the radical ascendant and the 12th year. And the lord of the 13th hour from the nativity of the radical ascendant and the 13th year. And the lord of the 14th hour from it will be the house of substance and the 14th year. And the lord of the first hour is named the lord of the ascendant of the hour. The lord of the second hour is the lord of the hour of the house of substance, and the lord of the third hour is the lord of the hour of the house of brothers: and so on for the others. Similarly, the lord of each of these hours is named by the name of the house: and he is also named the lord of the orb, and by him is signified every year, just as it is signified by the Alcochoden: that is, by the lord of the year: and some astrologers place the lord of the orb, that is, of the radical ascendant, in the first year, and in the second year the planet that succeeds him, and in the third year the planet that succeeds him, as has been said in the lord of the hour. From this, the Alfridaria disposition: that is, when the nativity is diurnal, the Alfridaria Sun will preside over the disposition of his life in the beginning, according to the quantity of his Alfridaria years, which are ten: after this, the planet that succeeds the Sun, which is Venus, whose Alfridaria years are eight. And after Venus, the planet that succeeds her, which is Mercury, and his years are thirteen: then the Moon: and her Alfridaria years are nine: then Saturn, and his Alfridaria years are eleven. Then Jupiter, and his Alfridaria years are twelve: then Mars, and his Alfridaria years are seven: then the Head of the Dragon, and his Alfridaria years are three: after this, the Tail: and her Alfridaria years are two. The collected years together are 75 years. After this, the disposition returns to the Sun, and similarly up to the last of the planets. But if the nativity is nocturnal, the disposition begins with the Moon, and she will dispose of her Alfridaria years, which are nine. Similarly, planet after planet, as we have said for the Sun. When a planet has disposed of its Alfridaria years, it will dispose of its own first seventh part of its Alfridaria only. Then in the second seventh, the planet that succeeds it will participate: after this, in the third seventh, the third planet that succeeds will participate, and so on until the planet that is before it participates in the last seventh of its Alfridaria years: and each has a judgment when it participates with another over the nativity. From this, the Almanar, that is, the preeminence by which it is said that a planet goes over a planet: that is, you will look at the mean course of the planet and its equated place: and if its equated place is less than its mean course, it will be ascending from the middle of its circle up to the summit of the circle: and if its equated place is more than its mean course, it will be descending from the middle of its circle down to its lowest point: and if its equated place is equal to its mean course, it will be in the middle of its circle. Then you will subtract the planet's place from its mean course after you have most certainly known this, that is, the equated place: or conversely, subtracting the smaller from the larger of them, and you will multiply what remains by seven and divide by 22: and what comes out of the division will be this for every planet according to the quantity of its ascension or descension. For Venus and Mercury, we take what is between both places, that is, what is between the places.

[Planetary Strength and Aspects]
We do as above with the Sun, Venus, and Mercury, because by this we know which of them is stronger in the circle of the apogee. But when Venus and Mercury, if either of them is oriental and its place is equal to less than the Sun's place, you will take the remainder, which is between the Sun's place and its place, and you will do with it as you have done, as was said, in the higher planets, by multiplication and division. And the signification of the planets is more proper and stronger when they have gone over each other, that is, when one has gone over the other in conjunction. In opposition, however, and in the quartile aspect, their signification will be less apparent and weaker. And yet, when one of them is ascending and the other descending, then the ascending one goes above the descending one. But when both are descending, the one with the lesser declination goes above the one with the greater or more declination. If, however, both are ascending, the one with the greater ascension goes above the one with the lesser ascension. It also says in another way, that is, so that you know the latitude of both planets, because their northern one goes over the meridian. And if both are northern, the one with the greater latitude goes over the one with the lesser latitude. If, however, both are southern, the one with the lesser latitude goes over the one with the greater latitude. Therefore, it is said that the Moon goes over Jupiter in these two operations.
