Similarly, if either of the two planets is in the middle of the circle, having no latitude, then the ascending northern one goes over the one that lacks latitude, and the one without latitude goes over the descending southern one. And from this, the opening of the gates is said to occur when an inferior planet joins a superior planet, and their houses are opposite. And from this, Albuzic, which is a thing that the Indians greatly observed. For they numbered 12 hours after the conjunction of the Sun and Moon, and applied them to the Sun, dividing the 12 hours into three parts, that is, into the hours of the Sun. And they judge over all four hours according to the judgment of the lords of the triplicity of the Sun at the hour of conjunction. Then they give to Venus after 12 hours and divide them again into three parts, and judge over every third division according to the lords of the triplicity of Venus at the hour of conjunction. After this, they do similarly with Mercury and the other planets in their succession until the orb returns to the Sun after 84 hours, and they do not cease to do so frequently until the second conjunction comes. And some say that Albuzic is this: that after the conjunction there are 12 unequal hours, which are called combust, and no one should begin any work in these. And after these hours, there are 72 uncombust hours in which the beginning of works is useful. And after these 72 uncombust hours, there are 12 combust hours similarly until the conjunction that follows. After this, they divide these 12 hours into three divisions, that is, into parts. They said that when someone begins to walk or wage war in the first four hours, the loss of life will be feared. In the second four hours, the detriment of one's body will be feared without the loss of life. And in the last four hours, the detriment of one's substance and one's own and all that they possess is to be feared.

[The Fifth Difference: Parts]
The fifth difference in the commemoration of all parts. And because we have completed the expositions of those things that follow from the names of the astrologers, let us now pursue the commemoration of all parts. And when we have noted the place of the parts, take from that place to that place and project this from the ascendant or from another place. We say that you add to that whatever is between the two places of the degrees of the ascendant, and project from the ascendant or from the beginning of the sign from which you project. An example of this is the operation of the Part of Fortune, because you take whatever is between the Sun and the Moon in degrees, and you add to those degrees of the ascendant sign. Whatever is collected, you project it from 30 to 30 degrees, and you begin to project from the beginning of the ascendant sign, and where the number ends, there is the Part of Fortune. And at night, conversely, from the Moon to the Sun, and you add the degrees of the ascendant sign above, and project this from 30 to 30, and begin to project from the beginning of the ascendant sign. Let us begin here, therefore, after the Part of Fortune, the 12 parts of the houses, and let us begin from the ascendant. The first house is the Part of Life, and it is taken by day from Jupiter to Saturn, and at night conversely, and it is projected from the ascendant. The Part of Bile is taken from the degree of conjunction or prevention that was before the nativity up to the degree of the Moon, and it is projected from the ascendant. The Part of Future Things, that is, the Part of the Sun, is taken by day from the Moon to the Sun, and at night conversely, and it is projected from the ascendant. The Part of Love and Concord, that is, the Part of Venus, is taken by day from the Part of Fortune to the Part of Future Things, and at night conversely, and it is projected from the ascendant. The Part of Stability and Trust of the Ascendant of the Duration of the Native is like the Part of Concord and Love. The Part of Animosity and Audacity, that is, the Part of Mars, is taken by day from Mars to the degree of the Part of Fortune, and at night conversely, and it is projected from the ascendant. The second house is the Part of Substance, and it is taken by day and night from the lord of the house of substance to the degree and minute of the house of substance, and it is projected from the ascendant. The Part of Poverty and Smallness of Ingenuity, that is, the Part of Mercury, is taken by day from the Part of Future Things to the Part of Fortune, and at night conversely, and it is projected from the ascendant. The Part of Beatitude and Triumph and Victory, that is, the Part of Jupiter, is taken by day from the Part of Future Things to Jupiter, and at night conversely, and it is projected from the ascendant. The third house is the Part of Brothers, and it is taken by day from Saturn to Jupiter, and at night conversely, and it is projected from the ascendant. The Part of Benevolence of Brothers is taken by day from the Sun to Saturn, and at night conversely, and it is projected from the ascendant. If Saturn is under the rays, it is taken by day from the Sun to Jupiter, and at night conversely, and it is projected from the ascendant.

[Fourth House Parts]
The fourth house is the part of the fathers. It is taken by day from the Sun to Saturn, and by night the reverse, and it is projected from the ascendant. The part of the father's death is taken by day from Saturn to Jupiter, and by night the reverse, and it is projected from the ascendant. The part of the years is taken by day from the lord of the Sun's house to Saturn, and by night the reverse, and it is projected from the ascendant. And if the Sun or any of Saturn's houses is in its own house, take it by day from the Sun to Saturn, and by night the reverse, and project it from the ascendant, and do not consider whether Saturn is apparent or under the rays. The part of inheritances and possessions is taken by day and night from Saturn to the Moon, and it is projected from the ascendant. The part of the native's nobility, and of him about whom there is doubt whether he is the son of that father to whom he is attributed, or of another, is taken by day from the degree of the Sun to the degree of its exaltation, and it is projected from the ascendant. But if the Sun is in the degree of its exaltation by day, and the Moon by night in the degree of its exaltation, the part will be in the degrees of the ascendant, and it will be the signification of the degree of the ascendant. The part of the end of things is taken by day and night from Saturn to the lord of the house of conjunction or arrival, and it is added above the degrees of the ascendant, and it is projected from the ascendant. The fifth house is the part of children, and it is taken by day from Jupiter to Saturn, and by night the reverse, and it is projected from the ascendant. The part that signifies the time when a son should be born, and the number of males or females, and what the woman will bear, is taken by day and night from Mars to Jupiter, and it is projected from the ascendant. The part of the knowledge of a male and female child is taken by day and night from the Moon to Jupiter, and it is projected from the ascendant. The part by which it is known whether the native about whom the question is asked is male or female is taken by day from the lord of the Moon's house to the Moon, and by night the reverse, and it is projected from the ascendant. The part signifying the son when Jupiter reaches him, that is, to the degree of the part signifying the son, is taken by day and night from Mars to Jupiter, and it is projected from the ascendant. The part of affection and joy is taken by day and night from Venus to Saturn, and it is projected from the ascendant. The part of the knowledge of the existence of children is taken by day and night from the Moon to Venus, and it is projected from the ascendant. The sixth house is the part of infirmity and azemena, that is, inseparable weakness of some member, and it is taken by day from Saturn to Mars, and by night the reverse, and it is projected from the ascendant. The part of servants is taken by day from Mercury to the Moon, and by night the reverse, and it is projected from the ascendant. And Alendezgod said that it is taken by day from Mercury to the Part of Fortune, and by night the reverse. And he said: it is necessary to use both parts together. The seventh house is the part of the betrothal of men or marriage, and it is taken by day and night from the Sun to Venus, and it is projected from the ascendant. And this part is similar to the part of the mandates of rumors. And the part of the betrothal of women or marriage, according to Hermes, is taken by day and night from Venus to Saturn, and it is projected from the ascendant. And this part is congruent with the part of the cultivation of the earth. Also, the part of the betrothal of women according to Velius is taken by day and night from the Sun to Mars, and it is projected from the ascendant. The part of affection and pleasure is taken by day and night from Venus to the degree of the seventh, and it is projected from the ascendant. The part of marriages is taken by day and night from Saturn to Venus, and it is projected from the ascendant. The eighth house is the part of death, and it is taken by day and night from the Moon to the degree and minute of the eighth house, and it is added above what Saturn has washed in its sign, and it is projected from the beginning of Saturn's sign. The part of the planet that kills is taken by day from the lord of the ascendant's degree to the Moon's degree, and by night the reverse. The part of the year in which the native fears death, and poverty, impediment, and destruction, is taken by day and night from Saturn to the degree of the lord of the house of conjunction or prevention that occurred before the native's birth. The part of bondage and imprisonment, whether one is freed from it or not, is taken by day from Saturn to the Part of Fortune, and by night the reverse. The ninth house is the part of peregrination, and it is taken by day and night from the lord of the ninth house to the degree and minute of the ninth house, and it is projected from the ascendant. The part of travel by water is taken by day from Saturn to the 15th degree of the sign of Cancer, and by night the reverse. And if Saturn is in the 15th degree of Cancer, the degree of the part will be the degree of the ascendant. The part of religion is taken by day from the Moon to Mercury, and by night the reverse, and it is projected from the ascendant. The tenth house is the part of region and kingdom, and what work the native does, and it is taken by day and night from Saturn to the Moon, and it is projected from the ascendant. The part of the king and kingdom is taken by day from Mars to the Moon, and by night the reverse, and it is projected from the ascendant. And there is another part similar to the part of the fathers. The part of work and kingdom according to Velius is taken by day and night from the Sun to the degree of the Midheaven, and it is projected from the ascendant. The part signifying whether there is a cause for the kingdom or not is taken by day and night from the Sun to the degree of the Midheaven, and it is projected from Jupiter. The part of Mars is taken by day from Venus to the Moon, and by night the reverse, and it is projected from the ascendant. The eleventh house is the part of friends, and it is taken by day and night from the Moon to Mercury, and it is projected from the ascendant. And Alendezgod said that it is taken by night the reverse. The part signifying the effect of friends and friendship is taken by day from the Part of Fortune to the part of future things, and by night the reverse, and so on. The twelfth house is the part of enemies according to Hermes, and it is taken by day and night from the lord of the house of enemies to the degree and minute of the house of enemies, and it is projected from the ascendant. And according to some ancients, it is taken by day and night from Saturn to Mars, etc. And these are the parts of the 12 houses. And these are other parts that the masters of astrological judgments use much. Among these is the part that signifies false rumors when it falls in a tortuous or mutable sign, or the lord of the house is retrograde or impeded, or malefics aspect it or are conjoined with it. And it signifies the truth of rumors if it falls with benefics or in their houses or terms, or if they aspect it, or if it is in a direct sign, and it is taken by day from Mercury.

[Parts of Kingdoms and Revolutions]
in Venus at night, and conversely, and it is projected. And according to Albumasar, in the day from Mercury to the Moon, and at night conversely, etc. The part of reason and profundity of sense is taken in the day from Saturn to the Moon, and at night conversely, etc. The part of wisdom and discipline is taken in the day and night from Saturn to Jupiter, and it is projected, etc. The part of war and battles is taken in the day and night from Saturn to the Moon, and it is projected from the Ascendant. The part of peace and concord of armies is taken in the day and night from the Moon to Mercury, and it is projected from the Ascendant. The part of looking in the revolution of the year is taken in the day from the Moon to Venus, and at night conversely, and it is projected from the Sun. Concerning the parts of revolutions in the causes of kingdoms. Because, with God's help, we have introduced these parts which are suitable for particular matters, we will pursue the parts which are suitable for the revolutions of the years of the world and the conjunctions signifying the causes of the kingdom's stability or its duration. Among these is the part which is called the part of the kingdom or empire, which is exercised in the revolution of the world: it is taken from Mars to the Moon, and it is projected from the Ascendant of the conjunction which signifies the change of the kingdom. Likewise, it is taken in another way, namely, from the degree of the Ascendant of the conjunction to the degree of the conjunction, and it is projected from the degree of the Ascendant of the revolution. Also, it is taken in another way from the degree of the Midheaven of the revolution to the Sun, and it is projected from Jupiter, i.e., from the degree of Jupiter. The part of the king's time, that is, how long he should endure, is taken at the hour of the king's election from the Sun to the 15th degree of the sign of Leo, and it is projected from the Moon; then it is taken from the Moon to the 15th degree of the sign of Cancer, and it is projected from the Sun. Another part concerning the time of the king's election is taken at the hour of the king's election in the day from Jupiter to Saturn, and at night conversely, and it is projected from the Ascendant of the revolution of the year in which the king arose. If Jupiter was in a common sign and the revolution was diurnal, and Jupiter was cadent from the angles, then it is taken from Saturn to Jupiter, and 30 degrees are added above, and it is projected from the Ascendant. But if Saturn and Jupiter were opposite to each other and both were cadent from the Ascendant, the midpoint between them is taken, i.e., half the degrees between them are taken, and it is projected from the Ascendant. And if Jupiter was in his exaltation, and the revolution was at night, it is counted from him to Saturn, and it is projected from the Ascendant. These are the parts from which the time of the king's election and its duration are primarily extracted. The first of these is to look at the hour of the king's election, which comes from the annual profection from the conjunction of the triplicity which signified the sect, from a certain number, for every 30 degrees a year, and for every two and a half degrees a month. When you know in what degree or sign this is, keep it, because this is the place from which you will equate the first part. And when you want to apply it, you will apply the Ascendant of the revolution of the year in which the elected one arose. After this, look from the oriental planet, from the Sun, and Saturn, and Jupiter in that year, to the degree of the equation of the first part, which is kept. Project it from the Ascendant of the revolution of the year, and where the number arrives, that is the place of the first part. The second part is found thus: take at the conjunction in which the king arose or began to reign, to what sign or degree the profection of the year arrived, from the number given for every 30 degrees a year, and 2 and a half degrees a month, up to the day the king arose, and that will be the place of the equation of the second part. Keep it. After this, look from the occidental planet, from the Sun, and Saturn, and Jupiter, to the place of the equation of the second part which you kept, and project it from the Ascendant of the revolution, and where it arrives will be the place of the second part. These are the parts which signify the strength of the king and his duration. There are other parts which are used in the revolutions of the years of the world, and by them it is known what is heavy in the market, and what will be light in price, or what is precious or vile, much or little. This is to look at where the part fell, that is, in whose planet's house, exaltation, term, or triplicity. If that planet is retrograde or combust or in a bad place, that thing will be vile and of little value. But if it is in a place of strength or in the angles, especially in the Midheaven, that thing will be heavy and of great price. And if the lord of the house comes to the place of its fall, that thing will be vile. And look at the aspects of the benefics and malefics to them, and also to the Moon and its ruler. And see how and by whom that part is aspected. If a benefic and the Moon aspect that part, that thing will be multiplied. If malefics aspect it, it will suffer detriment. The part of the disposition of the year from the Moon to Mercury. The part of water from the Moon to Venus. The part of barley from the Moon to Jupiter. The part of chickpeas (which is a kind of legume) from Venus to the Sun. The part of lentils from Mars to Saturn. The part of beans from Saturn to Mars. The part of millet from Saturn to Mars. The part of onions from Saturn to Mars. The part of wheat from the Sun to Mars. The part of nuts from Mercury to Mars. The part of sugar from Mercury to Venus. The part of dates from the Sun to Venus. The part of honey from the Moon to the Sun. The part of rice (which is a kind of grain) from Jupiter to Saturn. The part of olives from Mercury to the Moon. The part of grapes from Saturn to Venus. The part of cotton from Mercury to Venus. The part of sesame (which is a kind of white seed similar to flax seed, and doctors use it, and a useful ointment is made from it) from Mercury to Jupiter or from Saturn to Venus. The part of melons (which are large and yellow) from Mercury to Saturn. The part of sour foods from Saturn to Mars. The part of sweet foods from the Sun to Venus. The part of foods with the taste of celery or similar herbs from Mars to Saturn. The part of bitter foods from Mercury to Saturn. The part of sour medicines from Saturn to Jupiter. The part of salty medicines from Mars to the Moon. The part of poisonous medicines from the Dragon's Head to Saturn. And all these are projected from the Ascendant of the revolution of the year. These are all the parts that have come down to us. We have also introduced these last parts, and if there is a weak narration in them, it is so that I would not omit anything that could be introduced to the mastery of astrological judgments, but rather prefer it. The table of friendship and enmity of the signs. Friends: Aries, Leo, Sagittarius, Taurus, Virgo, Capricorn, Gemini, Libra, Aquarius. Enemies: Cancer, Scorpio, Pisces.

[The Wise Man Rules the Stars]
The commentary of John of Saxony on the text of Alchabitius. The wise man will rule the stars. My Ptolemy says in the wisdom of the Almagest: And it can be declared thus: He will rule the stars who can impede or prohibit the effects coming from them. But a wise man can do this, therefore, etc. The major premise is manifest: that he rules another who can tell him to do this and he does it, and to leave this and he leaves it. The minor premise is proven by the authority of Ptolemy in the first proposition of the Centiloquium, where it is said: The best astrologer can prohibit much evil that is to come according to the stars, when he has foreknown its nature. For thus he will forewarn him to whom evil is to come, so that when it comes, he may be able to endure it. And it is confirmed by the authority of the same in the eighth proposition of the same, where he says: A wise soul will assist the work of the stars just as a sower assists natural strengths. But it must be noted concerning the way in which a wise man can impede or assist the work of the stars. It is certain that we cannot simply impede celestial influence, just as we cannot impede the combustion of fire; but we can dispose the patient to receive celestial influence in one way or another. For we see that the same heat of the sun dissolves ice and hardens clay. Haly gives a familiar example of this in his commentary on the aforementioned proposition: The best astrologer, etc., saying: if we know that someone is to suffer a hot and dry illness of the nature of Mars, we can, before the advent of that influence, change him to the opposite, that is, to coldness and humidity; and thus the influence that should have caused him illness will reduce him to a temperate state. It is also clear to everyone that we can impede the action of fire from burning a specific combustible, that is, by removing it from the fire or by pouring water over it. Since therefore knowledge is divided according to the division of the things of which they are, everyone is called wise in his own knowledge, taking wisdom broadly for knowledge, as Albumazar takes it in many places of his Introduction: so that we may see of which wise men the proposed words are spoken: we can distinguish between wise men and wise men in a certain universal way. Therefore, among the number of wise men, some are truly wise, others apparently so. Aristotle touches on this distinction in the first book of the Elenchi, where he says: Some are beautiful because of their beauty; others, however, pretend to be so. And these, that is, apparently wise men, are divided into two parts: for some of them appear wise only according to the estimation of the common people, like the rich of this world. And some among the advanced, like the sophists. The first are those who have the riches of this world, of whom Albumazar speaks in his great Introduction where he discusses the sects contradicting astronomy. And these are of the new sect. Albumazar says there: He is more worthy in the eyes of the generality of the common people who has more substance. Thus it is because the dignity of substance among them is greater than the dignity of knowledge. And they say that when a man has substance, it does not hinder him if he is unskilled in the science of the stars, and medicine, and other sciences, which he proves with a most false proof: for they prove science by substance. And this proof of error is a most false proof: for things are proven by their genus and by what is similar to them, that is, wisdom by wisdom, substance by substance, and not by what is dissimilar to them, therefore it does not prove wisdom by substance. Others appear learned or wise among some advanced people, like the sophists. Of whom Haly says in the first book of the Elenchi: For some it is more worthwhile to seem and not to be than to be and not to seem; and Master Alanus de Insulis, speaking of them, says: Poor jurists avoid his schools: he stirs up real disputes: they become antagonists. Here he proves, here he disapproves: to this he concludes, to that. And the sophist shouts with a hundred mouths. Truly learned men differ according to more and less certainty, as the Commentator says in the second book of Metaphysics. Mathematical sciences are in the highest degree of certainty. Natural sciences follow them. These are less certain, that is, logicians and natural philosophers not transferring themselves to other sciences, they have nothing of philosophy except words: of these also Master Alanus says: He always shouts and argues, while he searches the hidden places of Aristotle. But if you ask what or how much the mind lives on by study, but rather by philosophizing. Mathematicians are more certain. And these are divided into two parts: for some of them study the motions of the times and do not care about judgments, or deny them. And these are of whom Albumazar speaks in the sixth and fifth sect of those who speak of judgments, indeed it will be seen later. The second, however, study motions and judgments: of whom Alanus speaks, referring to Albumazar himself: There Albumazar consults the stars, the poles, the sky, and the seven planets, and brings back their reports to the earth. He arms the lands and the perishable things with counsel. Against celestial wrath and the fury of the gods. Of these Ptolemy says in the proposed words: A wise man will rule the stars. In these words Ptolemy touches on three properties or conditions that a true philosopher must have, especially an astrologer, by which three kinds of men are repelled from astronomy. The first condition is stability of intention. The second is ability of disposition. The third is the renunciation of earthly possessions. He touches on the first when he says: man. The second when he says: wise. The third when he says: he will rule the stars. As for the first condition, Ptolemy says in the first proposition of the Centiloquium: The science of the stars is from you and from them. And Haly in his commentary on the same says: He who desires to know future things must proceed in two ways. One is to accept the motion of the stars and the works that are done in things according to their motion. And to look at the books that the ancients wrote about the signification of their motions, and to add to these what he has proven in his own theory. Therefore, since there is great labor in observing the motions of the stars, an astrologer cannot be effeminate or remiss. And since much time is required to consult the books of the ancients, he cannot be a vagabond. Therefore, it is necessary that an astrologer be firm and stable in meditation. And thus the effeminate and remiss are repelled from astronomy. As for the second condition, Ptolemy says in the seventh proposition of the Centiloquium: No one will be able to give certain judgments according to the complexion of the stars, unless he is a man who has well known the strength of the soul and the natural complexion. Therefore, he wants a man to be naturally disposed to this science so that he may profit in it. This, according to what seems to me, is this science above all sciences. For I have seen good clerics in logic and natural philosophy who could in no way grasp anything of astronomy, not even algorism. Therefore, it is clear that those who are naturally indisposed are repelled from astronomy, of whom Albumazar makes a sect, as will be seen immediately. As for the third condition, Haly says in the commentary on the first proposition of the Centiloquium

[On the Conditions for Astrological Knowledge]
Because it is necessary for us to be solicitous about worldly things, the knowledge of future things is taken away from us. But if we were separated from all worldly things, we could prognosticate future things. For this reason, we see many hermits who predict future things. And some epileptics, while tormented by epilepsy, predict future things, because then they do not use bodily senses but only the power of the soul. Therefore, the philosopher, our father, does not say that a rich man is a philosopher, as the philosopher says in the seventh book of Politics. It is not necessary for a philosopher to be the lord of land and sea, but it is sufficient for him to have a servant who ministers vegetables to him. And thus, those who have the riches of this world are repelled from astronomy. Socrates, realizing this, threw gold into the sea, as Valerius narrates. This condition does not please many, nor even me. As for these conditions, Albumazar consoles us in his Introduction, and especially as to the last one, because he changes it to the opposite. He says thus: "And perhaps some are not sufficient for the wisdom of this mastery, while they look at certain things to arrive from truth and their comprehension, so that they can repel error from themselves due to the brevity of their exercise in the knowledge of all things, the knowledge of which is necessary for them in that same intention, as to the first conditions." And after a few intervening words, he says: "And subtle men and those of profound wisdom, perhaps many of those who use them are not sufficient to comprehend them, since the science of this mastery will be the science of other masteries that are necessary in the presence of things due to the profundity that we have said is far from the senses, as to the second condition." Then he consoles us and says: "That which can be attained from its science should not be annulled because of that which cannot be attained." And after a few intervening words, he says that a little wisdom is of much profit. And in this, he changes the third condition to the opposite. And he proves that there is greater utility in astronomy than in any other science. And if error occurs in it, it is more tolerable and less harmful than in other sciences. And he says thus: "For we see physicians err in the prescience of infirmities and diseases, while they predict what happens to the sick from the gravity of the disease and its lightness, and the swiftness of health and its slowness, and also their health or death. But that little error of physicians does not prevent them from the pursuit of their mastery and from its disposition and exercise, nor does it generate blame or doubt among men towards them, who have sought utility and profit from a little error in their mastery through their cure and acquiesce to their medicines. Similarly, shipmasters do not abandon their mastery, nor do men abandon the course of the sea because of a little error of sailors. Similarly, the authors of other wisdoms and masteries can hardly escape the accidents of error or the advent of some impediment that happens to them; but because of this, their mastery is not annulled. And among all these things that we have said, the error of impediment is greater than the error of astrologers, because when a physician errs in the prescience of infirmities, or cure, or in medicines, perhaps this will be the cause of the perdition of souls. And when sailors err, perhaps this will be the cause of the perdition of ships and their shipwreck and the death of those who are in them. And if shepherds and the authors of animal deception err, perhaps this will be the provocation of the perdition of that same kind of animals. But if astrologers err, this is more attributed to the ignorance of the astrologer in the prescience of things, for the inquirer omits to guard against horrible things before they come and because of

[The Dignity of Astrology]
This perhaps will be a dismissal of caution, a provocation of those good things to come, and perhaps there will be loss in them, and perhaps not. In other arts, however, it is not so, because the greatest error of authors is loss and impediment without doubt. And in this, too, what we have said is the dignity and the dignities of the science of the stars. If, therefore, the art of the stars is more dignified and nobler than other arts, and the path of its art in error at certain times is below the path of other arts, and their error is sounder and less impeded, their truth is of greater profit. Therefore, it is right that all intellectual and wise people should receive astrologers and use them and acquiesce to their truth in what they say. This science, especially that part which is about judgments, has many rivals and adversaries. Ptolemy, noticing this in his Quadripartitum, confirms the judgments of the stars, and Albumasar in his great Introductorium. And both agree in the method of confirmation, except that Albumasar posits more than Ptolemy and uses more reasons. Both, in confirming judgments, begin with the operation of the sun. For Ptolemy says in the thirteenth proposition of the first part: "Because the sun operates with the air in all things existing on earth." And Paley, in his commentary, explaining Ptolemy's words, says: "Ptolemy wants to show us that the sphere of fire and air, which is changed by celestial bodies, changes all things that are on earth." And Paley, in his commentary on the second proposition of the same, says that the roots of this science are so manifest that common people, knowing nothing, know and understand them by observing and experiencing them. And Ptolemy, in the 21st proposition, says that ignorant common people know things before they happen. And what is more, he says that mute animals know things before they happen. Albumasar also confirms the science of judgments by many reasons, which it would be very long to narrate all now. Specifically, however, Albumasar disputes against those who deny the judgments of the stars and divides them into ten sects. And I will briefly touch on two or three words about each sect. The first sect says that the planets have no significance over things that happen in this world, which is below the circle of the moon. To these, Albumasar says that all philosophers agree that every substance that moves by natural motion produces natural changes in the essences of things connected to it by nature. And he declares this in the action of fire. But celestial bodies move by natural motion; therefore, they produce natural changes in the four elements connected to them by nature. Albumasar alludes to this reason in many words. The saying of Aristotle in the first book of Meteorology could also be assumed for that sect: "It is necessary for the inferior world to be contiguous to the superior motions, so that all its power may be governed from there." The second sect is of those who said that the planets have significations only over universal things, such as the four elements, and are genera and species. Against these, Albumasar puts forth, among other things, such a reason: "The whole is not the whole except through its parts; therefore, if they signify over the whole, namely over the species, it is necessary that they signify over the individuals which are parts of the species." The third sect is of certain disputants who said that the planets have no signification over the possible, but only over the necessary and the impossible. And Albumasar says that the philosopher dissolved the reasons of these and affirmed the possible by many reasons. And among others, he posits that which Aristotle posits in the first book of Peri Hermeneias, namely, that one should not deliberate or assist. The fourth sect is of some who looked into the science of the whole, which is the science of circles and their being. These said that the planets have no signification over things that happen and occur in this world from individuals of animals and seeds and metals. And that their signification is only over the corruption or change of times. And Albumasar says that these could not deny this quantity, namely, the change of times, to be from the strength of the work of the planets, because this is found and appears from their work, and its repulsion is a disgrace. And afterwards he argues against them from concessions. The fifth sect is of those who looked into the science of the whole and annulled the science of judgments from the part of experiments. And they said that the judgments of astronomy are not true because things happen by experiments, and the truth of a thing cannot be perceived by experiments unless it is found to be twice in one. And this is impossible in the planets, because when a planet is in some place among the signs, and the other planets are aspecting it or conjoined to it, they do not return to it from the signs except after many thousands of years, and the life of one man does not reach such a quantity of years. How then is it possible for a man to find the planets twice in one place so that he may prove from their return to their places what they signify? To these, Albumasar says that the ancients knew the natures of the planets and their significations from many and diverse things, some of which are particular and apparent, others universal. Particular apparent things are, for example, what is found from the opposition of the sun in heating and the moon in humidity and putrefaction, and from the works of the planets in the corruption and change of the air every day and night. Universal things are, for example, what is found from their signification in the revolutions of the years of the world and nativities. And briefly, the meaning of these words is that man in a short time can experience those things that commonly occur; but as for other things that rarely happen, such as great conjunctions, the sayings of our predecessors should suffice us. The sixth sect is of some arithmeticians who were lazy to look at the number of the stars and their equation from the book in which the science of the whole is most certain, namely, the Almagest, which Ptolemy published. But they sought the places of the planets by diverse tables and found the tables to differ as to the places of the planets. Therefore, they said that the judgments are not true since they do not have the true places of the planets. To these, Albumasar says that when an astrologer is about to make a judgment, he must rely on looking at the natures of the planets and their properties from the degree of each sign and its exaltation and the lords of its triplicity, and its place from the angle and its succedents and its fall from the angle and its presence in the house of substance and the house of brothers and the other houses of the circle, and then he judges. The degrees of the signs, however, have a particular signification which astrologers use in certain specific matters. But if there is an error in the place of a planet by minutes or one degree, this does not impede the art of judgments. And it is necessary for him who practices the art of judgments, when the calculator has given him the places of the planets from the signs at certain times, to judge by those places in which the planets are, whether they signify this or that. The certainty of the degree in which they are, from their signs according to truth, will be upon the calculators and will be demanded from them. And he gives an example of physicians, saying: "The physician must judge the nature of each medicine and for what it is useful and what diseases it benefits. But the inquiry into species in regions and their preparation is not to be demanded from physicians, but from the authors of species." So it is, he says, concerning the judgments of the stars. To him who practices judgments, it pertains only to defend that the planets signify over the things of this world, and what they signify; and it pertains to him to know their properties and natures. To the calculator, however, it pertains to verify their degrees. The seventh sect is of those who rejected this science because they looked into it and it was impossible for them to achieve what they wanted. And these are envious followers of this art over their knowledge in it, and they reject the science of the art of judgments because of envy. These are not to be contradicted, as Albumasar says, since their denial is for this art. For a denier should not be constrained except by that by which he is overcome and compelled to come to manifest truth. The eighth sect is of some who boast of medical science, so that they may acquire through it. Not, however, good and wise physicians in the art of medicine who have already read the books of the ancients in the science of medicine and have known the roots of their art and the diversity of elements or times and natures, and their corruption, and other things that are necessary for them in their art from simple and composite things. These have known the dignities of the science of the judgments of the stars. And they know that the science of the stars is the beginning of the science of medicine. And they use the art of judgments in the art of medicine almost frequently in the knowledge of diseases and their augmentation and diminution and in the times of healing. And their right intention in their art is multiplied, and the sick are freed by their hands and multiplied.

[The Ten Sects and Astrology's Divisions]
perfected by them. Some physicians, however, whose inexperience abounds, and whose reason is abbreviated in the knowledge of certain things necessary to them for this purpose, contend in their mastery that they should prioritize acquisition and postpone knowledge. Finally, they contradicted the science of judgments and said that there is no strength in the motions of the planets in this world. Against them, Albumasar cites the saying of Hippocrates, saying: "And Hippocrates already said in the book of air, when he made mention of the diversity of air and elements or natures, that the things we have said about the diversity of air are in the science of the stars. And that the science of the stars is no small part of the science of medicine." The ninth sect is that of the common people. And these are divided into two sects: one is of those who do not know the dignity of judgments and other sciences, nor the dignity of foreknowledge of things. The most worthy among them is he who has more substance. Of these, it was said before. Against them, Albumasar says that substance and fortune are adapted to the wise and the foolish, to the strong and the weak. And man is not praiseworthy for what is adapted to him from this, because this is not adapted to him by his knowledge, nor by his foolishness, nor by his strength or weakness, but he is praised for wisdom and knowledge, because the dignity of man above other animals is only through wisdom and knowledge and through the knowledge of things that have been and that are to come. And with some interpolations, he says that the most worthy thing in man is the knowledge of future things. The tenth sect is also of the common people. And these rejected the science of this mastery because they saw the multitude of errors of those who boast about it, because the common people receive things by the knowledge of appearance. And when they saw the multitude of errors of those who boast about this science in those things that are asked from the science of the judgments of the stars, thinking it false, they rejected it. And they refer the masters of this science to foolishness and said that it is a vain science. Albumasar says that these are not to be blamed in contradicting the masteries of this science, because most of those who boast about it are foolish, inexperienced, and fallible men. And with some interpolations, he says that these practice under the name of this mastery various seductions by which they seduce weak men. He means to say that some practice geomancy or sortilege under the name of this science. These seek nothing but profit. And he says that when these are asked about something, they extend in their answer to the thing that the questioner desires, and it suits them, wanting to make him happy for the sake of their greed. Let this suffice concerning the ten sects that Albumasar presents. And an eleventh sect could be added. And these are those who say that this science is against faith. To whom I say that they have not read the books of the ancient wise men, which if they had read, they would know that this science is not against faith, but rather for faith. For the doctors of this science posit a created world, which is the first foundation of faith. For Daly Albéragel says in the first part of his book, in the chapter on the nature of Jupiter, that at the time when God began to create the world, he placed Jupiter in the ascendant. And Albumasar says in his introduction: "And let us say first that the motion of the circle is from the power of the first cause." And with some interpolations, he says: "Behold how we have drawn the creator from apparent and known things that are perceived by the senses, that he is eternal, having power without the essence of an end, immobile and incorruptible. May his name be blessed and exalted with the greatest exaltation." I will briefly explain the division of astronomy and present the division that Albumasar presents in his great introduction. There are two kinds of astronomy: one is the science of the whole, that is, of circles and their motions. The second is the art of astrological judgments. Ptolemy also presents this division at the beginning of his Quadripartitum. And Daly in his commentary. The first kind is transmitted perfectly and completely as to principles and conclusions by Ptolemy in the Almagest. Or the first kind could be subdivided. The science of motions is twofold: some is instrumental, some tabular. That instrumental is twofold: because some are instruments for observing or investigating motions, such as Ptolemy's rules, armillary spheres, and similar things. Others are instruments for performing daily operations, such as the astrolabe, solid sphere, and similar things. The second kind, that is, the art of astrological judgments, has four principal parts. The first of which is concerning interrogations. The second concerning nativities. The third concerning the revolutions of years: and this is twofold, that is, concerning the revolutions of the years of the world and concerning the revolutions of the years of nativities. The fourth concerning elections. Daly Abéragel made a complete book on these four parts. Ptolemy, however, in the Quadripartitum, omitted two parts, that is, concerning interrogations and elections. But Daly, who commented on him, excuses him, saying: "These two parts can be sufficiently obtained from what Ptolemy says there." Besides these, there are some other parts of judgments, that is, concerning great conjunctions, concerning images, concerning seals, of which we have little or nothing. However, many ancient and modern authors, perceiving that these things were difficult to understand for those who first had to learn those sciences, made introductory books in which they set forth the principles and explained the terms that the masters of judgments use. Among other introductions, Alchabitius's book is the most approved among modern authors. Therefore, leaving others aside, we intend to deal with it for the present. Let us descend to the letter. requested by the lord. At the beginning of this book, seven things can be asked. First, what is the intention of the book. Second, what is its utility. Third, what is the title of the book. Fourth, to which part of philosophy it is subordinated. Fifth, when it should be read. Sixth, concerning the subject of the book. Seventh, concerning the division of the book. The intention of the book is to make clear the science of every thing whose science is necessary for the beginner to learn the science of the judgments of the stars. Its utility is clear: because everyone who wants to begin the science of judgments, the teaching of this book will be sufficient for him; which if he understands well, he will be able to understand all books of judgments by himself. The title of this book is as follows: "Here begin the Isagoges of Alchabitius to the science of the judgments of the stars." And it should be read before every book of the judgments of the stars. From what part it is, is clear from the preceding. For it is part of the science of the judgments of the stars. Its subject is that which is the subject in all judicial astronomy, that is, the celestial body insofar as through motion and light it causes generation and corruption in things existing under the orb of the moon. The division of the book will become clear in the process. This book is divided by the first division into two parts, namely, into a proemial part and an executive part. The executive part begins there: "In the name of the Lord, the zodiac, etc." The executive part is divided into five parts according to how the author divides it in the text, which he calls five differences, as will immediately become clear. The proemial part can be divided into four parts, because in the first, he invokes divine aid for the completion of his work; and with this, he seeks the goodwill of his king, at whose instance he perhaps composed this book. In the second part, he shows the cause of his book or the motive that moved him to make this book. In the third part, he excuses himself for the reasons. In the fourth part, he presents the division of his book. The second part begins there: "When he saw." The third part begins there: "I have not introduced." The fourth part begins there: "And I divided it into five differences." First, briefly, as a faithful man, he asks God for a long life, so that he can complete his work. And he asks for the durability of the honors of the king's sword and the preservation of his works and the expansion of his empire. "When I saw." In this part, he presents the causes that moved him to make this book. And he says that when he saw many of the ancients make introductory books to the science of the judgments of the stars, and some of them did not include all things necessary for introductions, and some transmitted what they transmitted too prolixly, so that they were lost among their confused sayings, that is, those things necessary for the introduction were obscured. And also some did not press in their sayings the order of discipline, placing first what should be placed first, and placing last what should be placed last, but did it first. He began to publish this book and collected in it from the sayings of the ancients those things that were necessary for the introduction, and omitted the useless. And "I have not introduced" here he excuses himself for the reasons and says that he did not include in this book the reasons that would be

[Ptolemy's Confirmation of Judgments]
It is necessary to defend what I have said: that these positions are in Ptolemy's book, without quadripartition. For there Ptolemy confirms judgments by many reasons. And he says that he made a book on the confirmation of judgments where he placed sufficient reasons for this. d iiij. Here he sets out the division of his book. And he says, 'And I divided it into these differences, as is clear from reading the letters.' The names of the lords. The zodiac. Indeed, the treatise begins when finished. And it can be divided into five parts, which are five differences according to how the author divides it in the letter. The first difference is about the essential and accidental being of the circle of signs. The second is about the natures of the seven planets. The third is what happens to the seven planets. The fourth is about explaining the terms or names that the masters of judgments use. The fifth is about the projection of parts. The second difference begins there: 'and with the help of God.' The third there: 'For the being of the planets.' The fourth there: 'The beginning of these.' The fifth there: 'and when I have noted.' The first part is divided into two, because in the first part he explains the essential being of the circle of signs. Secondly, about the accidental being. The second there. 'For the circle is formed at every hour.' The first part can be divided into four parts. In the first, he determines the division of the circle of signs and those things that follow that division. In the second part, he determines the dignities of the planets in the signs. In the third, about the figures of the signs. In the fourth, what the signs have from the limbs of man and what they have from regions and plants. The second part begins there: 'which the planets have.' The third there: 'these figures of the signs follow.' The fourth there: 'and one which.' The first part can be divided into five. In the first part, he sets out the division of the circle of signs. In the second part, he compares them to each other. In the third, he compares them to the four seasons of the year, and to the four ages, and to the four humors. In the fourth, he sets out the order of the planets and explains what he means when he says 'a planet is in a sign.' In the fifth, he adds something about the head and tail of the dragon. The second begins there: 'and six of these signs are northern.' The third there: 'and he calls them the fourth.' The fourth there: 'but to all planets.' The fifth there: 'it also signifies by the head and tail.' First, he says the circle of signs is divided into twelve equal parts which are called signs and are named by the names of the twelve images that are in the circle of signs, which are Aries, Taurus, Gemini, etc. And each sign is divided into thirty equal parts which are called degrees. And each degree is divided into sixty, which are called minutes. And each minute into sixty, which are called seconds. And each second into sixty, which are called thirds. And each third into sixty, which are called fourths. And so on to infinity. Around this part, two doubts can be raised. The first is about the number of signs. The second is about the order. Albumazar disputes about the number of signs, saying: 'Some of those who thought differently from us contradicted the sayings of the ancients regarding the number of signs. And they said, 'Why do you suppose that there are twelve signs, neither more nor less?'' To these, Albumazar responds, saying: 'The philosopher Aratus revealed 48 images that are in the circle, i.e., in the eighth sphere, and their names. And all the ancient sages authorized his opinion and agreed with him on this. And twelve of these images are in the circle of signs. Therefore, they said there are twelve.' Albumazar assigns another reason, saying: 'Philosophers found that all things that are made and destroyed in this world are composed of elements, and every individual that is made from the four elements has three beings: beginning, middle, and end. Therefore, the four elements multiplied by three make twelve; therefore, there are twelve signs.' The third reason is that by the motion of the sun, generation and corruption occur in things. Its work is more desired in this world than the work of other planets. And it rotates in these twelve images, and they are its place. And according to its course in these twelve images, the seasons of the year vary. Therefore, philosophers placed twelve images as more worthy of signification. And they attributed universal signification to them. To the other thirty-six images, they attributed particular signification. The second doubt is about the order and the beginning. For someone might say, 'Why did they begin with Aries, since a circle has neither beginning nor end?' To this, Ptolemy says in the 156th proposition of the first part of the Quadripartite: 'The reason for beginning with Aries is that it is a masculine sign, and the agent is more worthy than the patient, and the equinoctial passes through it, and from there, with the equinoctial, the greatest change of the whole firmament begins.' But someone might say by this reason that the beginning should be from Libra, which is a masculine sign, the equinoctial passes through it, and the greatest motion of the firmament is there. Why then did they begin with Aries rather than Libra? It can be resolved by Ptolemy's statement in the 140th proposition of the first part, where he says that the beginning in the firmament is that place where the complexion of the time is more humid, just as the first age of animals is when the complexion is more humid. It could also be said that generation begins with Aries, but corruption with Libra. Regarding the order, someone might ask why they placed Taurus after Aries, and then Gemini, then Cancer. Albumazar says that there are four simple qualities of the elements, namely, heat, dryness, humidity, and coldness. And two of these are like agents, namely, heat and coldness, and the other two are like patients, namely, dryness and humidity. Agents are more worthy than patients, therefore they began with agents. And of the agents, one is the principle of generation, namely, heat; the other is the principle of corruption, namely, coldness. But a thing is generated before it is corrupted, therefore they placed Aries at the beginning, which is a hot and dry sign of the nature of fire, which is primarily hot. And they placed Cancer at the end, which is a cold and humid sign of the nature of water, which is primarily cold. And they placed Taurus after Aries, which is a cold and dry sign of the nature of earth, which is primarily dry, because the dryness of earth is suitable for the heat of fire. And they placed the sign of Gemini before Cancer, which is a hot and humid sign of the nature of air, which is primarily humid, and the humidity of air is suitable for the humidity of water. For the clarification of the aforesaid, it is to be understood that in the eighth sphere there are forty-eight images, in which there is agreement among all the ancients, as he said. And in them there are 1022 stars which are called fixed stars and all move with one motion, namely, with the motion of the eighth sphere, about one degree in a hundred years. And the ancients placed them in six orders, so that those that are larger they placed in the first order, and there are eleven. And those that are smaller than these they placed in the second order, and there are 45. And those that are smaller than these they placed in the third order, and there are 208. And those that are smaller than these they placed in the fourth order, and there are 474. And those that are smaller than these they placed in the fifth order, and there are 217. And those that are smaller than these they placed in the sixth order, and there are sixty-three. Of these 48 images, 12 are in the path of the sun, as has been said, and there are 346 stars in them. The names of these images are Aries, Taurus, etc. And there remain 36 images, of which 21 decline from the path of the sun to the north and 15 to the south. Those that decline to the north have 360 of the aforesaid stars. And the names of the images are these: The first is Ursa Minor. The second is Ursa Major. The third is Draco. The fourth is the burning or blazing dog. The fifth is the barking or howling dog.

[Northern and Southern Constellations]
The sixth is the northern crown. The seventh is the kneeling or genuflecting one. The eighth is the falling vulture. The ninth is the hen. The tenth is the seated one upon a seat. The eleventh is Algol, that is, the devil's head. The twelfth is the one holding the reins. The thirteenth is the serpent bearer. The fourteenth is the serpent. The fifteenth is the hunter. The sixteenth is the flying eagle. Another book has the flying vulture. The seventeenth is the dolphin. The eighteenth is the first horse. Another book has the horse's head. The nineteenth is the second horse. Another book has the winged horse. The twentieth is the woman who has not known a man. The twenty-first is the triangle. Those that decline to the south from the aforementioned stars are 216, whose imaginary names are these: The first of these is the sea lion, which some call the bear. The second is Algebar, that is, the strong dog. The third is the river. The fourth is the hare. The fifth is Canis Major. The sixth is Canis Minor. The seventh is Noah's Ark. The eighth is the serpent. The ninth is the vase. The tenth is the comb. The eleventh is the one bearing the lion, and its middle part is of human figure and the other of a horse. The twelfth is the leopard. The thirteenth is the thuribles. The fourteenth is the southern crown. The fifteenth is the southern fish. And six of these signs are thus prayed by the author to the signs in turn. And I divided them into three parts. First, I compare them to the parts of the world, or this to the declinations. Second, I show them to the ascensions. Third, I show them to the qualities. The first is at the beginning. The second is there: and six of them are said to ascend directly. The third is there: and it is called the middle. First, it says that six of the aforementioned 12 signs are northern, because they decline from the equinoctial line towards the northern pole, that is, from the beginning of Aries to the end of Virgo. And the other six, that is, from the beginning of Libra to the end of Pisces, are southern, because they decline from the equinoctial line towards the southern pole. According to this part, it is to be understood that the equinoctial is the circle that the sun describes by the rapture of the firmament, that is, by diurnal motion when it is in the first point of Aries, and it describes the same in the first point of Libra. Therefore, it is called by Ptolemy the equator of day and night, because at that time day and night are of the same length throughout the world where the sun rises and sets. I say this because there are two places in the world above which the sun neither rises nor sets, which is in Aries or Libra, one of which is under the arctic pole and the other under the antarctic pole. Here that question could be moved: whether there is habitation under the equator. It seems not. For where there is perpetual heat, there is no habitation; but under the equator there is perpetual heat. For the sun always runs over that part and declines little from it. Also, the author of the sphere says that there are five zones in the sky, one of which is the torrid zone, that is, according to him, under the equator and from both sides up to the tropics, and two under the poles and two temperate. There he wants three of them to be uninhabitable, namely the torrid zone because of excessive heat, and the two existing under the poles because of excessive cold, and the other two are habitable because they are temperate. Briefly, I believe with Avicenna that there is habitation under the equator, and the best habitation. And briefly I put one reason that moved me. There is the best habitation where there is the greatest temperateness; but under the equator there is the greatest temperateness; therefore, etc. The major is known. I declare the minor: for under the equator day and night are equal, as has been said, and the air can be cooled as much at night as it is heated during the day. Also, the sun's declination varies most there. For the declination changes in one day by 24 minutes, so it can hardly happen that the sun passes directly over their heads, for this does not happen unless the sun enters Aries or Libra directly at noon. Also, the sun never remains at the same altitude above them; but immediately, if there was motion, the altitude would vary in an instant. For as quickly as the prime mover moves, it approaches the meridian and recedes from the meridian. And where great heating is to occur, it is necessary that the rays penetrate for some time, as we see in a burning mirror, if the mirror were moved, it would not ignite straws or anything else that was opposed. Also, cold planets restrain the heat of the hot ones there, because all are always near there, although some say that planets do not cause cold, but their coldness is less heat. In truth, I do not believe this, with all due respect to them. For I have seen that the same cause of cold does not produce as much cold in very northern parts as it does in less northern parts. It could also be proven by reason. If it were so that no planet influenced cold, but lacked heat, it would follow that the presence of Saturn in summer would make summer hot, because such an addition to such makes it more such; but we do not see this, why, etc. And if someone were to say that its lesser heat tempers the greater heat of the sun, like warm water with hot. This is not valid, because there is a material mixture. In celestial influences, however, there is a virtual mixture. And it is to be imagined in influences of greater and lesser heat as of two fires heating a pot, one of which is stronger than the other. It is certain that the lesser fire will not cool the pot nor hinder the stronger fire in its heating. The reasons in opposition are solved: for what says that there is perpetual heat there. I say that there is not perpetual heat there that impedes habitation. I deny the author of the sphere in this matter. And six of them are said to ascend directly. It could be divided, but there is no force. It briefly says that 6 signs from the aforesaid signs ascend directly, and 6 obliquely. They ascend directly from the beginning of Cancer to the end of Sagittarius. The other 6 ascend obliquely. This is from the treatise on the sphere, so it is not to be stood here. Afterwards, it says that the tortuous or obliquely ascending signs obey the directly ascending ones. According to this, it is to be noted that if two are born at certain times in which all other significations are equal as to the superior and also inferior root, but one is born under a directly ascending sign and the other under an obliquely or tortuously ascending sign, the one who was born under the oblique will obey the other who was born under the direct sign, as long as those signs are of the same longitude from the beginning of Cancer. For example: he who was born under Gemini will obey him who was born under Cancer; and he who was under Taurus, him who was under Leo; and he who was under Aries, him who was under Virgo, and so on for the others. Afterwards, it says that any two signs that are of the same longitude from the beginning of Aries are said to be concordant, like Pisces and Aries, Aquarius and Taurus, Capricorn and Gemini, and so on for the others. And it can be applied as before. And this is because the ascensions of those signs are equal. And this is what the author of the treatise on the sphere says: any two signs equally distant from either of the equinoctial points are equal in their ascensions. Afterwards, it says that the half of the circle that is from the beginning of Leo to the end of Capricorn is called the maximum half because of the ascensions. And it is the sun's half: because Leo is the house of the sun and the ascensions begin to increase notably there. And the sun has dignity in that whole half, like the planets in their terms. And the other half is the moon's, that is, from the beginning of Aquarius to the end of Cancer: and that is called the minimum half because the ascensions begin to be notably named there. And the moon has dignity there which the sun has in the maximum. From above.

[The Houses of the Planets]
And it is called the midpoint. That is, it compares the signs to each other as to their qualities in general. And it briefly says that the midpoint from the beginning of Aries to the end of Virgo is the hot midpoint, because it makes summer for us. And the other midpoint is cold, because it makes winter for us. It compares these to the four seasons, and to the four ages, and to the four humors or complexions. And it says that the fourth part, which is from the beginning of Aries to the beginning of Cancer, is hot and humid, like spring and like childhood and like the sanguine complexion. And the other fourth part, which is from the beginning of Cancer to the beginning of Libra, is hot and dry, like summer and like the second age and like the choleric complexion. And the other fourth part, which is from the beginning of Libra to the beginning of Capricorn, is cold and dry, like autumn and like the third age, which is the beginning of diminution, and like the melancholic complexion. And the fourth part, which is from the beginning of Capricorn to the end of Pisces, is cold and humid, like winter and like the last age and the phlegmatic complexion. It arranges the seven planets. It is taken from when a planet is in a sign, and it is clear in the letter. But note here the threefold acceptance of the sign as the author of the sphere states, because you will find it there, I do not put it here. The planets have. The author first determined the division of the circle of signs, and some things that follow that division. Here he wants to determine the dignities of the planets in the signs. And it is divided into two. Because first he determines the essential dignities. Second, the accidental ones. This part is there: and also concerning the accidental planets at the end of this difference. The first part is divided into two: because in the first he does what has been said, that is, he determines the dignities of the planets in the signs. In this part he determines the strengths they have in these dignities. As there: and because now, with God's help. The first part is divided into five parts according to the five dignities: because first he determines the dignity of the planets which is called the house. Second, the dignity which is called exaltation. Third, the dignity which is called triplicity. Fourth, the dignity which is called term. Fifth, the dignity which is called face. As there: these are the exaltations. These are the triplicities, we distinguish them thus. Fourth there: also in each sign. Fifth there: the faces of the signs. The first part can be divided into two parts: because in the first part it shows the houses of the planets. In the second part, each of them, except the Sun and Moon, has two houses, one of which is more principal, and that is called joy, and it shows which are those houses in which they rejoice. As there: the signs in which. The first is divided into two. First it sets out to determine the dignities of the planets and sets out the division in the letter. Second, it follows there: these are the houses. It says that the planets have in the aforesaid signs certain dignities or powers by nature and certain by accident. Those that are by nature are house, exaltation, triplicity, term, and face. But concerning these dignities which they have by accident, he will speak later. These are the houses. It says that Aries and Scorpio are the houses of Mars, and Virgo is the house of Mercury: Cancer is the house of the Moon: Leo is the house of the Sun: Sagittarius and Pisces are the houses of Jupiter: Capricorn and Aquarius are the houses of Saturn. Afterwards it says that the seventh sign from the house of any planet is called its detriment: for example, just as Leo is the house of the Sun, so Aquarius, which is the sign opposite to Leo, is the detriment of the Sun: and understand the same for the others. Then it says that the two signs which are the house of one planet are in agreement in the girdle, that is, in the circle of signs or the zodiac, which is wide in the middle and narrow at the poles. To understand this, it is necessary to imagine circles passing through the beginnings of the signs and through the poles of the zodiac, and the entire space comprehended between any two circles is one sign, as was exemplified in the preceding lecture. This agreement seems to me to do little to explain why two signs should be the house of one planet, because any two signs agree in that way. Therefore, the author's words can be explained or glossed differently, that any two signs which are the house of one planet agree in the zodiac as to their distance from the houses of the luminaries: and in that way it is true: for example, Gemini and Virgo are the houses of Mercury, and they are equally distant from Leo and Cancer, which are the houses of the luminaries, and Taurus and Libra, which are the houses of Venus, are equally distant from Leo and Cancer. And you will find this agreement in all. Ptolemy assigns the reason why Leo is the house of the Sun and Cancer is the house of the Moon, and similarly for the others in the 173rd proposition and the following 7th and 6th propositions of the first part concerning the houses of the luminaries, the Sun and Moon. He says that the two northern signs which are closer to our zenith, and for this reason cause heat, which are Cancer and Leo, were placed as the houses of the two great and noble luminaries. Leo, because it is masculine, is the house of the Sun, and Cancer, because it is feminine, is the house of the Moon. Others say in the commentary, explaining the aforesaid words, that the two northern signs are Cancer and Gemini: but Gemini is a hot and humid sign. Therefore it does not agree with any of them. In that it moistens, it does not agree with the Sun, which heats and dries: nor with the Moon, which is feminine and nocturnal. But the sign of Gemini is masculine and diurnal. But Leo agrees with the Sun, which is a hot and dry sign. Therefore it is fitting that Leo should be the house of the Sun, and because the Moon follows the Sun, therefore it is fitting that the house of the Moon should be near the house of the Sun. Then someone might say, why then is Virgo not the house of the Moon, since it is near Leo, which is the house of the Sun? Balinus says that the sign of Virgo is not suitable for the Moon: because Virgo is a dry sign, but the Moon is humid. And for this reason they placed Cancer, which is humid, as the house of the Moon. For the houses of the other planets, he assigns two reasons: one is taken from the order of the planets and signs. The other from the aspects. Briefly, to conclude his intention in a few words, he wants to say that Capricorn and Aquarius are the houses of Saturn, because these two signs are most distant from the houses of the luminaries, and Saturn is superior to all planets. And Sagittarius and Pisces are the houses of Jupiter: because these two signs are next to the houses of Saturn: just as Jupiter is below Saturn. Scorpio and Aries are the houses of Mars: because they are next to the houses of Jupiter, just as Mars is below Jupiter. Libra and Taurus are the houses of Venus for the same reason. And Virgo and Gemini are the houses of Mercury. And if you start the order from the inferior, you will find the same: for example, Virgo and Gemini are next to the houses of the luminaries and are the houses of Mercury: because Mercury follows the Moon in order: and so for the others. The other reason he assigns is taken from the aspects, and he wants to say that Saturn is greater in fortune: therefore his houses should be distant from the houses of the luminaries by an opposing aspect.

[Planetary Houses and Exaltations]
which is an aspect of perfect enmity. In this way, Capricorn and Aquarius are distant. For Capricorn is in opposition to the Moon's domicile, namely Cancer, and Aquarius is in opposition to the Sun's domicile, namely Leo. And Jupiter is the greater fortune; its domicile should be distant from the luminaries' domiciles by a trine aspect, that is, an aspect of perfect friendship. In this way, Sagittarius and Pisces are distant: for Sagittarius aspects Leo with a trine aspect, and Pisces aspects Cancer. And Mars is the lesser fortune; its domicile should be distant from the luminaries' domiciles by a square aspect, which is an aspect of medium enmity. In this way, Scorpio and Aries are distant: for Scorpio aspects Leo with a square aspect, and Aries aspects Cancer. Venus is the lesser fortune; its domicile should be distant from the luminaries' domiciles by a sextile aspect, which is an aspect of medium friendship. In this way, Libra and Taurus are distant: for Libra aspects Leo with a sextile aspect, and Taurus aspects Cancer. And the two remaining signs are left for Mercury, namely Virgo and Gemini, which are near the domiciles of the luminaries, because Mercury can never be more than one sign distant from the Sun; indeed, according to the equations of the Alfonsine Tables, it cannot be more than 28 degrees and 7 minutes distant from the Sun. The dignities in which each of the five planets has domiciles show which is the principal domicile of each of them. It says that Saturn rejoices in Aquarius, Jupiter in Sagittarius, Mars in Scorpio, Venus in Taurus, Mercury in Virgo. These are the exaltations. It says the Sun is exalted in the 19th degree of Aries, etc. The text is clear. Ptolemy assigns the exaltations of the planets in the 19th proposition of the first part of the Quadripartitum and in the 6th following. He wants to say that the 19th degree of Aries is the exaltation of the Sun because when the Sun enters Aries, the days begin to increase over the nights, and its heat begins to appear more there. And Libra is its fall, because there the nights begin to increase over the days, and the heat begins to diminish there. And because Saturn is opposite to the Sun, because where heat increases, cold diminishes, and vice versa, therefore Libra is the exaltation of Saturn, and Aries is its fall. And when the Moon conjoins the Sun in Aries, its light first begins to appear in Taurus; therefore Taurus is the exaltation of the Moon, and Scorpio is its fall, because it is the opposite sign. And because Jupiter causes northern winds, and Cancer is a northern sign, therefore Cancer is the exaltation of Jupiter, and the opposite sign, namely Capricorn, is its fall. And because Mars is naturally scorching, and especially when it is in Capricorn, it burns much more, as it inclines to the southern part, therefore Capricorn is its exaltation, and it is the sign opposite to Jupiter's exaltation, and Cancer is its fall. And because Venus naturally humidifies, and especially when it is in Pisces, Pisces is the exaltation of Venus, and the opposite sign, namely Virgo, is its fall. And because Mercury dries by itself, and in this is contrary to Venus, therefore Virgo is its exaltation, which is the sign opposite to Venus's exaltation, and Pisces is its fall. Albumazar assigns almost the same causes, although he uses different words, and he received them from Ptolemy; therefore, let these suffice concerning the causes of domiciles and exaltations. First, the author determined concerning the domiciles and exaltations of the planets. Here he determines concerning the triplicities. And because aspects accompany triplicities, he therefore determines subsequently concerning the aspects of the signs. And according to this, this part can be divided into two parts. In the first, he determines concerning the triplicities. In the second, concerning the aspects, there, "secondly, the signs are said to aspect each other." The first part can be divided into two. In the first, he does what has been said. In the second, he shows which signs are movable, which fixed, and which common. The second part begins there: "four of these signs." The first part is divided into four parts according to the four triplicities. The second part begins there: "triplicity." The third part begins there: "triplicity." The fourth part begins there: "fourth triplicity." The first part is divided into two. In the first, he determines concerning the triplicities in general. In the second, in particular. The first part begins at the beginning. The second part begins there: "Aries, Leo, and Sagittarius." He says first that all three signs that are of the same nature make one triplicity.
