Afterwards, he says that Aries, Leo, and Sagittarius make the first triplicity, because these three signs are of the same nature, namely fiery, masculine, diurnal, choleric, hot and dry, bitter in taste, and these three signs are oriental. And this triplicity, like any of the others, has three lords who are called the lords of the triplicity. The first lord of this triplicity in nativities or questions or any other matters that occur during the day is the Sun. The second is Jupiter. The third is Saturn. In matters that occur at night, the first lord of this triplicity is Jupiter. The second is the Sun. The third is Saturn. It should be noted here what Albumazar says in his introduction, that the first sign of this triplicity, namely Aries, produces temperate heat. The second, namely Leo, produces scorching heat. The third, namely Sagittarius, produces corrupting heat. When any of these signs falls in the ascendant of a conjunction or opposition of the Sun and Moon in winter, the cold is tempered. In summer, there is excessive heat, especially if the lord of that sign is present in that sign or in any of the angles aspecting the ascendant. Afterwards, he says that Taurus, Virgo, and Capricorn make the second triplicity because they are of the same nature, for all three are feminine, nocturnal, earthy, cold and dry, melancholic, sour in taste, southern. The lords of this triplicity during the day are: first Venus, then the Moon, then Mars. And at night: the Moon first, then Venus, then Mars. Albumazar says that the first sign of this triplicity produces temperate cold, strengthening animals and crops. The second produces harmful cold. The third produces corrupting cold. When any of these signs falls in the ascendant of a conjunction or opposition of the Sun and Moon in winter, and especially Capricorn, there is great cold, especially if Saturn is in that triplicity. Then he says that Gemini, Libra, and Aquarius make the third triplicity because they are of the same nature: for they are masculine, diurnal, sanguine, hot and humid, airy, western, sweet in taste. Their lords during the day are: first Saturn, second Mercury, third Jupiter. At night: first Mercury, second Saturn, third Jupiter. And Albumazar says that the first sign of this triplicity produces temperate, strengthening, and sweet winds. The second produces harmful winds. The third produces winds that dissipate animals and crops. When any of these is the ascendant at the hour of the conjunction of the Sun and Moon, winds move in that lunation. And similarly understand this concerning the opposition. Afterwards, he says that Cancer, Scorpio, and Pisces make the fourth triplicity because all three are feminine, nocturnal, northern, watery, cold and humid, salty in taste. Their lords during the day are: first Venus, second Mars, third the Moon. At night: first Mars, second Venus, third the Moon. Albumazar says that the first sign of this triplicity

[Rainfall Prediction from Conjunctions and Oppositions]
makes for temperate humidity. Secondly, abundant. Thirdly, destructive. When any of these signs are in the ascendant of a conjunction or opposition of the Sun and Moon, rain is to be expected in that month. For from this triplicity, and from Venus and the Moon, rains especially begin. Abraham Avenezra says that if, in the conjunction or opposition preceding the Sun's entry into Aries, whether it be a conjunction or opposition, any of these signs is ascending, and with this the luminaries are in the angles (i.e., in the ascendant, or midheaven, or in the occident, or in the angle of midnight), there will be excessive rain in that year. But if the luminaries are cadent from the angles, rain will not fall in that month and for the greater part of that year. And I have experienced many times that when the ascendant of the conjunction is a watery sign, and the Moon enters that sign before the opposition, on the same day that the Moon enters the degree that was in the ascendant, rain begins and lasts at least as long as the Moon remains in that sign. And in a similar way, you should understand this for windy and cold signs. I found this by experience, but afterwards I found this in the book of Abraham Avenezra, and I rejoiced greatly because I was more certain of the truth. But Abraham says that it is especially true if the ascending sign is one of the angles of the figure of that land. I understand this concerning the figure of the revolution of that year in that land. For it varies according to different regions. And if it is not one of the angles of the figure of that land, there will be clouds without rain. These triplicities are almost the same as the causes of the houses, which I pass over. Four of these signs are also called bicorporeal, and there are movable, fixed, and common signs. And it assigns them and gives examples. The letter is plain. It should be noted here that Ptolemy says in the 22nd proposition of the Centiloquium: 'To make or use new clothes when the Moon is in Leo is to be feared.' And Paulus says in his commentary on the same proposition that all fixed signs are prohibited for this, and especially Leo, which, besides being fixed, is a sign of great victories and signifies the victory of all kings who exercise and have bad dominion over them. And he says that to 'make' Ptolemy intends to cut and sew. By 'use' he intends to wear and utilize. From this we can derive a rule that all things we wish to be fixed we should begin when the Moon is in a fixed sign, such as building houses and so on. And things we wish to change quickly we should begin when the Moon is in a movable sign, such as traveling and so on. Now the signs aspect each other. The author has determined concerning the dignity of the planets, which he calls triplicities. And because triplicity is taken from a trine aspect, therefore in this incidental part he determines concerning aspects, and it can be divided into two parts: in the first part he determines concerning aspects. In this part, concerning the projections of rays. The second part begins there: 'When a planet is in any sign.' The first part can be divided into four parts according to the four aspects. In the first, he determines concerning the sextile aspect. In the second part, concerning the square aspect. In the third, concerning the trine. In the fourth, concerning the opposition. The second part begins there: 'and it aspects the square before it.' The third part there: 'it also aspects the trine before it.' The fourth part there: 'it also aspects the seventh.' He says first that the signs aspect each other in this way: Every sign aspects the third sign after it and the third sign before it, just as Aries aspects the sign of Gemini, which is the third before it, and the sign of Aquarius, which is the third after it. And this aspect is called sextile because it holds the sixth part of the circle, i.e., 60 degrees, which is the quantity of two signs, and this aspect is called an aspect of medium friendship, and it can be the reason why any two signs distant in this way agree in one quality and with this in sex. For example, Aries and Gemini agree in heat and masculinity, and similarly Aries and Aquarius. Taurus and Cancer agree in coldness and femininity, and similarly Taurus and Pisces, and so you should understand for all. Afterwards he says that every sign aspects the fourth before it and the fourth after it, and this aspect is called tetragon or square because it holds the fourth part of the circle, i.e., 90 degrees, which is the quantity of three signs. And this aspect is called an aspect of medium enmity, because any two signs distant in this way sometimes disagree in one quality, sometimes in both; they also disagree in sex, for if one of them is masculine, the other will be feminine. And this is the reason why in acute diseases, for the most part, a crisis occurs when the Moon comes to the fourth aspect of the place where it was at the beginning of the disease, especially if there is a disagreement in both qualities; and commonly then a salutary crisis occurs. For example, if the Moon was at the beginning of the illness in any of the signs of the fiery triplicity, especially in Aries, when it comes to the fourth sign, which disagrees in both qualities and in sex, commonly a crisis occurs for health, just as if it was in Aries, the fourth aspect will be in Cancer; if in Leo, the fourth aspect will be in Scorpio; if in Sagittarius, the fourth aspect will be in Pisces. In other signs, however, there is no disagreement except in one quality and in sex. For example: Taurus and Leo: Taurus is a cold and dry feminine sign. Leo is a hot and dry masculine sign. And you will find this disagreement in others in their own way. And because of this, crises in these signs sometimes occur for health and sometimes for death, according to the fortunate or unfortunate aspect to the Moon. Then he says that every sign aspects the fifth before it and the fifth after it, and this aspect is called trine because it holds the third part of the circle, i.e., 120 degrees. And this aspect is called an aspect of perfect friendship, because any three signs distant in this way form one triplicity and agree in natures, as was said in the immediately preceding chapter. Afterwards he says: every sign also aspects the seventh from itself, i.e., the opposite sign; and this is an aspect of perfect enmity by reason of opposition. And every planet that is in any degree of any sign aspects a planet existing in another sign in a similar degree with the same aspect with which those two signs aspect each other. And the author speaks of 30 degrees of the zodiac; but according to Ptolemy's doctrine, aspects are taken in the equinoctial; therefore the letter can be glossed in this way. And this is to be understood of the degrees of the equinoctial. For example: if any planet is in Aries and another in Gemini, and the ascensions of the direct circle of the one in Aries have been subtracted from the ascensions of the direct circle of the one in Gemini, if 60 degrees remain, they aspect each other with a sextile aspect. In this way, understand for other aspects. In this, the author, 'when a planet is,' briefly explains himself by saying: If any planet is in any sign, it projects its rays in a similar degree of the sign that aspects it with some aspect. For example: if any planet is in the first degree of Aries and in the second minute, it projects its sextile rays to the first degree of Gemini in its second minute. The author was too brief in this chapter, therefore it is necessary to dwell a little on the explanation of aspects and the projection of rays. It must first be understood that aspects are considered in three ways. In one way, according to equal degrees, and according to this mode the author in the text spoke of aspects and their projection.

[Three Ways of Considering Aspects]
There are three ways of considering aspects and the projection of rays. One way is to consider aspects and the projection of rays according to the degrees of the zodiacal circle, that is, by computing the degrees of the zodiac that are between one planet and another. This is the method that the author presents in his book, and Abraham ibn Ezra also holds this method. He says that it has been proven almost infinitely that aspects should be taken in the zodiac and not in the equinoctial, and this method is very easy. It has been sufficiently exemplified in the letter. The second way is to consider aspects in the equinoctial ascensions of the direct circle, according to which Ptolemy instructs to take them, as was said above in the letter. If, therefore, you wish to equate aspects according to this method, seek the ascensions of the planet in the direct circle, which begin from Capricorn, and keep them. Then, in the same way, seek the ascensions of the degree of the other planet in the same direct circle, and keep them. Then subtract the ascensions of the one that is closer to Capricorn according to the order of the signs from the ascensions of the one that is farther away. If 60 degrees remain, they aspect each other with a sextile aspect. If 90 degrees remain, they aspect each other with a quartile aspect. And if 120 degrees remain, they aspect each other with a trine aspect. For an opposition aspect, however, it is not necessary to seek ascensions, because two planets that are opposite in the zodiac are also opposite in the equinoctial. This method is easy, therefore it is not necessary to dwell much on it here. The third method of aspects and the projection of rays is very difficult, especially for those not practiced in calculations. It must first be understood concerning this method that the projection of rays is taken according to the ascensions of the direct circle if the planet whose rays we wish to project is in the midheaven or in the angle of the earth. And if it is in the degree of the ascendant or in the degree of the descendant, it is taken according to the ascensions of the region or horizon, using tables made for that region. If, however, the planet is not in any of these four places, but in intermediate places, then the radiations are taken mixed. Therefore, when you wish to project rays to a planet, consider if the planet whose rays you wish to project is in the midheaven or in the angle of the earth. Then seek the ascensions of that degree in the direct circle. To these, add 60 degrees if you want a left sextile radiation, that which precedes according to the order of the signs from the place of the planet. And reduce the degrees obtained after the addition to equal degrees in the direct circle according to the doctrine of the canons of the primum mobile. The zodiacal degree that results in that place is the sextile ray. And just as I said 60 degrees for the sextile radiation, so understand 90 for the quartile radiation and 120 for the trine radiation. If, however, you want right radiations, that is, those that precede from the place of the planet towards the west, subtract from the ascensions of the planet's degree 60 degrees for the sextile radiation, or 90 for the quartile radiation, or 120 for the trine radiation. And reduce the remaining number to equal degrees as before, and the zodiacal degree that results in that place is the ray. For example, in a left radiation, I assume that Saturn is in the angle of the midheaven at the end of the sixth degree of Virgo. The ascensions of that degree in the direct circle are 247 degrees and 48 minutes. I want to have a sextile radiation, so I add 60 degrees, which gives 307 degrees and 48 minutes. I reduce these to equal degrees in the direct circle, and they result in 10 degrees, 14 minutes, and 14 seconds of Scorpio. There are the left sextile rays of Saturn in this case. For example, in a right sextile radiation, I subtract 60 degrees from the aforementioned ascensions, and 187 degrees and 48 minutes remain. I reduce these to equal degrees in the direct circle, and they result in 7 degrees, 9 minutes, and 15 seconds of Cancer. There, therefore, are the right sextile rays of Saturn. If, however, the planet whose rays you wish to project is in the degree of the ascendant, seek the ascensions of the planet's degree from the table of ascensions of the oblique circle serving your region. And if you want a left radiation, add to the ascensions of the planet's degree 60 degrees for a sextile radiation, or 90 for a quartile radiation, or 120 for a trine radiation. For example, in a left sextile radiation, I assume that Jupiter is in the degree of the ascendant at the end of the 10th degree of Sagittarius. The ascensions of that degree in the oblique horizon are 275 degrees and 27 minutes. I want to have a left sextile radiation, so I add 60 degrees to them, and 335 degrees and 27 minutes result. I reduce these to equal degrees in the oblique circle, and they result in 12 degrees, 44 minutes, and 21 seconds of Aquarius. There, therefore, are the sextile rays of Jupiter. For example, in a right sextile radiation, I subtract 60 degrees from the ascensions of Jupiter's degree, and 215 degrees and 27 minutes remain. I reduce these to equal degrees, and they result in 25 degrees, 54 minutes, and 50 seconds of Libra. There are the sextile rays of Jupiter. If, however, the planet is in the degree of the descendant, you will work with the opposite degree. That is, you will take the ascensions of the nadir of the planet's degree in the oblique horizon and proceed in the same way as before. But after you have reduced to equal degrees, the place of the ray is the place opposite to the place you find. And to make it clearer, I will give an example. I assume that Jupiter is in the degree of the descendant at the end of the 10th degree of Sagittarius. I seek the ascensions of the 10th degree of Gemini and find 41 degrees and 9 minutes. I add 60 degrees for a sextile radiation, and 101 degrees and 9 minutes result. I reduce these to equal degrees in the oblique horizon, and they result in 2 degrees, 30 minutes, and 45 seconds of Leo. Therefore, the rays are in the opposite of this, that is, 2 degrees, 30 minutes, and 45 seconds of Aquarius. If, however, the planet whose rays you wish to project is not in any of the aforementioned places, then it is necessary to take the radiations in a mixed way, according to the proportion of the distance of the planet's degree between one angle and another. The method is this: if the planet whose rays you wish to project is between the midheaven and the ascendant degree, first take the ascensions of the midheaven degree. Then subtract from the ascensions of the planet's degree in the direct circle, and what remains is the distance from the midheaven, which you keep. Then, to the ascensions of the planet's degree in the direct circle, add 60 degrees for a sextile radiation, or 90 for a quartile radiation, or 120 for a trine radiation. And reduce what results to equal degrees in the direct circle, and what results, keep and call it the radiation of the direct circle. Then seek the ascensions of the planet's degree in the oblique horizon using the table of your region. To these, add 60 degrees for a sextile radiation, or 90 for a quartile radiation, or 120 for a trine radiation. And reduce what results to equal degrees using the tables of your region, and what results, keep and call it the radiation of the region. Then see the difference between the radiation of the direct circle and the radiation of the region. Multiply this difference by the distance of the planet's degree from the midheaven.

[Calculating Planetary Rays]
Divide the product by half the arc of the planet's diurnal degree. The proportional part will be obtained, which you add to the radiation of the direct circle. If the radiation of the direct circle is less than the radiation of the region, subtract it from itself if it is greater. What results will be the place of the rays. You will find half the arc of the planet's diurnal degree by subtracting the ascensions of the planet's degree in the oblique circle from the ascensions of its nadir and halving that. It could also be found in another way, the proportional part of the two radiations, namely, by taking a sixth part of the day and multiplying it by the hours of the planet's distance from the midheaven. But this method is more tedious than the first, because according to this method, it is necessary to divide the distance of the planet's degree from the meridian by the parts of the hours of the planet's degree to find the hours of distance from the meridian. I advise the first method. I give an example in this: let the degree of the midheaven be 20 degrees of Leo completed, and Saturn be in the sixth degree of Virgo completed. I seek the distance of Saturn from the midheaven by the ascensions of the direct circle. And I find the distance to be 15 degrees, 22 minutes. I will keep this. Then I subtract the ascensions of Saturn's degree in the oblique circle from the ascensions of the opposite degree. And there remain 201 degrees, 20 minutes, which is the entire diurnal arc of Saturn, which I will divide in half. And 100 degrees, 40 minutes result, which is half the diurnal arc of Saturn; I will keep this. Then I seek the ascensions of Saturn's degree in the direct circle, and I find 247 degrees, 48 minutes, to which I add 60 degrees, because I want the sextile sinister radiation. And 307 degrees, 48 minutes will result, which I reduce to equal degrees in the direct circle, and I find 10 degrees, 14 minutes, 14 seconds of Scorpio. And this is the radiation of the direct circle. Then I seek the ascensions of Saturn's degree in the oblique circle in the region whose latitude is 48 degrees. And I find 147 degrees, 11 minutes, to which I add 60 degrees, and 207 degrees, 11 minutes result, which I reduce to equal degrees in the oblique circle, and I find 19 degrees, 52 minutes, 14 seconds of Libra. I see that the radiation of the direct circle is greater than the radiation of the region. I subtract the smaller from the larger, and I find in the difference 20 degrees, 22 minutes, which I reduce to the same kind; and 1222 result. I also reduce the distance of Saturn from the midheaven to the same kind. The distance was 15 degrees, 22 minutes, reduced to the same kind, 920 minutes. I will multiply the difference by the distance, and 26684 seconds result. Then I reduce half the diurnal arc of Saturn to the same kind. Half the diurnal arc was 100 degrees, 40 minutes, reduced to the same kind, 6040 minutes, by which I divide the number that resulted from the multiplication. And three degrees, 6 minutes, 32 seconds will result, which I subtract from the radiation of the direct circle, because that was greater, and there remain seven degrees, 7 minutes, 42 seconds of Scorpio. There are the sinister sextile rays of Saturn in the proposed case. If, however, I wanted the dexter radiation, where I instructed to add 60 degrees, I would subtract 60, and proceed as before. If, however, the degree of the planet whose rays you wish to project is between the ascending degree and the angle of the earth, see its longitude from the ascending degree, which you will know in this way: Subtract the ascensions of the ascending degree in the oblique circle from the ascensions of the planet's degree in the same oblique circle. And if you want the sinister radiation, what remains will be the distance of the planet from the ascending degree. Then seek half the nocturnal arc of the planet's degree, which you will know in this way: Subtract the ascensions of the planet's nadir degree from the ascensions of the planet's degree, and the entire nocturnal arc will remain, which you halve. Having observed these things, seek the ascensions of the planet's degree in the oblique circle by a table made for the latitude of your region, to which add 60 for the sextile radiation. And what results, reduce to equal degrees in the oblique circle, and let it be called the radiation of the oblique circle. Then seek the ascensions of the planet's degree in the direct circle, to which add 60 degrees for the sextile radiation and the others, and what results, reduce to equal degrees in the direct circle, and keep what results, and let it be called the radiation of the direct circle. Then see the difference between the radiation of the region and the direct circle, by subtracting the smaller from the larger; multiply this difference by the distance of the planet from the ascending degree. And divide the product by half the nocturnal arc of the planet's degree, and the proportional part will emerge, which you add to the radiation of the region if it is less than the radiation of the direct circle, or subtract from the radiation of the region if it is greater than the radiation of the direct circle. And what results after addition or subtraction will be the place of the rays. I give an example in this: let the ascending degree be 18 Scorpio, Jupiter be in 10 Sagittarius. I seek the ascensions of the ascending degree in the horizon of 48 degrees, and I find 245 degrees, 55 minutes. Then I seek the ascensions of Jupiter's degree in the same oblique horizon, and I find 275 degrees, 27 minutes. I subtract the ascensions of the ascending degree from the ascensions of Jupiter's degree, and there remain 29 degrees, 32 minutes, which is the distance of Jupiter from the ascendant. Then I subtracted the ascensions of Jupiter's opposite degree from the ascensions of Jupiter's degree, and I halved the remainder, and I found 117 degrees, 9 minutes, which is half the nocturnal arc of Jupiter's degree. Then I added 60 degrees to Jupiter's ascensions, and 335 degrees, 27 minutes resulted, which I reduced to equal degrees in the oblique circle, and I found 12 degrees, 45 minutes of Aquarius. And this is the radiation of the region; so I kept it. Then I sought the ascensions of Jupiter's degree in the direct circle, and I found 338 degrees, 21 minutes, to which I added 60 degrees, and 398 degrees, 21 minutes resulted. I subtracted one revolution, i.e., 360 degrees, and 38 degrees, 21 minutes remained, which I reduced to equal degrees in the direct circle, and I found 50 degrees, 57 minutes of Aquarius; and this is the radiation of the direct circle. Then I subtracted the smaller radiation from the larger, and I found in the difference 6 degrees, 48 minutes, which difference I multiplied by the distance of Jupiter from the ascendant, and I divided by half the nocturnal arc, and I found in the proportional part 1 degree, 42 minutes, 47 seconds, which I subtracted from the radiation of the region, because that was greater. And after subtraction, there remained 11 degrees, 2 minutes, 13 seconds of Aquarius; and there is the place of Jupiter's rays. If, however, you wished to project the rays to the right, then you should see the distance of the planet's degree from the angle of the earth by the ascensions of the direct circle, which you will find by subtracting the ascensions of the planet's degree in the direct circle from the ascensions of the angle of the earth in the direct circle. And then you should add the proportional part of the two radiations to the radiation of the direct circle if it were less than the radiation of the region, or subtract if it were greater. In no other way does the operation differ, except where I instructed to add 60 degrees to the ascensions, etc., and to subtract 60, etc. If, however, the degree of the planet whose rays you wish to project is between the occidental degree and the degree of the 10th house, you will proceed with the opposite degree of the planet directly by the same way, as I have already said between the ascendant and the angle of the earth. For when the planet's degree is between the occidental degree and the midheaven, its opposite is between the ascendant and the angle of the earth.

[Calculating Planetary Rays Beyond the Angle]
The degree is between the ascendant and the angle of the earth. And the degree opposite the planet is as far from the ascendant as the degree of the planet is from the degree of the occident: that is the same operation: neither more nor less. But after you have completed the operations, the place of the rays is the place opposite to that place which you found, as I exemplified to you: when the planet is in the degree of the occident. But if it happens, as it often happens, that the degree of the planet is before the angle: the place where its rays fall is beyond the angle: as where the degree of the planet is between the midheaven and the ascendant and the rays fall beyond the ascendant, that is, between the ascendant and the angle of the earth. This case occurs almost frequently in trine radiation: and often in quartile: and sometimes in sextile. The method is this: if the place of the planet whose rays you wish to project is between the midheaven and the ascendant and its rays should fall beyond the ascendant: see the distance of the planet from the midheaven by the method previously described: and see half the diurnal arc of the planet's degree by the method previously described and keep both, that is, the distance and half the diurnal arc. Then find the ascensions of the planet's degree in the direct circle. Also find the ascensions of the ascendant's degree in the same direct circle. Then subtract the ascensions of the planet's degree from the ascensions of the ascendant's degree. And what remains, keep: and let it be called the part of the radiation of the direct circle. Then find the ascensions of the planet's degree in the oblique circle. And find the ascensions of the ascendant's degree in the oblique circle: and subtract the ascensions of the planet from the ascensions of the ascendant's degree: and what remains, keep and let it be called the part of the radiation of the region. Then subtract the smaller part of the radiation from the larger and the difference remains, which multiply by the distance of the planet from the midheaven and divide the product by half the diurnal arc of the planet's degree and a proportional part will result, which add to the part of the radiation of the direct circle if it is smaller than the part of the radiation of the region. Or subtract if it is larger: and what results will be the equated part of the radiation: which if it is less than 60 degrees, the sextile rays fall beyond the angle; if it is greater, they fall before the angle. And if this part is less than 90 degrees, the quartile rays fall beyond the angle; if greater, they fall before the angle. And if this part is less than 120 degrees, as is almost frequently the case, the trine rays fall beyond the angle; if it is greater than 120, they fall before the angle. If therefore the rays fall beyond the angle, subtract the equated part of the radiation from 60 degrees for sextile radiation, or from 90 for quartile radiation: or from 120 for trine radiation: and what remains, add to the ascensions of the ascendant's degree in the oblique circle and what results, reduce to equal degrees in the oblique circle and the degree of the sign that comes out will be the place of the rays. If you know this operation, you will know how to direct a planet existing in one quadrant to a place existing in another quadrant. I have not seen this method explained or placed in any book. So that what I have said may be clearer, I will put it in this example. I assume that the degree of the midheaven is 10 degrees Cancer and Saturn is in the fourth degree of Virgo: and the ascendant's degree in the oblique horizon in a region whose latitude is 48 degrees is 7 degrees 59 minutes Libra. I sought the ascensions of the midheaven's degree in the direct circle and found 190 degrees 53 minutes. Then I sought the ascensions of Saturn's degree in the direct circle and found 245 degrees 55 minutes. I subtracted the ascensions of the midheaven from the ascensions of Saturn's degree and 55 degrees 2 minutes remained: this is the distance of Saturn from the midheaven. Then I subtracted the ascensions of Saturn's degree in the oblique circle from the ascensions of the opposite degree in the same oblique circle and 203 degrees 3 minutes remained: and this was the diurnal arc of Saturn's degree which I bisected and found 101 degrees 31 minutes 30 seconds, which is half the diurnal arc of Saturn's degree. I subtracted the ascensions of Saturn's degree in the direct circle which were 245 degrees 55 minutes from the ascensions of the ascendant's degree in the same direct circle which were 277 degrees 19 minutes and 31 degrees 24 minutes remained which was the part of the radiation of the direct circle. Then I subtracted the ascensions of Saturn's degree in the oblique circle which were 144 degrees 277 minutes from the ascensions of the ascendant's degree in the same oblique circle which were 190 degrees 53 minutes: and 46 degrees 26 minutes remained which was the part of the radiation of the region or oblique circle: I saw that the part of the radiation of the oblique circle was greater than the part of the radiation of the direct circle. I therefore subtracted the smaller from the larger and 15 degrees 2 minutes remained which was the difference of the two parts which I multiplied by the distance of Saturn from the midheaven and divided by half the diurnal arc of Saturn's degree. And 8 degrees 8 minutes 59 seconds resulted and this was the proportional part of the difference which I added to the part of the radiation of the direct circle and 39 degrees 32 minutes 59 seconds resulted. These are the degrees of ascensions which were in the figure from Saturn to the ascendant's degree: and because they were less than 60, I knew that the sextile rays of Saturn in this figure fell beyond the ascendant's degree. I therefore subtracted these degrees from 60 for sextile radiation and 20 degrees 27 minutes 1 second remained: which I added to the ascensions of the ascendant's degree in the oblique circle which were 190 degrees 53 minutes: and 211 degrees 20 minutes resulted which I reduced to equal degrees in the oblique circle and found 22 degrees 54 minutes 52 seconds Libra: there were the sextile rays of Saturn in the proposed example. This method should be used for other angles. And let this suffice concerning radiations. Also, the five planets have terms in each sign. He has finished with the three essential dignities of the planets. In this part, the author determines the fourth essential dignity which the planets have in the signs. And he divides it into two parts: because in the first part he places the terms of the planets. In the second part he resolves a certain controversy which exists among some concerning triplicities and terms. The second part begins there. Some propose. The first part can be divided into two parts: so that first he begins to treat of the terms of the planets generally. Secondly, he places a table of these terms. The second part begins there because of the diversity of the same. First, he says that the planets, that is, Saturn, Jupiter, Mars, Venus, and Mercury have terms arranged by different degrees. And the first term of Jupiter is from the beginning of Aries up to the end of the sixth degree of the same. And from the beginning of the seventh degree of the same Aries up to the end of the 12th is the term of Venus. And from the beginning of the 13th degree up to the end of the 20th is the term of Mercury. And from the beginning of the 21st up to the end of the 25th is the term of Mars. And from the beginning of the 26th up to the end of Aries is the term of Saturn. Afterwards he says: and these degrees are diverse: so that they do not proceed equally nor according to the order of the planets, it would be difficult to keep them in memory: therefore he placed them in a table as appears in the text. e iij

[Triplicities and Terms]
Some prefer triplicities to terms, which resolves the controversy among the wise regarding triplicities and terms. And it says that some prefer triplicities to terms, and some prefer terms to triplicities. This controversy is resolved by saying that the lords of triplicities are stronger as regards the nourishment of children, because in nativities they signify nourishment, and from them is taken the signification of whether the child will be vital or not. The lords of the terms, however, are stronger in direction, because when the ascending degree of any nativity is directed, it is directed to the terms of fortunes and misfortunes. And the lord of that term is called the divider or disposer of the order as long as the direction endures in that term; and if there is any planet or its rays there, it will be a participant. More will be said about this in the following, not preceding. It should be noted here concerning the terms that there was disagreement among the ancient wise men about the terms. And there were three famous opinions about the terms, one of which was of the Indians, another of the Egyptians, and the third of the Chaldeans. Ptolemy, in the 218th proposition of the first part of the Quadripartite, more approves the terms of the Egyptians and says that he found an old book of terms which, due to its age, was for the most part made. And that agreed with the terms of the Egyptians; and in that book, the sum of the degrees of the terms of each planet was as great as the number of its greater years which they give in nativities. For example: the greater years of Saturn are 57 years, of Jupiter 79, of Mars 66, of Venus 82, of Mercury 76. And all these collected make 360. If you wish to experience this, compute the degrees of all the terms of any planet, for example, Jupiter, and you will find the number of its years, namely 79. And so for the others. Daly, in the commentary on the 206th proposition of the first part of the Quadripartite, says: Those of Egypt were wise magicians who were from ancient times, for these were of great study and exercise in all sciences and wisdoms by which man could be helped. And we know this through the chronicles of the ancient wise men, according to what they spoke of them, and through what remains of their works for many thousands of years up to the present day. I therefore say what I saw from an experience that I found in a place called the eye of the sun, because in a short time I saw great miracles. These are the words of Paly. But he is silent about the experience. In the Centiloquium, in the commentary on that proposition, 'the face of this age,' he mentions an experience of a scorpion seal made in stone, as can be seen there; and whoever wishes to see it, let him see it there. And the faces of the signs. Here he determines concerning the dignity and the ultimate essential that a planet has in the signs, which is called faces. And it can be divided into three parts: because in the first part he places the division and ordering of the faces. In the second part he teaches how to find the faces by numbers. In the third part he places a table for them. The second part begins: 'When you have a degree in any sign.' The third is at the end where he places the table. He says that every sign is divided into three equal parts called three faces, and each face is of 10 degrees. And these faces begin from the beginning of Aries and proceed in the order of the signs of the planets, so that the first face is of Mars, that is, the first 10 degrees. The second face of Aries, that is, the next 10 degrees, are of the Sun, who succeeds Mars in the order of the spheres. The third is of Venus, who succeeds the Sun. And the first face of Taurus is of Mercury, who succeeds Venus. The second of the Moon, who succeeds Mercury. The third of Saturn. And the first of Gemini of Jupiter. And so according to this order up to the end of the signs. Afterwards he teaches how to find by numbers to which planet any face belongs. And he says, when you have a degree of any sign and wish to know whose planet's face it is in that degree, compute the number of signs from the beginning of Aries up to the beginning of the proposed sign; and multiply that number by three; and to the product add the complete faces of the proposed sign. For example, if 10 complete degrees have passed, add one. If 20 complete, add two. Then from the total number subtract 7 as many times as you can. What remains, count from Mars in the order of the planets. And where the number ends, the following planet is the lord of the sought face. For example, I have 15 degrees of Leo. I want to know whose face the 15th degree of Leo is. I know that from the beginning of Aries there are 4 complete signs. I will therefore multiply 4 by 3, and it will be 12. And I know that one complete face has passed in Leo; therefore I will add one, and it will be 13 complete faces from the beginning of Aries. I will subtract 7 from that, and 6 will remain. I will give the first unit to Mars, the second to the Sun, the third to Venus, the fourth to Mercury, the fifth to the Moon, the sixth to Saturn. Therefore, the following face, which was not complete, will be of Jupiter. Afterwards he places a table whose use is easy. For you will seek the name of that sign whose face's lord you seek, and you will find directly who is the lord of the first face, and who of the second, and who of the third. And because, with God's help, he has now finished concerning the dignities of the planets in the signs. In this part he determines concerning the strengths they have in these dignities. And it can be divided into two parts: because in the first part he shows how many strengths a planet has in each dignity. In the second part he compares these dignities to sensible things. There is a certain saying about this matter. The first part can be divided into two: because first he continues to speak. He says that, with God's help, he has completed concerning the dignities of the planets in the signs. Now he wants to show how many strengths each has in these dignities. Afterwards he says that the lord of the house has great strengths. The lord of exaltation has four. The lord of triplicity has three. The lord of the term has two. The lord of the face has one. Afterwards he repeats that controversy about the terms. And he places a comparison in the dignities of the planets, saying that some have made such a comparison of the dignities of the planets that a planet existing in its house is like a man existing in his own house and dominion. And a planet in its exaltation is like a man in his kingdom and glory, and it is clear in the text. From this text it can be noted that if any planet suffers great misfortune in its house or exaltation, this is very detestable. Just as it would be very detestable if a king were conquered in his own kingdom and in the strongest place of his kingdom. Therefore, if luminaries are eclipsed in their own houses or exaltations, this is a bad sign. He will speak of this. The figures of the signs follow these. The previous author determined concerning the dignities of the planets in the signs and concerning the strengths they have in these dignities. In this part he determines concerning the figures or forms of these signs, that is, he shows us which signs have human forms and which have forms of other animals. And it remains undivided. He says that some signs are called rational, those whose images are figured to the images of men. And these are Gemini, Virgo, Aquarius, Libra, and half of Sagittarius.

[Sign Classifications and Terrestrial Divisions]
the last part of Sagittarius. And these are said to have beautiful voices. And their virtue is greater when they are in the East. And some of the signs are said to have voices, namely Gemini, Virgo, and Pisces. Some of them are said to be quadrupedal, namely Sagittarius, Leo, Aries, Taurus, and Capricorn. And some of these are domestic, meaning those that are figured according to the shapes of domestic animals. And these are Aries, Taurus, and Capricorn. And their virtue appears more when they are in the South. But the virtue of Virgo, Capricorn, and Aquarius appears more when they are in the North. And some of the signs are seen as vicious, ugly, and tortuous, namely Aries, Taurus, Cancer, Scorpio, and Pisces. And their virtue appears more in the West. Some, however, are sterile, namely Gemini, Leo, Virgo. And some are said to have few children, namely Aries, Taurus, Libra, Sagittarius, Capricorn, and Aquarius. And some of these signs are very luxurious, namely Aries, Taurus, Leo, and Capricorn. And some are said to have many children, namely Cancer, Scorpio, and Pisces. And some of the signs are said to have a half-voice, namely those that have the voice of roaring and bellowing animals, such as Aries, Taurus, Leo, Capricorn, and the last part of Sagittarius. Some of the signs are said to be entirely voiceless, namely those that are figured according to the images of voiceless animals, such as Cancer, Scorpio, and Pisces. Daly Abenragel briefly explains the forms of the signs, saying: Some signs are in the form of humans. Others in the form of beasts. Others in the form of wild beasts. Others in the form of reptiles. Those in human form are Gemini, Libra, Aquarius, Virgo. In the form of beasts are Aries, Taurus, Capricorn, and Sagittarius. In the form of wild beasts, i.e., predatory animals, is Leo. In the form of reptiles are Cancer, Scorpio, and Pisces. Each of the signs has its own signification. Ptolemy determined the figures of the signs. In this, he shows us what the signs have from the limbs of humans, and from regions, and from planets. And it can be divided into two parts: because in the first part he does what has been said. In the second, he determines the pains of the planets in the signs. The second begins there: And the figure of the planet will signify pain. The first can be divided into 12 parts according to the 12 signs. It is clear what he says in the text, except that the names of the regions are not known to us. It is to be noted here that Ptolemy divides the entire habitable earth into four parts. And according to Ptolemy's division, one can imagine a line passing from East to West through the middle of the habitation, so that this line divides the southern part from the northern. And Daly says that this line is distant from the equator by 36 degrees. And according to this division, it is distant from the last habitation in the North by 30 degrees or so, so that the total width contains 66 degrees. And such is the distance from the equator to the arctic circle: indeed it is 66 degrees, 26 minutes, and 30 seconds. Therefore Daly says "or so." And he says that at the end of this line towards the West is the passage of Hercules. And this is where one passes into Spain, and there is a narrow sea there, so that one standing on one shore can see one standing on the other. There are three islands there, one of which is seen by those passing into Spain through the western land. And on it stands an idol holding keys in its hand to show that beyond that place there is no habitation. And on each of the other two islands stands an idol in the same manner. And in the eastern part, at the end of the aforesaid line, stand idols in the same manner, holding keys and showing that beyond that place there is no habitation towards the East. Daly says that Hercules placed these idols as a sign that he had acquired the whole world. The length of the aforesaid line, according to Daly, is 180 degrees. Having seen these things, in Ptolemy's opinion, imagine this line divided in the middle so that 90 degrees remain towards the East, and another 90 towards the West. And imagine a line passing through the poles of the world through the middle of the division of the aforesaid line, so that it passes through the middle of the habitable earth according to latitude. The first line, however, was said to pass through the middle of the habitable earth according to longitude. It is clear, therefore, that the two aforesaid lines, which divide the entire habitable earth into four parts, join at the intersection of the lines, which is a point in the middle of the habitable earth. With this division understood, it is easy to see Ptolemy's intention in the division of signs and lands. Thus Ptolemy says that these three signs, Aries, Leo, and Sagittarius, which form the first triplicity, belong to the fourth part of the habitable earth, which is between the North and the West. And Jupiter governs that fourth part because he is northern; and Mars has participation with him because he belongs to the western part. And the three signs of the second triplicity, namely Taurus, Virgo, Capricorn, belong to the part that is between the South and the East; and Venus governs it because she is southern; and Saturn has participation with her because he belongs to the eastern part. And the three signs of the third triplicity, namely Gemini, Libra, and Aquarius, belong to the part that is between the East and the North; and Saturn governs it because he belongs to the East and Jupiter has participation with him because he belongs to the North. And the three signs of the fourth triplicity, namely Cancer, Scorpio, and Pisces, belong to the part that is between the South and the West; and Mars governs it because he belongs to the West; and Venus has participation with him. From the foregoing, anyone can conjecture to which sign any land belongs. For he will know by the longitude and latitude of the region to which quarter it belongs. For example: any land whose latitude is greater than 36 degrees and whose longitude from the West is less than 90 degrees is of the north-western quarter, and so on for the others in their own way. Therefore, having known the quarter in which your land is, you know that one sign out of the three signs of the triplicity of that quarter regards that land. And you will be able to know which of those three regards it by the customs and habits of the people living in it. For example: you know that the land of Christians is in the north-western part, so you know that Aries, Leo, and Sagittarius rule over it. And if I want to know over which part of it each of these signs rules, I look at the customs and conditions of the people with which great signs they agree. It is clear that the Romans are the most famous and noblest of this quarter, so it is fitting that the noblest sign among these three be attributed to them, and this is Leo, the house of the Sun. It is also clear that the Germans are irascible and furious men of the nature of Mars, so it is fitting that Aries, the house of Mars, be attributed to them. It is also clear that the Spanish are good soldiers, greatly exercised in arms, so it is fitting that Sagittarius, which is the sign of military affairs and wars, be attributed to them. And Ptolemy places this division in the text in the second part of the Quadripartitum. For he says thus: and the provinces agreeing with Aries are the land of the...

[Regions and Climates]
and the land of Salacia. I believe it should also be said of Scalavia and Germania. And those that concord with Leo are: Italy, Gaul, Apulia, and Sicily. And Daly says there: here are the ministers of Rome. And those that concord with Sagittarius are the lands of Turkey, Calatia, and Hispania. I do not care about the attribution of other signs to other lands, because neither their names nor the editions of men are known to me, nor would it be of any use to me to know them. If anyone knows them and does not wish to dwell on them, let him apply them in the manner described in the aforementioned three signs. Abraham Avenezra says that the first clime is of Capricorn and Aquarius, and its governor is Saturn. The second clime is of Sagittarius and Pisces, and its governor is Jupiter. The third clime is of Scorpio and Aries, and its governor is Mars. The fourth is of Leo, and its governor is the Sun. The fifth clime is of Taurus and Libra, and its governor is Venus. The sixth is of Gemini and Virgo, and its governor is Mercury. The seventh is of Cancer, and its governor is the Moon. Abraham Avenezra sets forth the conditions of those born under each sign, and his opinion is this: He who is born under the first face of Aries will be reddish and thin; his belly will be somewhat constricted, his flesh attenuated; he will have a mark above his left foot and on the elbow of his left hand; and his friends will be many, and he himself will hate evil. But he who is born under the second face will have blackness combined with the beauty of his face; his body will be temperate, quick to anger, concealing evil will in his mind; of high heart; his enemies will be many. He who is born under the third face will have a reddish and saffron color; he will be solitary. He who is born under the first face of Taurus will be short of stature; his eyes large; lips thick; and he will have a mark on his neck; and he is quick of heart; his friends many; he will delight in various manners. But he who is born under the second face will have a round face; a broad belly; beautiful eyes; and his mind will be willing and quick to act; and he will be hairy around the shoulders; and he will have a mark on his loins. And he who is born under the third face will be of beautiful color and beautiful face; and he will have a mark in his left eye; and he will be a laborious man; nor will he be fortunate in women. But he who is born at the end of this sign will lack natural testicles, or be an hermaphrodite. He who is born under the first face of Gemini will be of beautiful and decent body; and of eyes and hair; he will have a mark on his head or in his eyes. His sight will be keen; he will be least irascible; and he will be a worker and least fortunate with women. And he who is born under the second face will be short of stature and black, and a mark of blackness above his elbow; and his words beautiful and sweet. He who is born under the third face will have very small eyes; and he will be a suspicious and gentle man; and he will speak irrational words; and he will be a liar. He who is born under the first face of Cancer will be of decent body and hair; his eyebrows will be narrow, his nostrils long, and his shoulders broad; and he will have a mark on his right elbow or arm; and his soul good; his friends many; and he will be learned and ingenious. He who is born under the second face will have a reddish color, short stature; lacking a beard; and he will have a mark in his eyes. He who is born under the third face will be fat and short of stature; and he will have a multitude of hairs on his eyebrows. He who is born under the first face of Leo will be beautiful in body and face; and the color of his face will be reddish mixed with white; his eyes mixed; his chest straight; and his legs will suffer from disease in the upper part; he will be known among people; and simple, not mixed with the company of kings. He who is born under the second face will be beautiful; his chest will be broad; his testicles and legs slender; and he will be honored among his family and of high heart. But he who is born under the third face will be somewhat short of stature; and his color will be white mixed with rosy; his voice vehement; loving women; and he will have many friends and suffer many diseases. He who is born under the first face of Virgo will be of decent stature; his body will be erect and beautiful; and he will be learned and active; his hair curly; and he will love justice; his voice vehement; he will be sterile; his soul good; his face beautiful; and he will be a scribe and well-taught. But he who is born under the second face will be of beautiful appearance; his eyes small; his nose beautiful; and he will be disciplined and simple, of a willing heart. He will love to be praised. He who is born under the third face will be beautiful in appearance, susceptible to discipline; of true senses and simple and wise. He who is born under the first face of Libra will be beautiful of face; and ulcers will be on his head; and he will be a worker and simple and disciplined. He who is born under the second face will be of beautiful countenance and will have an impediment in his eyes; and he is of a willing heart. He who is born under the third face will be beautiful and will be known and honored among people. And he who is born at the end of this sign will be of no sex or of both sexes. He who is born under the first face of Scorpio will be little beautiful; and he will have a mark on his head; and his chest will be broad. And he will have a mark on his left foot or in his right hand; and he will be a man of good discipline, full of discretion, and quick in speech. He who is born under the second face, his head will be large; and he will be of moderately beautiful figure; and he will have a mark on his knee and back; and he will be a man of discipline, multiplying his words. He who is born under the third face will be short of stature; his eyes small; desirous of eating; loving women. But he who is born at the end of this sign will be of no sex or of both sexes. He who is born under the first face of Sagittarius will be of beautiful appearance; graceful in aspect; of straight stature; loving good; associating with kings and magnates. He who is born under the second face will have a decent body; his face saffron; his eyebrows compressed; and he will have a mark on his chest. He who is born under the third face will be tall; beautiful of face; his eyes like a cat's; his chest broad; and he will have a mark on his left leg. He who is born under the first face of Capricorn will have a decent body; a broad chest; and he will have a black mark on his elbow; he will be astute, disciplined, simple, and willing. He who is born under the second face will be beautiful; he will have long nostrils; his eyes beautiful; his will evil and irascible; he is a man of knowledge. He who is born under the third face will be beautiful of body; his face yellowish; and on his left arm there will be a mark or on his knee; quick to anger; despising evil or fighting for evil; loving women; a man of discipline, loving companions. But he who is born at the end of this sign will be an illegitimate child, and this sign is of little value in the nativities of women. But he who is born under the first face of Aquarius will be beautiful in body and face; and he will have a mark on his chest or left foot; and he will be a disciplined man and loving companions. He who is born under the second face will be tall; his face will be red; and he will have a mark on his back and under his elbow; and he will be in pain all his days. He who is born under the third face will be beautiful of body; short of stature; rosy of face; he will have a mark under his elbows; and he will be a lover of women. And he who is born at the end of this sign will be diversified in his figure and in all his works. But he who is born under the first face of Pisces, his body will be white; and his face likewise; his chest broad; his beard beautiful; his forehead clear; his eyes more black than white. And some member will be lacking to him; he will love to sleep; and he will be gluttonous and drunken; and he will have a mark under his elbow.

[Planets and Body Parts]
or in the foot. A native born under the second face will be of short stature, beautiful in appearance, with a black beard, hairy, and will walk with difficulty among the sons of men. A native born under the third face of Pisces will be of splendid appearance, his eyes beautiful, and he will be sickly. Indeed, the author first shows how the planets relate to the members of the human body. In this part, he shows us how the planets relate to the members of the human body in those signs. And this part can be divided into 12 parts according to the 12 signs, where the parts begin. The first part can be divided into two, because first it proposes, second it follows there: in Aries. He says first that if any planet signifies some infirmity or debility in the human body, it will have in each sign a proper member in which that infirmity will be. And it is fitting to treat the pains of the planets in the signs. And it begins from Aries, proceeding according to the succession of signs and planets. What the author says is clear in the text. For the evidence of one part, I give one example. I assume that in some nativity, Saturn signifies a debility of some member to the native, and Saturn is in Aries. I say that that debility or infirmity will be in the chest. And if Saturn is in Taurus, that infirmity will be in the belly, and so you understand for the other signs. I also assume that Mars in a nativity (you understand this for the revolution of the native's years) signifies a wound, and Mars is in Aries, the wound will be in the head. If in Taurus, the wound will be in the neck, and so for the other signs and planets you understand. Ptolemy wants the members in which diseases and impediments fall to be taken from the figure of the sky at the hour of nativity or revolution. For he says in the 74th proposition of the Centiloquium: when Mars is in the ascendant of any nativity, there will be a scar on the face or head of the native. For Daly says that the head is of the ascendant, and the neck is of the second house, the arms of the third house, and so according to the order of the houses, as was said about the signs. He will speak more extensively on this matter, God willing, in the chapter of the sixth house. Also, the author determines in this part about certain special properties of the planets that are in different degrees of the circle of signs, and there are six of them. For there are some masculine degrees and some feminine. And there are some lucid degrees and some dark. Also, there are some degrees that are called wells. And there are some degrees that are called azemena. And there are some degrees that are called augmenting fortune. And there are some degrees that are called consortes. And according to this, this part can be divided into six parts: because in the first part it enumerates masculine and feminine degrees. In the second part it enumerates lucid, dark, and smoky degrees. In the third part it enumerates degrees that are called wells. In the fourth part it enumerates degrees that are called azemena. In the fifth part it enumerates degrees that are called augmenting fortune and degrees of exaltation. In the sixth part it enumerates degrees that are called consortes. The first part begins at the beginning. The second begins there: and in each of these signs. The third begins there: and in the signs there are degrees. The fourth there: and there are in the signs certain degrees. The fifth there: and in the circle. The sixth there: and all two degrees. The first part can be divided into two parts: because in the first part it begins to enumerate masculine and feminine degrees literally. In the second part it provides a table of them. As it says, it is clear in the text. Afterwards it says that there are certain degrees in the circle that are called lucid and some dark, and some smoky, and some that are called empty. And it begins by enumerating them first. And then it provides a table of them, and it is clear. After that it says that there are in the circle certain degrees that are called wells. And it enumerates all of them in the text. And some books have a table made of them. Then it says that in the signs there are certain degrees that are called azemena. And it says that azemena is a certain bodily debility, such as blindness or deafness or something similar, or the loss of a member. In this regard, it is to be noted that Daly Abenragel says in the first chapter of the sixth house of his book on nativities: When the azemena part is in the partition of the ascendant and the Moon is conjoined with it, or the lord of the ascendant signifies azemena, it will be in that member of the native that falls in the partition of that sign. It is also to be noted that if the Sun in someone's nativity is in an azemena degree, there will be a debility in the right eye; if the Moon is, in the left. Afterwards it says that there are certain degrees in the circle that are called augmenting fortune, and it enumerates them in the text. In this regard, it is to be noted that Paly says in the commentary on the 229th proposition of the first part of the Quadripartitum: you should know that the degrees augmenting fortune are the degrees of exaltation of the Sun and fortunate planets, such as the 19th of Aries, the 3rd of Taurus, the 15th of Cancer, the 27th of Pisces. Similarly, there are those in which the terms of the fortunes are joined, such as the 12th of Sagittarius and the 13th of Pisces. And there are also degrees of the terms of the fortunes. And degrees in which there are fixed stars of the nature of fortunes. And conversely, those in which there are stars of the nature of misfortunes. And afterwards it says that all two degrees that are of the same longitude from the heads of the movable signs are of the same strength. And they are called consortes, such as the 20th degree of Capricorn and the 10th degree of Sagittarius. For these two degrees are equally distant from the head of Capricorn. And the 20th of Libra and the 10th of Virgo are equally distant from the head of Libra. And the 20th of Cancer and the 10th of Gemini are equally distant from the beginning of Cancer. And the 20th degree of Aries and the 10th of Pisces are equally distant from the beginning of Aries. Ptolemy says in the 229th proposition of the first part: Other astrologers have spoken much about degrees and divided them into lucid, slippery, and smoky degrees. And some of them are azemena, and some of them are wells. And they have spoken of many other things, as you will find in many astronomical books. And if they found this by experience, it is good to work by it. And perhaps if it happened to them that some planet or star was in a degree or its ray, and it made fortune, they concluded that the degree did this. And if indeed it is so, it is fitting that you move from one degree to another. And here let us put an end to our reasoning. It seems from the text that Ptolemy does not much approve of the degrees augmenting fortune. For he says: if it is so, it is fitting that you move from one degree to another. For degrees are called lucid or dark because of the fixed stars existing there. And Paly wants, according to what was previously alleged, that degrees are called augmenting fortune in which there are stars of the nature of fortunes. It is clear, however, that fixed stars change their places with respect to the zodiac of the ninth sphere. From that text of Ptolemy, it is possible.

[Judgments from the Ninth Sphere]
Judgments or indications should be made according to the ninth sphere, and not according to the eighth. For since he wishes to change these degrees, it is consequent that the degrees according to which judgments ought to be made do not change. Albumazar in his introduction sets forth these degrees, namely, masculine and feminine, lucid and shadowy, etc. And he says there that if a planet in a nativity or interrogation of a male is in a masculine degree, or in a nativity of a female or interrogation in a feminine degree, its signification will be stronger. Concerning lucid, shadowy, and famous degrees, he says that if a planet falls in a lucid degree, its signification will be stronger in the signification of honors and it signifies beauty. And if it falls in a shadowy degree, it signifies hardness and slowness and a horrible and dark and evil thing. And when it falls in a dusky, or shadowy, or smoky degree, or in an empty degree, it signifies something slightly horrible. And if a planet falls in a degree of a well, its beauty and appearance will depart, and it will be weakened in its signification. For when fortunes fall into them, they are weakened in their signification. But when malefics fall into them, their signification is weakened. And perhaps fortune will signify an accidental event because of their weakness over evil. Concerning degrees that increase fortune, he says the ancients thought that there would be degrees in the circle that increase fortune. And they said that when planets are not in places signifying the native's fortune, and the Moon or Part of Fortune is in these degrees, or these degrees themselves are ascending, they increase the native's fortune. And if the planets signify a fall for him, these degrees move him to exaltation by some quantity with a certain motion. Concerning degrees of sublimity, he says: Some have said that when the Ascendant is one of these degrees, or the Sun is in a diurnal nativity, or the Moon in a nocturnal nativity in some of them, and it is in the best place in the figure. And when with this the planets of the root of the nativity signify fortune, it will lead the native to sublimity and a seat of nobility, and he will rule lands and cities, and possess much wealth. And because, with God's help, the author first determined concerning the essential being of the circle of signs, here he determines concerning its accidental being. And it is divided into two parts: first, it continues the things said; second, it follows there: for the circle of signs. And that is divided into two parts: first, it determines concerning the accidental division of the circle of signs. Second, it determines concerning the properties and significations consequent to that division; and it begins there: the fourth part which is from the Ascendant. And that is divided into two parts: first, it sets forth the properties and significations of the quarters. Second, it sets forth the significations of the individual houses; and that begins there: and one of the houses. First, he says after completing the essential being of the circle of signs, now he wishes to treat of its accidental being. Afterwards he says that the circle figures at every hour such a figure which is divided into four parts, which the circle of the horizon and the circle of the meridian divide. And each of these quarters is divided into three equal parts according to the division of the ascending sign in the direct circle. And in this way the whole circle is divided into 12 parts which are called towers or houses, whose explanation is in the canons of the tables. Two great circles passing through the poles of the world are to be understood: one is the meridian circle; and the other is the circle passing through the point of the zodiac which is in contact with the eastern horizon, and through the opposite point, namely, which is in contact with the western horizon, intersecting the meridian circle above the poles of the world. These two circles divide the whole heaven into four parts which are sometimes equal to each other, sometimes unequal; but for the most part they are unequal. For if the beginning of Aries or the beginning of Libra is in the Ascendant, these quarters are equal. In all other dispositions, however, they are unequal. Afterwards, let the portion of the equinoctial circle intercepted between the meridian circle and the circle passing through the beginning of the Ascendant be understood to be divided into three equal parts. Similarly, let the other portion of the equinoctial circle which is from the Ascendant to the lower part of the meridian circle, namely, to the angle of the earth, be understood to be divided into three equal parts. Then let great circles passing through the aforesaid divisions and through the poles of the world be imagined. Then the portion of the zodiac intercepted between any two of the first circles is one house. This is Ptolemy's position; and this is commonly held. There is also another imagination concerning the houses which Abraham Avenezre holds. And he imagines circles passing through the divisions of the equinoctial and through the intersection of the meridian circle and the horizon in the northern part. This method is not commonly held; therefore, I do not care to explain it much. To find the beginnings of the 12 houses of the astrolabe is not difficult; indeed, it is easy, whose doctrine to interpose here would be long and superfluous, since it has been sufficiently set forth in the canons of the astrolabe. But whoever wishes to equalize the houses by tables will find complete doctrine in the canons of the tables of the primum mobile. Then the author says the beginning of this division is the Ascendant, whose beginning is at the point of the hemisphere on the eastern side. Then follows the second house; then the third; and so on to the twelfth. The fourth and significations of the circle of signs consequent to its accidental division. And he says that the fourth part of the circle which is from the Ascendant to the Midheaven, namely, the 12th, 11th, and 10th houses, is called the eastern masculine approaching. And it signifies the beginning of life and is called puerile sanguine. And the other fourth is from the Midheaven to the degree of the west, namely, the 9th, 8th, and 7th houses, is called the southern feminine receding from us; and it signifies the middle age which is called the perfection of youth; and it is called aestival and choleric. The third fourth which is from the degree of the west to the angle of the earth, namely, the 6th, 5th, and 4th houses, is western masculine approaching us; and it signifies the end of life; and it is called autumnal melancholic; and it is of middle age. The fourth part which is from the angle of the earth to the Ascendant, namely, the third, second, and first houses, is northern feminine receding from us; and it signifies what happens to a man after his death as regards the memory of men, namely, whether good or evil is said of him. And this part is called senile phlegmatic defective and hibernal. And this is a correct comparison which the author sets forth here, just as that which he set forth in the essential division of the circle, except that he adds that this signifies the beginning and middle and end of life and what happens to a man after his death. Afterwards he says that the whole half which is from the Midheaven going through the Ascendant to the fourth house is called the ascending half. And the other half which is from the fourth house going through the degree of the west to the Midheaven is called ascending. And the whole half which is

[Houses and their significations]
that which is above the earth is called the right, and that which is below the earth is called the left. Then it says that the first house, 7, 4, 2, 7, and 10 are called angles. And 2, 5, 8, and 11 are called succedents to the angles. But 3, 6, 9, and 12 are called cadent from the angles. Then it adds a notable point: it says that when a planet is in an angle or in a succedent, it is said to be effective; and if it is in the cadent houses, it is said to be ineffective. Each of these houses, the author says, has its own proper significations. The 12 houses, and all of this can be divided into four parts: in the first part, it sets out the significations of the 12 houses as they pertain to human existence. In the second part, it sets out the significations of the houses as they pertain to colors. In the third part, it sets out certain rules that can be called aphorisms. In the fourth part, it teaches how to choose significators. The first part begins at the beginning. The second begins there: they signify: and the 12 houses' colors. The third there: and it is said in the signification of the houses. The fourth there: and when you wish to know the planet ruling the matter. The first part can be divided into twelve parts according to the significations of the 12 houses, and where they begin will be clear. First, it says that each house signifies something about human existence. For the first house, which begins from the eastern horizon and is called the ascendant, signifies the bodies of men and life: the beginnings of all works in interrogations, speeches, rumors, and other such things. And it signifies the thought of the querent, that is, what the querent has in mind, and it signifies the beginning of life. And the lord of the first triplicity of the first house, the first, signifies life and the nature of the native or querent, and his delights and desires, what he loves or hates: and what good or evil befalls him at the beginning of life. And the second lord of the triplicity of this house signifies the life and body and strength or health of the native, and the middle of life. The third lord of the triplicity signifies the same as the second, and signifies by itself the end of life. From this letter, it can be gathered that if the first lord of the triplicity of this house is stronger than the other two, the first part of life will be better, and so you should understand for the other two. Concerning this house, certain things are to be noted. First, it is to be noted concerning the intention of the querent, which Ptolemy says in the 94th proposition of the Centiloquium: The place of the stronger significator in the ascendant is that which is in the mind of the querent. Therefore, when you wish to know the intention of the querent, see which planet has more strength in the ascendant at that hour when he comes to you to ask, and see in which house out of the 12 houses that planet is. And you should speak according to the significations of that house in which it is. For example, I assume the ascendant is Leo, and the Sun has more strength in the degree of the ascendant, and I assume that the Sun is in the 2nd house. I say that his intention is to ask about his substance or about profit or about something similar. And if the Sun had been in the third house, I would have said that he wanted to ask something about the existence of a brother or brothers, and so on for the other houses in their own way. And if, when he came to you, he held something in his hand or concealed it in some other way, and if you wish to know the substance and nature of that thing, look at the stronger planet in the ascendant. If it aspects the ascendant, that thing will be of the substance of the ascendant sign. If it does not aspect the ascendant, its substance will be of the sign in which the planet is. If it is an earthy sign, it will be of the nature of earth or some other thing born from the earth. If it is a watery sign, it will be some other thing of the nature of water, or born from water. If it is airy, it will be some other thing of the nature of air. If it is a fiery sign, it will be some other thing that operates by fire. And if you wish to know the color of the thing, look at the lord of the hour and judge its color. Of the colors of the planets, it will be said later when we speak of the natures of the planets, God willing. And if you wish to know whether the thing is new or old, look at the Moon: if it is above the earth, it will be new; if it is below the earth, it will be old. And if you wish to know whether it is long or short, look at the lord of the term of the degree of the angle of the earth, and if it is in the apogee of its circle, the thing will be long. If it is in the opposite of the apogee, it will be short. If in the middle longitudes, it will be moderate between long and short. This is the opinion of Ptolemy in the 90th proposition of the Centiloquium. When the significator aspects the ascendant, etc. Haly Abenragel says that if someone asks you about his life, whether it will be long or short: look at the lord of the ascendant and the Moon. If they are safe from misfortunes, it signifies a long life. And if they are combust or unfortunate, it signifies a short life. It is to be noted concerning nourishment, that is, whether a child will live or not. Haly Abenragel says that when the lords of the triplicity of the luminary of the time (meaning the lords of the triplicity of the sign in which the Sun is, if it is a diurnal nativity, or of the Moon in a nocturnal nativity) are in the ascendant, or in the 10th house, or 11th, or 5th, it is a signification of good and easy nourishment. And if they are in the seventh, it signifies bad nourishment: and anxious and laborious. When the degree of the ascendant and the luminary of the time are afflicted, it signifies that he will not be nourished unless the lords of the triplicity are safe and firm in the angles. When the Moon is unfortunate in the ascendant, it does not signify nourishment. When the Moon is in the 4th house, corporally conjoined with an unfortunate planet, or aspects an unfortunate planet from the 4th or by opposition, it signifies that he will not be nourished and his mother is in danger: or perhaps she will die.
