Aben Ezra says: If the lord of the ascendant is combust, the native will not live for the space of 8 days. A nativity was brought to me of a child whose ascendant was Virgo, and Mercury was in Pisces in its detriment, retrograde and combust. And I believed this saying and said that the child would not live for eight days, and he died on the sixth day. Haly Abenragel says: the conjunction of planets does not signify humanity. He means that the conjunction of several planets in the ascendant does not signify nourishment. And he gives a notable example there. He says: the king of our city called me, and one of the women gave birth to a son, and the ascendant was Libra, 8 degrees of Mercury's term: and Jupiter, Venus, Mars, and Mercury were in it, and a society of astrologers gathered there, and each of them gave his opinion: and I was silent. The king said to me: what do you have that you do not speak? To whom I replied: give me a term of three days: because if your son passes the third day, it will be a great miracle concerning him. And when the native had completed 24 hours, he began to speak: and he spoke and made a sign with his hand, and the king was very frightened by it. And he said it was possible that he would say some prophecy: or some miracle. And the king went to the native: and we with him to hear what he would say. And the infant said: I am born unfortunate: and I am born to judge the loss of the kingdom and the destruction of the German people. Then the native immediately fell and died. Concerning those who die before they receive food, Ptolemy says in the Quadripartitum: generally I say that when any luminary is in any of the angles, and there is also some unfortunate planet having participation with it in longitude, which is degree by degree with it: or aspects it in a figure of two equals. And it does not have a fortunate planet participating with it in figure. And the disposer of the luminaries of the place is found in the places of the unfortunate planets, that native will not receive food and will die at the hour he is born.

[Dragon's Tail in Ascendant]
Abrabam says that if the Dragon's Tail is in the ascendant of a nativity, that native will be blind, and the distance from the ascendant in degrees will be the years. For example, if it is in the 10th degree from the ascendant, he will be blind in the 10th year. Elections of this kind are the beginnings of things, such as beginning to build or to do something. Hyspalensis says in the elections of the first house: If you know someone's nativity, be careful in their election not to place a sign in the ascendant in which there was an infortune in their nativity. But if you do not know the nativity, choose according to the nature of the thing for which the election is made. For example, if the election is for beginning to write a book, Mercury should be fortified. If for going to war, Mars should be fortified. If for building, a fixed sign should be placed in the ascendant. The same Hyspalensis says, when wishing to choose a time for bloodletting, make sure that the Moon is in a trine or sextile aspect to Mars. And be careful that it is not conjunct with him bodily, or in a square or opposition to him. And make sure that the Moon is in a sign of diminishing humor. The second house. The author here sets forth the significations of the second house. And he says that the second house signifies substance and sustenance and helpers and ministers, and it signifies the end of youth. And Anduzgar said, see which of the three lords of the triplicity of the house of substance is stronger in itself, that is, in the place where it is in the figure, and it will signify substance. If it is in the tenth house, he will have substance from a king. And if it is in the house of trust, that is, in the eleventh, it will be better. Another letter says if it is in the house of faith, it will be more. I believe that the first letter is true. For the house of trust is the house of the king's substance. And the first lord of the triplicity gives substance at the beginning of life; if he is fortunate, the native will be rich at the beginning of life. The second gives substance in the middle of life; if he is fortunate, the native will be rich in the middle of life. The third gives substance at the end of life; if he is fortunate, the native will be rich at the end of life. And understand similarly about their misfortunes, that is, if any of them is unfortunate, the native will lose substance in that part of life which is attributed to him. Hyspalensis says in the canons of this house, consider whether the lord of the second house is in the ascendant or gives its strength to the lord of the ascendant and is not in a fallen house. If so, he will have gain without labor. And if the opposite is true, it will be the reverse. And if Jupiter is angular in the nativity, or is in his honor, or has strength in the ascendant, or aspects the Part of Fortune, or is the lord of the house of the Sun in a day nativity, or the lord of the house of the Moon in a night nativity, or is the lord of the hour, the native will not lack wealth in his life, because this, that is, Jupiter, is the lord of substance. But if the lord of the ascendant aspects the lord of substance or its house or the Part of Fortune with an aspect of enmity, he will destroy substance with his own hand. If the lord of the ascendant is in the second house unfortunate, he will give his substance by his own will. But if there is an unfortunate planet there who is not the lord of the ascendant, he will take from him by force or theft. If Capricorn is the ascendant, the native will be greedy and avaricious, because the lord of the ascendant and the lord of the second are the same, namely Saturn. Ptolemy says in the canons of this house, concerning matters pertaining to gains of substance, how they will be, it is fitting for us to inquire only from the Part of Fortune, which we always know by that which is between the Sun and the Moon, projected from the ascendant in day nativities and in night nativities. According to which it should be noted that the Part of Fortune according to Ptolemy is projected in this way: subtract the true place of the Sun from the true place of the Moon, and what remains is counted from the degree of the ascendant, and where the number ends, there is the Part of Fortune. Ptolemy commands to always do this, whether it is by day or by night. More will be said about this, God willing, in the exposition of the fifth difference, for there it has its place. Afterwards, Ptolemy says the judgment of this is in this manner. I mean, take the planets governing the sign. Daly says there that the rule by which we know the native's wealth is to take the planets governing the place of the Part of Fortune and prefer the one who has more dignities there. Then Ptolemy says, and when the governors of the Part of Fortune are strong and powerful, the native will have great wealth, especially if the two luminaries testify there with a concordant testimony, that is, a trine or sextile aspect. Ptolemy, know that Saturn signifies that the native's wealth will be from women, or by labor of the earth, or by the sea. And Jupiter signifies that wealth will be from stewardship or from gifts of good and religious people. And Mars signifies that wealth will be from producing soldiers or governing men of arms. And Venus signifies that wealth will be from gifts of friends and women. And Mercury signifies that wealth will be from sciences and merchandise. Daly Abenragel says that in this we must first look at the fixed stars which are of the first magnitude. And if we find any of them in the degree of the ascendant, or in the degree of the tenth house, or in the degree of the seventh, or in the degree of the fourth, or in the degree of the Sun if the nativity is diurnal, or in the degree of the Moon if the nativity is nocturnal. And the best of all these places is the degree of the ascendant, then the degree of the tenth house, then the degree of the seventh, then the fourth. And if any of the aforesaid stars are in two places, or in three, or more, and the native is of royal lineage, he will be a high king. And if he is not of royal lineage, he will have power and command similar to the power and command of a king, and he will attain great nobility and high dominion, and he will rule over cities and nations. And know that the fixed stars, that is, of the first honor, elevate a man to a high degree and great dignity and change him from the lowest to the highest. Ptolemy says the same in the 29th proposition of the Centiloquium: fixed stars give gifts exceeding measure, but often end in evil. Daly says in the commentary on the same proposition, when these stars alone preside, that is, without the testimony of fortunate planets, their death will be a most evil death. Daly Abenragel says, when the Part of Fortune is cadent, that is, in a bad place, or is under the rays of the Sun, or in the rays of an infortune, and its lord is in a peregrine place, that is, in a place where it has no dignity, and the lord of the second house does not aspect the ascendant, the native will be laborious and poor and will live a narrow and miserable life. Neither the Sun nor Mars nor Saturn is good in the second house in any nativity, nor will the native have good from it, because the Sun destroys planets and takes away their light, and Mars is the significator of impediments, labors, and lack of substance. Saturn signifies poverty and indigence, and this is especially true if the lord of the house of substance is combust with the damnation of the Part of Fortune. Abrabam says, if you wish to know which of those born will be poor or rich, look at the lord of the second house. If he is fortunate, he will be rich; if combust or retrograde or in his fall, he will be poor, as has been said in nativities, so understand in questions. Concerning elections made in this house, Hyspalensis says, if you wish to buy something for the sake of gain, make sure that the Moon is in a trine or sextile aspect to the Sun, and be careful that it is not under the light in the third.

[Sun and Ascendant Lord]
Sun: It is better that the lord of the ascendant gives strength to the planet existing in the tenth or eleventh house, so that the recipient is not retrograde. If Jupiter is in the ascendant, fourteenth, eleventh, or second house, it is good. Also, look for the Part of Fortune to be in a good place, and it is better that the lord of the Part or the Moon or the Sun aspects it. The third house here sets forth the significations of the third house, and says that the third house signifies brothers and sisters, relatives and kin, and loved ones; and it signifies faith and religion, messages and embassies, changes, short journeys. And it signifies the state of life before death. And Anduzgazar says that the first lord of the triplicity of this third house signifies older brothers. The second, middle brothers. The third, younger brothers; and their status and dignity are judged according to the status of these lords. Daly Abenragel says that when the Sun is the lord of the third house from the ascendant and burns the lord of the second house or the Part of Substance, it signifies that the native will lose substance on account of brothers, and will pay for them impositions, losses, and many damages. When the lord of the third house and the Part of Brothers or Jupiter are in common signs or signs of many children, and the Fortunes aspect them with friendly aspect and with reception, it signifies that the native is the firstborn among his brothers, and that he will have powerful and good brothers. If the lord of the house of brothers is combust, or the Part of Brothers is combust, or if the Sun is in the house of brothers, or opposite Jupiter; these are significations of few brothers, and that they will be destroyed and scattered. When the lord of the house of brothers is unfortunate above the earth, it signifies that harm and occasion will come to the brothers who were before him. And if this misfortune occurs while he is below the earth, it is bad; and this harm will come to the brothers who will be after him. And in this way you will speak in good and fortune when he is fortunate in good and strong places. If the lord of the house of brothers is in the ascendant, it signifies that the native is the firstborn, or will be alone without ever having brothers or sisters; or when there is no planet between the ascendant and the midheaven, it similarly signifies that the native is the firstborn. And if any brothers are born after him, they will be lost. And if any of them remain, he will always be older and better. When in any revolution of the native's years, the lord of the third house is in the tenth from the ascendant of the nativity, one of his brothers will die in that year. Similarly, if the lord of the third radical house of the nativity is in the tenth house of the revolution; this is because the tenth house from the ascendant is the eighth from the third house. If someone asks you about the state of his brother, look at the third sign from the ascendant, which is the house of brothers, and its lord of the triplicity and the lord of that house, and what aspects it from fortunes or misfortunes, and in what place it is: for if you find the lord of the third house in the sixth house, or applying to the lord of the sixth house, or the lord of the sixth in the third, you will say that his brother is sick. And if you find him in the fifth or second, you will say that his brother is not in his place, because he has gone out of his place. And if you find the lord of the third house unfortunate, or in the twelfth, you will say that his brother is in anxiety or in sickness. And if you find the lord of the third with Mars, both conjoined and entering combustion under the Sun's rays, you will say that he will not escape from sickness. And if both are combust, indicate death in all ways. And in this way you will look if you are asked about things pertaining to other houses, such as a father or son or wife. Hyspalensis says, wanting to begin a journey, make sure that a fortunate planet aspects the third house or its lord, so that there is no malefic there or its square aspect or opposition. If the Moon is in the third house, it is good. Cancer, Leo, and Capricorn are bad for a short journey. The Moon in the ascendant or in the fourth house is bad in every election. Beware that the Moon is not in the via combusta, which is from the 19th degree of Libra to the third of Scorpio. Also beware that the Moon is not near the head or tail of the Dragon within 12 degrees. The fourth house here sets forth the significations of the fourth house. And it says that the fourth house signifies fathers and inheritances and the ends of things; and it signifies treasures and all hidden and concealed things; and it signifies the end of life. And Anduzgazar says that the first lord of the triplicity of the fourth house signifies fathers. The second signifies cities and lands. The third signifies the end of things and prisons. Daly Abenragel says: Look at the state of the father and the lords of the triplicity of the fourth house. If the first lord of the triplicity of the fourth house is in its house or in its exaltation, or in its hayz, received by the Sun or Jupiter, and is in a high place of the midheaven or in the fifth house, it signifies a good state of the father, nobility, high position, riches, power, and a long life and good fortune, and this if the sign in which this planet was is masculine: however, if the sign itself is feminine, it signifies to the mother what we have said; and especially if the planet is feminine. What hayz is, he will explain later, God willing. And if the second lord of the triplicity of the fourth house is strong, the father will have lands and will cultivate them and will work in them and will have good utility or profit from this part. And if these planets are in a diverse or contrary state, judge them. And if the third lord of the triplicity of the fourth house is strong and fortunate as we have said, the father will be a man who extracts treasures and cuts vines, and prepares precious stones. And if he is in a state diverse from what we have said, he will be a stone cutter or will work in bad and stinking materials. If the Sun in diurnal nativities or Saturn in nocturnal ones. And the Part of the Father similarly aspects the ascendant or its lord from a square or opposition, it signifies that the native's father will abhor and hate him and will try to kill him. And if the Moon and the Part of the Mother aspect the ascendant or its lord, that abhorrence and malevolence towards the son will be from the mother. Hermes said that the fourth house is the pit of the planets because it is at the bottom of the celestial circle and in infirmity; and it is in a trine aspect to the twelfth house, which is the house of darkness, labors, anxieties, and prisons; and it is the joy of the greater infortune; and it is in a sextile aspect to the sixth house, which is the dark house of sickness and damages, the joy of the lesser infortune. When any planet is in the fourth house and in its fall, it is like a man suffocated in solitude until he comes out of it. Daly Abenragel says that when the Part of Fortune is unfortunate in a masculine sign, judge that the father will die before the mother. If in a feminine sign, the mother will die before the father. The Part of the Father is taken from the Sun to Saturn by day, and from the Moon to Saturn by night.

[Part of Mother and Father]
The Part of the Mother is taken in the day from Venus to the Moon, and at night the opposite, and it is projected from the Ascendant. If the lord of the Part of the Father is above the earth, and the lord of the Part of the Mother is below the earth, judge that the mother will die before the father. And if the contrary is true, judge the contrary. Daly Abenragel says that Albezen, son of Albezib, said: One day, when I was with Abolaben, and Meraefo was with him, a certain old man came to me and gave me a chart, in which was written the figure of a nativity. And he told me to look at that figure. And I asked him whose figure or nativity it was, and he replied that it was of a certain son of his. And while I was looking at it and thinking about it, Abolaben took it from my hand and looked at it for a while and said: "The first thing we see in this nativity is that this native is born of adultery, because he is not the son of him who says he is his son." I said, "How do you know this?" And he replied, "This old man says that this nativity is of his son, and the father of the native, whose nativity this is, died four years ago, and he died in the same year that the native was born." And I asked how he knew this. And he said: "I looked at the degree of the father and found it opposite the mother, and there was not more than one degree between them. And I found the Part of the Father in the second house from the Ascendant, which is the eighth from the fourth, and there was one degree between the Part and Saturn, for which reason I judged that the father of this native died in the year he was born. And this old man says that he is his son, therefore the native is illegitimate." And then the old man said: "I am not the father of this native, but he is the son of my son, and my son, his father, died in the same year of this nativity, as this good man said."

[The Fifth House]
The Fifth House. Here the author sets forth the significations of the fifth house. He says that this house signifies sons, both male and female. And it signifies affections and envoys or messengers and gifts. And what will happen after death, whether praise or blame. And Anduzga said that the first lord of the triplicity of the house of children signifies children and their life. The second signifies affections. The third signifies envoys or messengers. Ptolemy says, in the reasons for this house, that we should look at the planets existing in the place of the zenith of our heads, and at the place that follows it, which is the place of fortune, and at the place participating with them in the figure. Daly says in the commentary that the place which is the zenith of our heads is the tenth house. And the place that follows is the eleventh house, which is the house of fortune. And the rule by which we will know about children is taken from the planets existing in these places, or existing in places participating with them, such as the Ascendant and the seventh house, both of which participate with the tenth and eleventh. And if we find a planet in these places, we will look if we find any in the fourth or fifth house, and we will take the signification from there. Ptolemy says that we will judge the Moon, Venus, and Jupiter in giving children. The Sun, Mars, and Saturn in taking away, and we will give Mercury participation with whichever of these it participates with in the figure. Daly says in the commentary: If any of the fortunate planets are in the aforesaid places, it signifies that he will have children. If any of the unfortunate planets, he will have no children, and if he has any, they will be weak and few. And if Mercury has participation with the fortunate planets, it will be fortunate; if with the unfortunate, it will be unfortunate. Ptolemy says, and the opposition of the 144th part of the fourth part, you will be able to know the particular matters of children by considering, if you look well, in each of them, at the planet giving children, so that you place it in the place of the Ascendant, and you will know the other particulars of children generally, as by a nativity. Daly says in the commentary: What Ptolemy wants to relate in this place is what happened in my nativity. I looked and found Jupiter in the tenth house and in the 28th degree of Capricorn, aspecting itself with the Moon and Saturn, and this signified that I would have children and that they would die, because Saturn was with Jupiter in the tenth house. And because Jupiter was in a feminine sign, and the Moon likewise, it signified that there would be more than one, and that there would be more females. And because Jupiter was oriental, it signified that I would have a male. And so I had three children: one male and two females, and all died. The ascending degree of the male's nativity was around the degree of Saturn in my nativity, and because of this he died quickly. And the ascending degree of one female was in Pisces in the sextile of Jupiter in my nativity and in the trine of my Moon's nativity; and the Sun was hyleg in the sign of Capricorn. And the ascending degree of the other female was in Capricorn. And this is wonderful, for which reason it can be known that nativities always agree with each other. Hispalensis says, wishing to choose the hour for generating a male child: let Jupiter be in any angle, or let the Sun be oriental, and let the lord be male, and it is better that the ascending sign be masculine and also its lord. And if the Moon is fortunate by Jupiter, it will be better. For a female, take feminine signs and feminine planets, and let Jupiter be occidental. Daly Abenragel says: When there is any fortune in the fifth house, and the lord of the fifth house is free from misfortunes, and aspects the Midheaven, the native will have many children, and they will live and prosper. And if the contrary is true, it signifies the contrary. Look in all nativities: if you find the luminaries unfortunate, having no aspect, the native will have few children. In knowing the time when children will be had, look at the planet that has more dignities in the house of children. If you find it in the oriental part, he will have children in his youth. If you find it in the Midheaven, he will have them in the middle of his age. And if in the seventh, he will have them at the beginning of old age. If in the fourth, he will have them around the end of his life. Likewise, when the year comes to the sign in which Jupiter or Venus was in the radix of the nativity, he will have a child in that year. Daly Abenragel says: If you are asked about a woman, whether she is pregnant or not, look if you find the lord of the Ascendant and the Moon in the house of children; or if you find the lord of the house of children in the Ascendant, free from misfortunes, say that that woman is pregnant. And if the lord of the Ascendant or the lord of the house of children has given its strength to a planet existing in an angle. And likewise, if the lord of the Ascendant has been received by the one receiving it, say that she is pregnant. And if the lord of the Ascendant has given its strength to a planet falling from an angle, it signifies that she is not pregnant.

[The Sixth House]
The Sixth House. Here are set forth the significations of the sixth house. It says that the sixth house signifies infirmities and servants, and it signifies the end of life and what will happen in old age. Anduzga said that the first lord of the triplicity of this house signifies infirmities and their increase or deterioration. The second signifies household slaves and servants. Note the difference between a household slave and a servant. For a household slave is the same as a domestic, and is called a purchased servant. A servant is one who is of servile condition. As Adam said in verse:

[Sixth House and Critical Days]
The third triplicity of the sixth house signifies what good or evil may befall one from servants and the utility and work of animals. And with this, it is a significator of beasts and cattle and all quadrupeds that are not ridden. It signifies their multitude or scarcity and their strength, and how many will be in his hand and how many will depart from his hands. It also signifies prisons and detentions. Ptolemy says in the 60th proposition of Centiloquium: "Albobara, truly and certainly, are the hours in which the changes of diseases are declared for good or for evil, or quickly. And the places of the Moon in angles are excluded from the direct circle. The alterations that predict these and indicate them are the true places of the Moon in the angles of the almuten. Those that predict these are the places of the Moon in the angles of the 16th side. And if 15 days have passed since the beginning of the illness, and it is equal, and nothing external has happened to disturb the sick person, then if we find a fortune, whether from fixed stars or wandering stars, it will signify a prosperous alteration. But if it is an adverse alteration in fortune, unless the misfortune itself is contrary to the illness and in its hayz. The Moon in these angles signifies acute diseases, and the Sun signifies chronic diseases. And similarly, every planet according to its own customs. Haly in his commentary on the same says that Ptolemy taught us the number of critical days and what they are and who determines good or evil and alterations in order. The utility in this is greater for physicians than for astrologers, and this is because many philosophers agree on the determinations, saying that there are alterations and many things between the nature of the sick and acute diseases on the fourth day and the seventh day and the 14th day and the 21st day, and these increase according to what is accepted by mere hearing and doctrine without science. And they do not reason in this except by what has passed from their experiments. But Ptolemy said and revealed how it happens. And according to Ptolemy, it is that nature is overcome by the disease at its beginning and prevents it from performing its operations according to equality, nor does it resist the disease at the hour it conquers, but waits for the Moon to be in the first place in which it was at the beginning of the disease, because then the strength of those who move in it will not be as it was at the beginning of the disease. Then it is incited to resist it, just as a prudent actor does not act with a foolish accused when he wants to resist him, unless his strength has been weakened and in that place where he lacks helpers. And it excites that nature in the fourth sign from the sign in which the illness began, and the Moon being in that which is contrary to its nature from every fourth sign, and similarly the seventh, because these places, that is, the fourth aspect and the opposition, signify enmities and contrarieties. And the time that is between the beginning of the disease and the entry of the Moon into the degree of the square in which it was at the beginning of the disease, through the ascensions of the signs in the direct circle and the projections of the rays, is seven days. And in the same way, what is between the Moon at the beginning of the disease and itself in opposition is 14 days. And what is between the beginning of the disease and the second aspect which is contrary to the beginning of the disease is 21 days. And according to this method, the method of the other days proceeds. And these points will be the angles of the square which the line of the direct circle includes. And to those points, other points are indicative, and it is that the Moon reaches the point that cuts off each arc whose side subtends one of the sides of the square through the middle. And in these arcs are the sides of the figure having eight angles. And all these points are contrary to the points in which the disease began by nature. Therefore, the astrologer should observe whether in these points, both from fixed stars and wandering stars, whether they are fortunes or misfortunes. And if it is a fortune, it indicates that it signifies the victory of nature over cholera. Misfortunes, however, signify that cholera will overcome nature, unless the misfortune is contrary to the disease and strong in its hayz. For it will not make the Moon fortunate when it is in its hayz, but it will remove the disease by being contrary to it, and by the misfortune being contrary to the disease, as if it were cold and the disease hot, or if it were hot and the disease cold, and with these similar things in species of diversities. And he says that the Sun in chronic diseases is like the Moon in acute diseases, whose greater time will be the orb of the Moon, and in chronic diseases, the orb of the Sun. Ptolemy also subtly hints to us when he says that every star is according to its customs. Indeed, he taught us that whatever is immoderate in us and is in customs that we do not have, he calls a disease. And he said this is just, unless something external happens that disturbs the order of determination. And those who expounded the book of Hippocrates' Aphorisms spoke of the thing that destroys determination, and therefore it is not necessary for us to recite it in this book. The whole intention of Ptolemy and Haly stands in this, that the reason why the 4th, 7th, 14th, and 21st days are critical days is that the Moon frequently comes to the fourth aspect of the place in which it was at the beginning of the disease on the seventh day, and the Moon frequently comes to the opposite place on the 14th day, and frequently comes to the second fourth aspect on the 21st day. Therefore, Haly says that when the astrologer wants to judge a critical day, he should observe the time when the Moon will come to the fourth aspect of the place in which it was at the beginning of the disease, and if it then conjoins with benevolent planets or aspects them with a laudable aspect, or if it conjoins or aspects fixed stars that are of the nature of fortunes, it signifies that the crisis will be for good. And if it conjoins or aspects misfortunes, it signifies the contrary, unless the misfortunes are contrary to the matter of the disease and with this the misfortune is in its hayz, because then it can signify good, but this is by accident. For example, if the illness is phlegmatic and the Moon aspects Mars, it signifies good. And when the Moon reaches a good place whose side subtends the octagon in the equator, it will be an indicative day. The side of the octagon is 45 degrees, and it is half of the fourth aspect. And although it is not an aspect, it has a greater convenience with the aspect than other places. And therefore, when the Moon is in the fourth aspect, it should be conjoined with fortunes when it reaches the middle of that place, then nature feels relief and begins to rise against the matter of the disease by digesting it, and then signs of digestion appear in the urine, and sometimes a crisis occurs on the fourth day, that is, when the Moon finds a fortunate planet there. Then the signs of digestion should precede at the time when the Moon reaches the place whose side subtends 16 angles, and this is the middle of the octagon. Let these suffice concerning the causes of critical days. Ptolemy says in the 70th proposition of Centiloquium that when the Moon is in opposition to the Sun mixed with nebulous stars, it signifies inseparable diseases in the eyes. And similarly, if the Moon is occidental and in the angles, both malefics are occidental, ascending after the Moon, and the Sun is in the angle, and both malefics are ascending before the Sun and opposite to it, that is, one to the other, the native will lose both eyes. Haly says in his commentary on the same that the greater impediment in the two luminaries is when there are two malefics, that is, Saturn and Mars, ascending before the Sun and after the Moon, and one of them is in opposition to the other. And the Sun signifies the right eye, and the Moon the left. And it is inevitable that he will lose both eyes when it is so.

[Illnesses of the Spirit and Body]
The significator in his nativity is in this manner. Nebulous stars are like the Twins, and the place where the water that Aquarius pours falls, the drops of Leo, and others that do not shine. Daly Abenragel says in the reasons for this house, we first want to speak in this chapter about the occasions and accidents that occur in the spirit, which are illnesses of the spirit. Afterwards, we will speak about those that occur in the body, which are illnesses of the body. Then he says, I say that demons are those who do not have Mercury with the Moon in any aspect in their nativities, with none of them aspecting the Ascendant; and the stronger one in his nativity, if it is diurnal, is Saturn; if nocturnal, Mars. And whichever of them is in the angles, this is the nativity of demons. When the Sun is afflicted by infortunes or by the lord of the house of illness, and is above the earth in a diurnal nativity, or the Moon is in such an affliction below the earth in a nocturnal nativity, the native will suffer blindness in the right eye. And if this misfortune of the Sun is below the earth in a nocturnal nativity, or above the earth for the Moon in a diurnal nativity, this damage and blindness will be in the left eye. When the Sun and Moon are both in the sixth house, afflicted, the native will undoubtedly be blind. When Mercury is conjoined with Saturn or in his square or opposition aspect, or is cadent from an angle in a vile and unfortunate place, or is combust or retrograde, or peregrine in a mute sign, the native, from any of these significations, will have a damaged or mute tongue. When Mercury is the lord of the sixth house, or in opposition to Saturn, the native will be deaf. The greater and stronger signification of muteness is when the lord of the Ascendant and the lord of its exaltation, and the lord of its triplicity, and Mercury and the Moon are all in mute signs. When the Sun is unfortunate or afflicted below the earth, it signifies affliction of the stomach. And when the Moon is afflicted below the earth, it signifies affliction of the lungs. And if Mars is in this manner, it signifies affliction of the liver. And if Saturn is in this manner, it signifies affliction of the spleen. And if Mercury is in this manner, it signifies affliction of the gall. Ptolemy says in the 89th proposition of the Centiloquium that it is detestable in the signification of illness for the significator of the question to enter under the rays, or for the Part of Fortune to be unfortunate. Daly Abenragel says in the questions of this house, if you are asked about someone ill, whether he will recover or not: look at the Moon and the Sun and the almuten of the Ascendant; and if they are free from misfortunes and do not have an aspect with the lord of the house of death, I say he will escape from that illness. And if two of them are as we said, he will likewise escape. And if the Moon and the almuten of the Ascendant, especially if she is the lady of the time (i.e., if the question is nocturnal), have an aspect with the lord of the house of death, he will not be able to be freed from death. And whenever any of the significators applies to an infortune, the illness will be strengthened until it separates from it. The time of death will be when the almuten of the Ascendant or the Moon conjoins with the lord of the house of death, or with the infortune that afflicted it, or applies to its square or opposition aspect. Here he places the significations of the seventh house. The seventh house. And he says that the seventh house signifies women and marriages and conditions and oppositions. Anduzgam

[Marriage and Relationships]
He said that the first lord of the triplicity of the seventh house signifies women. The second signifies contentions. The third, participations and mixtures. Ptolemy says in the reasons for this house, it is fitting that I look at the state of the Moon in the nativity hour of the man for marriage, so that first I look at the Moon: if it is in the two eastern quarters, the man's marriage will be in his youth or he will marry a young girl after he has advanced in years. And if it is in the two western quarters, the marriage will be late or he will marry an old woman. And if the Moon is under the rays and participates with Saturn, he will never marry. And if it applies to Saturn, he will marry a laborious and wicked woman. And if it applies to Jupiter, the woman will be of good abstinence and good ornament. And if it applies to Mars, she will be bold and proud. And if it applies to Venus, she will be beautiful and of good reception. And if it applies to Mercury, she will be good, intelligent, and of good words. And it is fitting that I look at the marriage of women from the state of the Sun in her nativity hour, so that if the Sun is in the two eastern quarters, the marriage of the woman who has such a nativity will be in her youth or she will marry a young man after she has advanced in years. And if it is in the two western quarters, she will marry late or an old man after she has advanced in years. And if the Sun participates with Saturn, the husband will be of good law, a lover of labor. And if he has participation with Jupiter, he will be of good abstinence, noble of heart. If with Mars, he will be strong of heart without any love. If with Venus, he will be pure. If with Mercury, he will be proficient in his deeds and a doer of many things. Daly Abenragel says in the questions of this house: If someone asks you about marriage, whether it will happen or not, look at the Ascendant and its lord and the Moon and the planet from which it separates, and give these as significators of the querent; and the seventh house and its lord and the planet to which the Moon applies as significators of the one about whom the question is asked. And if the querent is male, conjoin the Sun with its significators and make it participate in the signification. And if the querent is female, give her Venus and make her participate in the signification. Afterwards, look at what kind of application the lord of the Ascendant or the Moon has with the lord of the seventh house, and what kind of application the planet from which the Moon separates has with the planet to which it applies, or Venus with the Sun. Therefore, if the lord of the Ascendant or the Moon applies to the lord of the seventh house, or the planet from which the Moon separates applies to the planet to which it applies, or the lord of the Ascendant or the Moon is in the seventh house, it signifies that the querent will have the thing sought, but with many petitions and prayers. And if the application is by square or opposition, it signifies that this will be with delay and labor and pain. But if the lord of the seventh house applies to the lord of the Ascendant, or the planet to which the Moon applies applies to the planet from which it separates, or the lord of the seventh is in the Ascendant, that thing will happen easily and with great willingness of the woman and her part, especially if that application is by trine or sextile. And if you find no application between the significators, it signifies that the thing will not happen. If someone asks you if he will fulfill his desire with a woman that night or not, look if you find Venus aspecting the Ascendant in the question. I say his desire will be fulfilled that night. And if the question is whether he had intercourse with that woman last night or not, judge this in the same way, no more and no less. If you are asked about a woman, whether she is a virgin or not, look at the Ascendant and its lord and the Moon, and if you find them in fixed signs, say that she is a virgin, safe from all blemish, pure. And if she is in common or mutable signs, say that she is a woman and has or had a husband. And

[On the Eighth House]
If the question is about a girl who says she is a virgin, say: she is corrupted and has had relations with others. If someone asks you about a woman, how many husbands she will have, look from the lord of the tenth house to the degree of Mars, and as many planets as you find between them, so many husbands she will have. And if Mars is in the seventh house, look from Mars to Jupiter in the same way and judge according to that, and you will be certain with God. Here are placed the significations of the eighth house. The eighth house is the house of death and fear, and it signifies inheritances of the dead which the heirs should possess after death. It also signifies the end of the years of life after old age. Anduzgamus says that the lord of the triplicity of this house signifies fear. The second signifies precepts and ancient things. The third signifies inheritances of the dead. Ptolemy says it is fitting that you look at the state of the degree of the killer, which planet is there or aspects it, and according to the nature of that planet will be the judgment of death. So if Saturn is the lord of death, it will occur due to long illnesses, due to consumption, namely rheumatism, and due to a defect of nature, etc., such things. And if Jupiter is the lord of death, death will be due to apostemata of the throat and lungs, etc., of this kind. And if it is Mars, death will be due to continuous and acute fevers. And if it is Venus, death will occur due to illness of the stomach and liver and heart, and by flux of blood and apostemata going through the body and fistulas. And if it is Mercury, death will be due to epilepsy and due to foolishness and loss of sense. Haly says in the commentary on the 15th proposition of the fourth part: Ptolemy divided death for us into two kinds: one comes from illnesses. The other comes from a thing in which the physician has nothing to see, such as one who dies by sword, spear, fall, fire, and bite of beast and wild animal, or drowning in water, and many other occasions. And when the governing planets are safe from misfortunes and in their own dignities and powerful, and when no contrary planet is elevated over them, then death will occur due to illnesses. But another death occurs when the planets are unfortunate or weak or in alien dignities contrary to them, or when contrary planets are elevated over them. To narrate all the ways in which death occurs would be too long here, and whoever wishes to find this will find it in the fourth part of Ptolemy's Quadripartitum. Ptolemy says in the 74th proposition of the Centiloquium: When Mars is corporally conjoined to the head of Algol and the Moon does not aspect the ascendant, nor is Fortune in the 8th house, and the lord of the anareta of the luminaries is opposite Mars or in its fourth aspect, the native's head will be cut off. But if the luminary is in the midheaven, he will be hanged. And if malefics aspect from Gemini and Pisces, his hands and feet will be cut off. Haly says in the commentary that when Fortune is in the eighth house, it prohibits a bad death. Indeed, I heard from someone who was with the very spirited son of Haly at sea, who, when he wanted to enter the sea, which was too tumultuous with winds agitating the waves, rebuked him, saying: I do not fear death at sea. For Jupiter was in my nativity in the house of death and oriental, which prohibits a bad death for me. And I saw him die in bed. It also happened to me that Adam's servants showed me the nativity of their lord's son, and I found the Sun in the midheaven, and he was the lord of the anareta and hylech, and Mars in his fourth aspect, and Saturn in the angle of his earth, the ascendant being Pisces. Therefore, terrified, I delayed giving judgment, saying: it is necessary that before I judge, the days of nourishment be completed. But when I was very solicitous about the boy, investigating his movements or deaths, I understood nothing from which I would fear for him the truncation of hands and feet and hanging, since he was gentle and modest. But when he reached 30 years, Adam's men entered the house, and fleeing, they were accused of fraud against the one who ruled the city, and they were caught in that house, and he with them lost his hands and feet and was hanged. And I saw him without hands and feet, hanged. Ptolemy says in the 59th proposition of the Centiloquium: when you are asked about an absent person, do not judge his death until you remove drunkenness from him, nor a wounded person until you remove bloodletting, nor acquired substance until you remove money entrusted to him. For the judgment is the same for these men. Haly says in the commentary there: he who deals with judgments judges by forms that are close to the truth. Therefore, there is no difference in the strength of judgments between a sleeping person and a dead person, and between a wounded person and a bloodletting person, nor between him to whom money is entrusted and him who acquired it. Indeed, I heard from my father, may God spare him, when he was with those who hid from the emperor's face, with Abraham, son of Almos, whom Albashten, son of Abraham, an astrologer, visited daily secretly, who advised him to bring a large bronze shell full of water, in which he placed a stool, and advised him to sit on it for the greater part of the day. And he advised this so that he might make the emperor's astrologers err in the matter of his hiding, and when the emperor asked his astrologers where he was, they said that he was in the middle of the sea. Haly Aberagel says that when Mars is in the eighth house, damaging the lord of the eighth house, the native's death will be by iron. And if Saturn is in the eighth house, damaging the lord of the eighth house, the native's death will be due to prison and punishments. When the Moon is in the eighth house with the Dragon's Tail, it signifies that the native's death is due to a secession or a laxative medicine. When Mercury is in the eighth house with the Tail, it signifies that the native's death will be due to evil deeds or due to poison or acts of necromancy. When the degree of the occident and its lord are both damaged, they signify a bad death for the native. When the Sun is damaged in a diurnal nativity or the Moon in a nocturnal nativity, it signifies the same. When the significators are damaged above the earth, they signify a manifest and open death. And when they are damaged below the earth, death will be hidden and secret. When any unfortunate planet is in the eighth house or conjoined to the lord of the eighth house, it signifies a strong and bad death. And if any fortunate planet is in the eighth house or conjoined to the lord of the eighth house, it signifies a good and beautiful death. And if Jupiter or Venus is in this house, strong and free from the rays of the unfortunate planets, the native will be fortunate and praised and will live 73 years, and perhaps more. Here are placed the significations of the ninth house. The ninth house signifies peregrinations and long journeys, and it signifies epistles and envoys and rumors and dreams. Anduzgamus says that the lord of the triplicity of this house signifies peregrinations and everything that happens to him in peregrinations; the second signifies faith and religion; the third signifies wisdom and

[The Tenth House]
Daly Abenragel says in the reasons for this house: look at the journeys of the native, and then at the lord of the triplicity of the house of journeys. For when the lord of the triplicity of the house of journeys is first in good state, strong, fortunate, and received, it signifies honors there through journeys, and he will move from one place to another and will be fortunate in journeys. And if he is in a state different from what we have said, he will have impediments and burdens in his journeys and movements, and he will be despised in them, and he will be extracted and expelled from his land and place, nor will he have any utility or profit in his journeys. And if the lord of the triplicity of the house of journeys is second, and is in good state, strong, and received, the native will be of good law, religious, and a keeper of the law. And if he is in a different state, he will be of bad law, will be called evil, and will be of evil works and incredulous. And if the lord of the triplicity is third, and is in good state, the native will be a truthful interpreter of dreams, and whatever he sees in dreams will be true and will not lie. The same Daly says: know that Mercury has power and proper signification in the cause of law and legality, separately from other planets. And know that if he is in the house of Saturn or in his aspect, the native will be of deep thoughts, firm in belief, praising the things of the other world more than this one, and believing them and thinking much about them and loving them, and holding that the things of that world are better than this one. He will abhor games, jokes, and comforts; humble and patient of labor and indigence, especially if the falling fortunes are not aspecting the ascendant. And if Mercury is in the house of Jupiter, or in his aspect, the native will be of good name, good law and legality, and will be an observer of the law. And if he is in the house of Mars, or in his aspect, and the same aspect is from the fourth or opposition, the native will be a murderer, irascible, a malefactor, of bad law, and will despise his law. The tenth house. Here he places the significations of the tenth house. It is the house of kingdom and sublimation and exaltation of memory and voice in command and magistracies and also of the mother. And it signifies the middle half of the house. Andugaz says: the lord of the triplicity of the tenth house. The first signifies the work of the native and his exaltation and the sublimation of his seat. The second signifies the voice of command and boldness in commanding. The third signifies its stability and durability, that is, how long it will last in its dominion. Ptolemy says in the 5th proposition of the Centiloquium: the ascendants of the enemies of the kingdom are those falling from the ascendant of the same, and the ascendants of those dominating in that angle of it. But the ascendants of the ministers are the succeeding angles. The ascendants of cities, however, in their constructions, judge all things that will happen in them. But the ascendants that are in the ordinances of kings of certain cities predict all things that will happen under their kingdom. And the ascendant of the appearance of any sect in those cities, namely, shows whatever will be under that sect in those cities. Daly says there in the commentary that the cadent signs are those of which there is no angle or after the angle; there are four: namely, the twelfth, third, sixth, and ninth from the ascendant. And he says that it is known to every astrologer that when the ascendant of a nativity, or any angle of it, is the ascendant or any angle of the inception of a kingdom, or of the nativity of someone to whom a kingdom is suitable, a kingdom will be perfected for him in that kingdom; and there will be honor for him in that, and not in another. Indeed, ancient kings observed the nativities of all born in their kingdoms, and whose ascendant they found to be the house of the enemies of the kingdom, or the sixth or third or ninth, they killed the child, because his kingdom would be against their kingdom. And after a few interpolations, he says that the ascendant of any city is the sign whose ascent begins when someone places the first stone in it. The ascendant of a sect is the ascendant sign at the time when that sect begins to prevail over another sect and the inhabitants have adopted it; and that signifies how long it will last, and what will happen in it as long as it lasts. Daly Abenragel says: when the sign of the midheaven is of the fiery signs, especially if it is Leo or Aries, and the Sun is in it, and the part of the king is there in the aspect of fortune, the native will undoubtedly be a king. The eleventh house. Here he places the significations of the eleventh house. He says that the eleventh house is the house of fortune, trust, and praise, and of friends and ministers and helpers; and it signifies the last half of middle life. Andugaz said: the lord of the triplicity of the house of trust, the first, signifies trust. The second signifies friends. The third signifies their utilities or profits. Ptolemy says in the 39th proposition of the Centiloquium: the evil of the eleventh house and its lord in the enthronement of kings signifies what will happen to his counselors and his substance from evil; and in the same way, the evil of the second will signify that the people will gain little with that king. Daly says in the commentary: astrologers have agreed on this: the tenth house in every ordination of kings is its place, and the eleventh is of his helpers and his substance, and the ascendant is of the people, and the second is of the substance of the people; and therefore the eleventh impedes the counselors, and the second the substance of the people. Daly Abenragel says in the reasons for this house: look at the lord of the triplicity of this house, the first. If you find him received, fortunate, and strong, indicate that the native will have many friends, gains, utility, and good from them. And if he is unfortunate and damaged, the native will be solitary among men, will not have friendship with anyone, and will withdraw and distance himself from those who seek his love and companionship. And if the lord of the triplicity of this house, the second, is strong, fortunate, and received, he will be fortunate, honored, and rich, abundant in good state and good life. And if he is different from this state, he will be laborious, and indigent, and manifestly poor and miserable. And if the lord of the triplicity of this house, the third, is fortunate, strong, and in good state, the native will have children who will remain after him in good state, and riches, and his fortune. And if he is unfortunate, weak, and cadent, and in bad state, the native will not have a son who remains after him, nor an heir of his generation. And know that the best state that can be in the cause of friends is that the lord of the ascendant is received by the lord of the eleventh house, the same lord of the eleventh house being fortunate and in good state. For when it is so, he will have love and agreement with companions and friends. The twelfth house. Here he places the significations of the 12th house. He says that the 12th house signifies enemies and labors, sadness and envy, and whisperings and cunning, and beasts that are ridden, and it signifies the end.

[Significations of the Twelfth House]
Anduzgar says that the first day of the triplicity of this house signifies enemies, the second signifies labors, the third great beasts. He concludes by saying: 'Best of all, it signifies.' Daly Abenragel says in the judgments of this house: 'Look first at the lord of the triplicity of this house. If you find him fortunate, strong, and elevated, judge that the native's enemies will lean upon him and do whatever they wish. But if he is cadent, afflicted, combust, or peregrine, the native will lean upon his enemies, and they will be hindered, and the evil they intended for the native will befall them. And if the lord of the triplicity of this house is fortunate, the native will have moderate sorrows and anxieties. But if he is in an adverse state, there will be many impieties and sorrows, and labors, impediments, and great losses will befall him in what he possesses and in his body. And if the lord of the third triplicity of this house is fortunate, the native will be dialectical and of good eloquence, and fortunate in his reasons and causes, and he will prosper against any adversary. But if he is in an adverse state, he will be weak in reason and impeded in speech, and he will have no right against his adversaries and evildoers.'

[House Colors and Planetary Joys]
The twelve houses also signify colors. Here are the significations of the houses as to colors: The first and seventh are white. The second and twelfth are green. The third and eleventh are yellow. The fourth and tenth are red. The fifth and ninth are the color of honey. The sixth and eighth are black. Afterwards, it says that each of the planets has an accidental power in some of these houses, which is called joy. Mercury rejoices in the Ascendant. The Moon rejoices in the third house. Venus in the fifth. Mars in the sixth. The Sun in the ninth. Jupiter in the eleventh. Saturn in the twelfth. Then it says that the angles signify strength, order, and perfection. Those cadent from the angles, however, signify weakness and detriment, except for the ninth and third houses. The third signifies a suitable thing, revealed with fame, and also that these are the joys of the luminaries, as it was already said that the Sun rejoices in the ninth and the Moon in the third. And the twelfth and sixth houses signify concealment and vileness of things. Afterwards, it says that the angles, namely the first house, the tenth, the seventh, and the fourth, and the lords of these angles, signify greatness of honor and fortune, and remoteness from fall and misfortune. And the presence of the lords of the angles in the cadent houses from the angles signifies misfortune and disgrace of falls. And the second house succeeds the tenth, and its lord signifies medium fortune, that is, it signifies fortune, but not as great as the tenth. And the fifth house succeeds the fourth, signifying medium fortune through gifts and the cause of children. And the eighth house and its lord signify medium fortune through the cause of ministers and helpers. And the eighth house and its lord signify medium fortune through the cause of inheritances from the dead and from hidden things.

[Lords of Angles in Angles]
Afterwards, it sets forth the significations of the lords of the angles when they are present in those angles. And it says that the presence of the lord of the Ascendant in the Ascendant signifies his fortune through himself and through his own acquisition. And if he is in the seventh, it signifies acquisition through wives. And if he is in the tenth, it signifies acquisition of magistracies. And if he is in the fourth, it signifies acquisitions through inheritances and through the cause of fathers and through the production of waters, the population of lands, and from ancient and radical things (another letter has 'and radical things'). The presence of the lord of the tenth in the tenth house signifies fortune through the king and great kingdom and high magistracies. And if he is in the seventh, it signifies kingdom through victory, contention, and through the cause of men. And if he is in the fourth, it signifies kingdom through the cause of the king's ministers and through the cultivation of lands and through the building of cities and the division of rivers and through the guardianship of cities and from ancient things. And if he is in the Ascendant, it signifies kingdom through ingenuity and through the king's ingenuity and from the things of the common people.

[Lords of Seventh and Fourth in Angles]
The presence of the lord of the seventh house in the seventh house signifies fortune through negotiations and through conventions and commendations, that is, deposits and through wives and through benefactors. And if he is in the fourth, it signifies fortune through conventions and negotiations and through the causes of fathers and inheritances and the cultivation of land. And if he is in the Ascendant, it signifies fortune through conventions and negotiations and through the causes of medicine and astronomy and through spiritual things and ingenuity and other similar things. And if he is present in the tenth, it signifies fortune through conventions and negotiations and through men and through the causes of the kingdom. The presence of the lord of the fourth house in the fourth house signifies fortune from fruit and through the causes of fathers and through ancient things. And if he is present in the Ascendant, it signifies fortune from the cultivation of land and fruit through depth of counsel and ingenuity; and if he is present in the tenth house, it signifies profit from the cultivation of land and fruit through the cause of kings and magistracies. And if he is present in the seventh house, it signifies fortune from the cultivation of land and fruit and from the part of the wife and through the cause of men and benefactors and through negotiations. Then it says that these things signify the lords of the angles when they are present in those angles. And as it was said about the angles, so you should understand about the other houses in their own way, according to the nature of each house. It says that it introduced the lords of the angles so that they might be an example in the other houses. When you wish to know the ruling planet, the author teaches how to choose the significator, and it can be divided into two parts: in the first part, it does what has been said. In the second part, it gives an example there. For example, the author's opinion is this: that in knowing the significator of a thing, we must look at two things. First, we must look at the house in which the nature of that thing whose significator we seek is located. Second, we must look at the planet that by its nature signifies that thing. For example, if a question is asked about substance, we must look at the second house, which is the house of substance; and with this, we must look at Jupiter, who by his own nature signifies substance. And if a question is asked about a woman, we must look at the seventh house, which is the house of a woman, and with this, we must look at Venus, who by her own nature is the significatrix of women. And so for others, according to the proper natures of the houses and planets. It is to be understood, however, that the planet we choose from the part of the house we must hold as the principal significator. And the planet that signifies the nature of the thing we must make a participant in the signification. Therefore, the meaning of the text is: when you wish to know the ruling planet or significator of a thing, look at which of the planets has more strengths in the house of the thing, from the strengths mentioned in the chapter on their strengths and dignities. And the one who abounds in the number of strengths, that one is the ruler or significator. And it is to be understood that in interrogations, the Ascendant or the first house is always attributed to the querent. The planet abounding in the number of strengths in the house of the thing about which the question is asked is the significator of the thing sought. The author gives an example in the text. And he says: if you have been asked about substance, and you wish to know which of the planets is the ruler or significator, and the second house, which is the house of substance, is, for example, the degree of Aries, because Aries is the house of Mars, Mars has strengths there. And it is the exaltation of the Sun, and therefore the Sun has four strengths by reason of that. And it is the triplicity of the Sun, and by reason of that, it has three strengths there; and it is the term of Jupiter, and by reason of that, it has two strengths there; and the face of Mars, and by reason of that, it has one strength there. Therefore, the Sun has seven strengths there, and Mars six, and Jupiter two. It is clear, therefore, that the Sun has more strengths there. And such a planet, that is, having more strengths, is called Almuten, that is, the victor. Therefore, the Sun in such a figure would be the significator of substance, and in the same way, it must be done for others.

[Accidental Planetary Powers and Hayz]
Also, concerning the accidental powers of the planets. Thus, the author first determined the essential dignities of the planets. Here he determines their accidental dignities, and he explains himself very briefly, saying that there is an accidental dignity of the planets called Hayz, and it is this: that a diurnal planet is above the earth by day and below the earth by night. And a nocturnal planet is above the earth by night and below the earth by day. And if a masculine planet is in a masculine sign and a feminine planet in a feminine sign, then that planet is in its Hayz, that is, in its similitude; and its strength will then be like the strength of a man in the place of his perfect gain of fortune. And if the exposition of the first part of Alchabitius's Introduction to the Art of Judgments of the Stars is complete. Someone asked about an absent person, whether he was dead or alive, and the Ascendant of the question was the 20th degree of Leo, and such a figure occurred. Question about an absent person, whether he is alive or not.

[A Horary Question on Life and Death]
In this question, I looked at the ascendant and its lord, and the Moon, for whom the question was asked. I looked and found the lord of the ascendant in the midheaven, which at first glance seemed to indicate prosperity. But because I found Saturn in the angular house of the East, near the angle, within two degrees, I doubted the life of that person, especially because the Part of Fortune was unfortunate there. Then I looked at the house of death and found Venus stronger there, that is, in the house of death, having more testimonies because of exaltation and triplicity. I looked at its place in the figure and how it related to the ascendant, to the lord of the ascendant, and to the Moon, and I found it aspecting the ascendant with a quartile aspect, and Saturn existing there with the same aspect, which made me doubt life even more. Then I looked at the Moon and found it oppressed under the Sun's rays; this was one sign of death. I also found the Moon separated from Venus, going to the conjunction of the lord of the ascendant, and it transferred the nature of the lord of the house of death to the lord of the ascendant. This was a more certain sign of death. From these, I concluded that the man for whom the question was asked was dead, and it was found to be so. And because Saturn, being in the ascendant, was the lord of the seventh house, signifying the wife of the person for whom the question was asked, and Venus, signifying death, aspected him, this signified that perhaps the deceased had committed fornication with the wife of the person for whom the question was asked. The second difference in the natures of the seven planets. This is the second difference of this book, in which the author determines the natures of the seven planets. And it can be divided into four parts: first, it determines the natures and properties of the seven planets. Second, it determines the order or principality of the planets in perceptions. Third, concerning the nature of the head and tail of the dragon. Fourth, it determines the order of the planets in the lordship of days and hours. The second part begins there: 'concerning the order of the planets'. The third there: 'the head of the dragon'. The fourth there: 'if there is any day'. The first part is divided into seven parts: first, it sets out the nature of Saturn. Second, Jupiter. Third, Mars. Fourth, the Sun. Fifth, Venus. Sixth, Mercury. Seventh, the Moon. Where the parts begin is clear in the text. First, it sets out the nature of Saturn and what it signifies from things and human customs and from sects and so on, all of which clearly appears in the text up to that part about the years of Fridaria. Concerning that part, it is to be understood when it says 'the years of Fridaria of Saturn are', it is to be understood as the year of governance in the life of the native. For the elucidation of this, it is to be known that in a diurnal nativity, Fridaria begins with the Sun and governs it for 10 years. Afterwards, Venus governs it according to the quantity of its years. Then Mercury: thus according to the order of the planets, going to the end of life. If, however, the nativity is nocturnal, the governance begins with the Moon and governs it according to the quantity of its years. After the Moon, Saturn governs it according to the quantity of its years, and so according to the order of the planets. There is a proper chapter on this in the fourth difference, and there it will speak more extensively about this, God willing. When it says in the text: 'the greatest', it is to be understood concerning the years that the planets give in the duration of things, namely in sects and in other great matters. When it says 'greater and middle and lesser', it is to be understood concerning the years that the planets give in the nativities of men for living: and as I say about Saturn, so you should understand about the other planets. Ptolemy says in the 82nd proposition of the first part that the greater and stronger work of Saturn is to cool and dry a little because of the strength of cold: and he sees this as being because it is very far from the heat of the Sun and the humid vapors of the earth. Albumazar refutes Ptolemy, and I will, God willing, present his reasons at the end of this part on the natures of the planets. Daly says in the commentary on the aforementioned proposition that Ptolemy means that Saturn performs this work because its work is very far from the work of the Sun, which is the work of heat, and from the Moon, whose work is to attract humors: because when he looked at the comparison of Saturn with the Sun and Moon, he found that it was contrary to both, and because of this, he said that it is fitting that it be cold and dry. And Ptolemy himself glossed this comparison in what follows. Ptolemy says that to know the virtue of this planet and others will be for the rectification of figures in respect to the Sun and Moon, because we see some of them changing the air in one manner of change and some of them in another manner in different arrangements of change, increasing and decreasing. Daly says in the commentary: 'If you remember what we told you by which I can prove the virtues of the stars, you do not need a gloss in this. And if you have forgotten this, listen. I tell you that the Sun and Moon, because their works are more apparent than the works of other stars, are more manifest to us: and the works of the remaining stars seem hidden: it is fitting that you look at the stars having commonality with the two luminaries through figures: that is, through aspects, whether they increase in their works or diminish from them: and so you will look at all of them: until you know the certainty of all, not once but many times. And if you find that they always follow one manner of operating, you will know for certain what kind of virtue they have.' Daly Abenragel says about the nature of Saturn: 'Saturn is an old, great, weary, despised planet of anxieties, sadness, and long illnesses. Its nature is cold and dry and it is assimilated to melancholy, which is governed by all humors, and none by it. When it is the almuten of a nativity, and it is in Cancer, the native will be of a very ugly face and a marvelous creature in its form and vision, so that all who see him and hear him spoken of will be terrified and amazed.' Alfraganus says that the body of Saturn is 91 times as large as the Earth. Jupiter is a masculine fortune. Here he sets out the nature of Jupiter, and what he says in the text is clear. 'The virtue of Jupiter, however, is of a temperate complexion, and its place of motion is median between the coldness of Saturn and the heat of Mars, and because of this, it happens that it heats and moistens.' Daly says in the commentary: 'Many believed, when they heard this word of Ptolemy, that the works of the stars, according to his opinion, followed the places of the spheres according to whether one existed above another, as believed by Hiza, Avenquiton, Alkindus, and others who hindered us with such reasons. But I say that the works of the stars are according to nature, how can quadrivial propositions be written, since the roots of these two sciences are diverse, one from the other. Furthermore, if all celestial bodies are not of any complexion: hot, humid, cold, nor dry, as Aristotle proved, how can Jupiter's complexion be temperate because its sphere exists between those of Mars and Saturn? For if you look closely at Ptolemy's statement, you will find that it is not as they believed. And after he taught us the way by which we might know the virtues of the stars, he puts this another way in this place, saying that since we have proven the mode of operation that operates in the air surrounding us, we have found it to be median between the great coldness that Saturn makes and the great heat that Mars makes, and this affirms what he said, that it heats and moistens.' Daly Abenragel says: 'Jupiter is the planet of equality, community, goodness, improvement, intellect, sense, and piety: it is temperate, equal, and a fortune. By aspect and bodily conjunction, it signifies goodness, improvement, law, simplicity, and chastity. It directs and does not condemn; it populates and does not destroy; it abhors Saturn and its natures. When God began to create the world, it was in the ascending house, shining in Aries, Taurus, and Gemini; and its light diminished in Cancer, Leo, and Virgo. It darkens in Libra, Scorpio, and Sagittarius; its darkening diminishes in Capricorn, Aquarius, and Pisces.' Alfraganus says that the body of Jupiter is 95 times as large as the Earth. Mars is masculine. Here he sets out the nature of Mars, and Mars properly dries and by the force of its nature burns because it has a fiery color, and because it is around the Sun, and because the sphere in which the Sun is placed is below it. Daly says in the commentary: 'Ptolemy means that the work of the virtue of Mars, that is, what we experience, we find to be of great dryness. To what he said, that the virtue of Mars burns because it has a fiery color, I say that the stars are simple substances and not composed of the natures of diverse elements: the appearance of their color is correct because there is nothing there that changes the color suitable to the same substance. Ptolemy, however, teaches us by this saying a rule by which we know the virtue of the stars, which we cannot understand by ourselves, and we can understand it.

[Mercury's Influence on Weather and Ptolemy's Theories]
of the planets signifying rains, and through it and through its change from sign to sign, and through its state, retrogradation, and direct motion, and its oppositions and conjunctions, they will know the movements of the winds and their strengths, whether they will be strong or weak in all parts of that year. For when it is in one sign and enters another, or when it is stationary or retrograde, it signifies strong winds, humidity, and rain, and in the air, disturbances from clouds and similar things. Similarly, that which is in opposition to the Moon, with the Moon existing in any of the watery or airy signs, signifies what is predicted. In the revolution of the years of the world, it has great and true significance over those holding offices of kings. Alfraganus says that the quantity of Mercury's body is one part of 32,000 parts of the Earth's body. A fortunate female nocturnal planet places the nature of the Moon. The meaning of the letter is clear. Ptolemy says the greater virtue of the Moon is to moisten, because it is very close to the Earth and because of the cold smokiness that is elevated by it. And because of this, manifest bodies change to such a state, for it causes bodies to change and putrefy for the most part. And it also has a small participation with the Sun in heat, because it receives light from it. Albumazar refutes Ptolemy on the cause of the natures of the planets, and his words are these: because many kings of Greece were wise after Alexander, son of Philip, and each of them was called Ptolemy; there were ten of them, and one woman; they reigned in Egypt; and the years of their reign were 275. All of them were wise, among whom was Ptolemy, who published the book Almagest on the cause of the motion of the circle and whatever is in it concerning the planets. And one of them published a book on the judgments of the stars, referring it to Ptolemy, the author of the book Almagest. It is said that he who published the book of judgments also published the book Almagest; the truth of this matter is unknown. But he who among them published the book of judgments narrated in his book the natures of the planets and their causes. He began to say that the Sun heats with sweetness and delay, and that its work in this is more evident and stronger than the work of the other planets because of its magnitude, and the more it rises to the zenith of our heads, the more its heat increases for us. And he thought that the nature of the Moon is humid because of the proximity of its circle to the Earth and because of the reception of vapors that rise from it. And he thought that the nature of Saturn is cold and dry because of the length of its circle from the heat of the Sun and its distance from the humidity of the Earth's vapors. And he thought that Mars' nature is hot and dry because its color is similar to fire, and it is near the Sun, and it is below it, and its heat rises to it and heats it. And he thought that Jupiter is of an equal complexion, because its circle is between the circles of Saturn and Mars. And for this reason, its nature is hot, humid, equal, and temperate. And he thought that Venus's nature is hot, humid, and equal. Its heat, however, is from the proximity of its circle to the Sun. Its humidity, however, is from the humid vapor that reaches it from the Earth. He thought that Mercury's nature is dry at certain times and humid at others. Its dryness is due to its proximity to the Sun and because it does not move far from it. Its humidity, however, is due to the proximity of its circle to the Moon's circle.
