This is what Ptolemy worked on regarding the natures of the planets, and this is the reasoning he used for it. But we will now say that there is something to be criticized in his words, that is, worthy of reprehension. For he thought that the Sun heats things with sweetness and delay, and he found this from his work. But what he said, that the nature of the Moon is humid because of the proximity of its circle to the Earth and the reception of vapors that rise from the Earth to it, this is refuted by the wise, because the space between the surface of the Earth and the nearest place where the Moon is, is 128,044 miles, approximately, by the measure that one mile is 1,000 cubits. And this is clear in the book in which the distances of the superior bodies from each other are narrated. And vapors do not rise more than 16 stadia from the Earth's surface, according to what Ptolemy narrated, which is 400 cubits; for 16 stadia make two miles and a tenth and a thirteenth of one mile, approximately. The length of the Moon, which is closest to the Earth's surface, is, as we said, approximately 128,044 miles. How then can the Earth's vapor reach the Moon so as to corrupt or change its nature? In a similar way, he refutes him on the natures of the other planets, but I pass over this for brevity. Daly, in his commentary on the aforementioned opposition regarding the nature of the Moon, refers to Albumazar's arguments. Daly, explaining Ptolemy's words, says: Ptolemy taught us that the virtues of the stars follow the magnitude of their bodies, and the Moon's body is small, as narrated in the Almagest, and its work follows the Sun's work in one part. He says here that this is because it is very close to the Earth, and its virtue reaches us quickly, and because of this, its work appears more than the work of other stars. And we see visibly that it attracts the humors of the Earth and the bodies that follow it, and because it has light from the Sun, it operates in earthly things with a moderate accidental heat, with which it causes the humors existing in bodies to putrefy and change, as shown in physics and in nature. And it is manifest that light causes heat, and this can be proven by mirrors that burn and similar things. And since the Moon has light from the Sun, it is fitting that it has a moderate heat, which it produces as if by accident. And this is what Ptolemy means to say. And because Albumazar did not understand this, he believed that he erred in his statement, saying, "How can humid smokiness ascend to the Moon when smokiness cannot ascend beyond 16 stadia, and the Moon is quite far?" I, however, laughed at such statements as these, and I said, "How did he not understand this?" For Ptolemy did not mean to say that humid smokiness ascends all the way to the Moon, but he said that the ascent of humid smokiness towards the Moon teaches us that it attracts the humors of the Earth and other bodies following it, just as a magnet attracts iron. Alfraganus says, on the authority of Ptolemy, that the magnitude of the Moon's body is one part of 39 parts of the Earth; and he says that the largest body of all bodies is the Sun, and after the Sun, the largest stars are 15. For he says that each of them contains the Earth 107 times. Third in magnitude is Jupiter, and fourth is Saturn. After Saturn are the fixed stars of the second order, each of which contains the Earth 90 times. After them are the stars of the third order, each of which contains the Earth 72 times. After them are the stars of the fourth order, each of which contains the Earth 54 times. After them are the stars of the fifth order, each of which contains the Earth 37 times. After them are the stars of the sixth order, and the smallest of them, indeed the smallest of all that are seen, the proof of which is placed.

[Planetary Distances and Rulerships]
The Earth contains 18. The largest body after them is Mars. After Mars, Earth. After Earth, Venus. After Venus, the Moon. And lastly, Mercury. It is clear, therefore, according to Alfraganus, that the largest of all bodies is the Sun, and the smallest is Mercury, with the exception of generable and corruptible things. Regarding the distances of these bodies from the Earth, Alfraganus says that the closest distance of the Moon from the Earth is 33 times the Earth's semi-diameter and 2/20 of it, which will be 104,120 miles. And the longest distance of the Moon, which is the closest distance of Mercury, is 64 times the Earth's semi-diameter and 7/6 of it, which is 208,542 miles. And the longest distance of Mercury, which is the closest distance of Venus, is 167 times the Earth's semi-diameter, which is 542,750 miles. And the longest distance of Venus, which is the closest distance of the Sun, is 1120 times the Earth's semi-diameter, which is 3,640,000 miles. And the longest distance of the Sun, which is the closest distance of Mars, is 1220 times the Earth's semi-diameter, which is 3,965,000 miles. And the longest distance of Mars, which is the closest distance of Jupiter, is 8876 times the Earth's semi-diameter, which is 28,847,000 miles. And the longest distance of Jupiter, which is the closest distance of Saturn, is 14,405 times the Earth's semi-diameter, which is 46,862,500 miles. And the longest distance of Saturn, which is equal to the distance of the fixed stars, and the quantity of the semi-diameter of the circle of the signs, is 20,110 times the Earth's semi-diameter, which is 65,357,500 miles. And when this is doubled, the quantity of the entire diameter of the circle of the signs, i.e., the eighth sphere, will be 130,715,000 miles. And when this is multiplied by 3 and 1/7, the quantity of the circumference of the circle of the signs, or of any other larger circle described in the eighth sphere, will be 410,818,570 miles. And the measure of each degree of the greater circle will be 1,141,160 miles. Regarding the order of the planets: Here he sets the order of the planets in the conception of children, namely, the order in governing the fetus as long as it is in the mother's womb. He says that Saturn governs it from the hour of conception until the end of one month. In the second month, Jupiter governs it. In the third, Mars. In the fourth, the Sun. In the fifth, Venus. In the sixth, Mercury. In the seventh, the Moon. And because of this, as he says, the child in the seventh month seeks to exit, because the operations of all the planets are completed in him; and those who are born then can live for the same reason. Then the governance returns to Saturn, and he governs it in the eighth month; and then those who are born do not live because of the malice of Saturn. Then Jupiter governs it in the ninth month; and then they commonly are born and live because of the goodness of Jupiter. Then he sets the order of the planets in the governance of the body after birth, as to the progression in ages; and he says that the Moon begins to rule the native from its entry into the world, and rules it for four years, which are the years of nourishment. Then Mercury rules it for ten years. Then Venus for eight. Then the Sun for nine. Then Mars for 15. After this, Jupiter for 12. Then Saturn until the end of life. The Dragon's Head has the nature of the Tail. Here he sets the nature of the Head and Tail of the Dragon.

[Planetary Day and Hour Rulers]
If there is any day. Here he sets the order of the planets as to the lords of days and hours. He says that if a day belongs to a planet, the first hour of that day, according to which the first hour begins from the rising of the Sun, belongs to that planet. And the second hour belongs to the planet that succeeds in the order of the heavens, descending. And the third to the third planet in order, and so on in order until the end of the 12 hours of the artificial day. And that planet to which the 12th hour belongs is the lord of that night. And to whom the 25th hour, i.e., the first hour of the following day, belongs, that is the following day. And the author gives an example in the text, so it is not necessary for me to give it. And thus the exposition of the second difference of this book is completed. And because, God willing, the third difference of this book, in which the author determines the being of the planets in themselves and their being in relation to each other, namely, one to another. And he divides it into two parts: because in the first he determines their being in themselves. In the second part, their being in relation to each other. The second is there: "Regarding their being in relation to each other." And he divides that into two: because first he determines the being of the five planets with respect to the luminaries. Second, their being among themselves. The second is there: "But first he determines their being in themselves." And the meaning of the text is this: Planets are sometimes said to be ascending and sometimes descending, and sometimes they are said to be increased in light and magnitude, and sometimes diminished in light and magnitude. And sometimes they are said to be increased in number, and sometimes diminished in number. And sometimes they are said to be increased in motion, and sometimes diminished in motion. And all planets except the Sun are said to be five northern and five southern. And they are said to be ascending and descending in the north and south. These are the things that happen to the planets in themselves. And the author explains these in order in the text, saying that a planet that ascends in its eccentric circle, so that it is in the upper part of its eccentric, not distant from the apogee by 90 degrees before or after, then its light appears less, and it also appears smaller in quantity, and its course is then slow as to the motion of the center of the epicycle. It is then said to be stronger. But when it is at one of the middle longitudes of its eccentric, i.e., distant from the apogee by exactly 90 degrees, then it is equal in light and magnitude and course, i.e., it is not said to be large or small in light or magnitude, and the motion of the center of the epicycle is equal to its mean motion. But when it is outside these places, namely, distant from the apogee by more than 90 degrees before or after, then it descends and appears greater in light and magnitude, and the center of the epicycle then moves faster than its mean motion. And when the equated argument of the planet is less than 180 degrees, namely, when the equation of the argument is added to the mean motion, then it is said to be increased in number. And if the equated argument is more than 180 degrees, i.e., when the equation of the argument is subtracted from the mean motion, then it is said to be diminished in number. But in the Moon, when the equation is added, it is said to be increased in number; when it is subtracted, it is said to be diminished in number. And when any of the three superior planets moves

[Planetary Motion and Latitude]
When a planet moves with more than its mean motion, it is called augmented motion. When it moves with less than its mean motion, it is called diminished motion. The same applies to the Sun and Moon. When it moves exactly with its mean motion, it is called equal motion. When Venus or Mercury moves faster than the Sun, it is called augmented motion; when slower, it is called diminished motion. When any of the six planets crosses the node of intersection of its deferent with the ecliptic, which node is called the ascending node, it is northern and ascending, meaning it increases in latitude until it is 90 degrees from the intersection. When it is more than 90 degrees from the intersection, it is northern and descending, meaning it decreases in latitude until it is 180 degrees from the intersection, and then it is at the opposite intersection of the first and has no latitude, meaning it is in the ecliptic. When it crosses that, its latitude becomes southern, and it is southern and descending until it is 270 degrees from the first intersection. When it crosses this number, it is southern and ascending until it returns to the first intersection where its latitude will be zero. This is the meaning of the letter regarding the state of the planets in themselves. Their state relative to each other will be discussed and determined later. First, it determined the state of the planets in themselves, then the state of the five planets with respect to the luminaries. And it is divided into four parts according to the four states that the planets have with respect to the Sun and Moon. The first is face-to-face vision. The second is security. The third is combustion. The fourth is oriental and occidental. Therefore, it first determines face-to-face vision. Second, security. Third, combustion. Fourth, oriental and occidental. The first part is in the first. The second begins there: and from this guidance. The third there: and every planet. The fourth there: and from which the higher ones. The meaning of the first part is: When any planet is occidental to the Sun, that is, it rises after the Sun's rising, and there are as many signs between it and the Sun as there are between the house of that planet and Leo, which is the house of the Sun, such a planet is said to be in face-to-face vision with the Sun. For example: Capricorn is the house of Saturn and is the sixth sign from the house of the Sun, that is, Leo. Therefore, when Saturn is in the sixth sign from the Sun, counting the number of signs from the Sun towards Saturn according to the order of the signs (otherwise it would not be occidental if not counted in this way), then it is said to see it face-to-face. And the sign of Sagittarius is the fifth from Leo. Therefore, when Jupiter is in the fifth sign from the Sun, starting from the Sun towards Jupiter according to the order of the signs, it is said to see it face-to-face, and so on for others. And when any planet is oriental to the Moon, and there are as many signs between it and the Moon according to the order of the signs as there are between the house of that planet and the house of the Moon, that is, Cancer, then it is said to be in its face-to-face vision. For example: Cancer is the sixth sign from another house of Saturn, that is, Aquarius. Thus, when the Moon and Saturn are in the sixth sign, there is face-to-face vision between them. And also Cancer is the fifth sign from the house of Jupiter, that is, Pisces. Thus, when the Moon is in the fifth sign from Jupiter according to the order of the signs, there is face-to-face vision between them, and so on for others in their own way you can exemplify. From this, the guidance of the planet. Here it is determined concerning the second state of the five planets with respect to the luminaries, that is, concerning guidance, which is the same as security. And the meaning is this: when any planet is in its own term and in one of the angular houses (the ascendant, or the 10th, or the 7th, or the 4th house), and one of the luminaries is in one of the angular houses from that planet, so that the planet is oriental to the Sun by day and occidental to the Moon by night. This means that by day it is in the 10th sign from the Sun, for then it is in an angle from the Sun and oriental. Or by night it is in the 4th sign from the Moon, for then it is in an angle from the Moon and occidental. Then it is said to be in its guidance. The angle of opposition does not apply here. The reason is that a planet existing in opposition to the Sun or Moon is neither oriental nor occidental. Afterwards, it says that every planet, from the time it is hidden beneath the Sun's rays until the time it begins to appear, is called combust. And it begins to be combust when it begins to enter the rays. And when it comes near the Sun, within 12 degrees, it is called oppressed. When it is with the Sun in the same degree, and there is less than the Sun's semidiameter between them, and with this the planet's latitude is less than the Sun's semidiameter, it is said to be united or incorporated with the Sun. And when it has passed this union, it is said to be in convalescence until it is freed from the Sun's rays. From which the three higher ones appear. Here it determines the oriental and occidental nature of the planets. It says that the three superior planets, when they emerge from beneath the Sun's rays and begin to appear in the morning before the Sun's rising until they come to the opposition of the Sun, this means that they are closer to the eastern horizon circle than to the western. When the Sun is in the line of midnight, then they are called oriental and dexter. They are called oriental because they rise before the Sun, and they are called dexter because they are in the right part of the sky from the Sun. For the western part is right and the eastern is left. For if a man turns his face towards the south, it is clear that the east is to his left and the west to his right. And when any of the three superior planets has passed the opposition of the Sun, it is called occidental sinister. It is called occidental not because it is in the western part of the sky from the Sun, but the opposite is true. But it is called occidental because it sets after the Sun. And it is called sinister because it is in the eastern part of the sky from the Sun, which is left as stated. Venus and Mercury, each of them, within the time in which it circuits its epicycle, conjoins the Sun twice. Once by direct motion, that is, in the superior part of the epicycle. Another time by retrogradation, that is, in the inferior part of the epicycle. Therefore, when any of them separates from the conjunction of the Sun in the middle of retrogradation, that is, in the inferior part of the epicycle, it recedes from the Sun towards the western part of the sky. And when it has moved away from the Sun as much as it can be seen, it is seen in the morning before the Sun's rising. Therefore, then it is called oriental dexter until it is combust by the Sun, that is, until it joins the Sun in the superior part of the epicycle by direct motion. And when it has separated from the Sun by direct motion, it is seen in the evening after the Sun's setting. Therefore, then it is called occidental sinister until it is again combust. And there is a difference between Venus and Mercury and the three superior planets. For Venus and Mercury, sometimes in their recession from the Sun, or in their emergence from beneath the rays, they are oriental, and when they emerge from beneath the rays, they are occidental. But the superior planets, always when they emerge from beneath the Sun's rays, are oriental. And they are said to increase in magnitude until they are 30 degrees from the Sun. And from 30 to 60, they are called strong. And after 1

[Planetary States and Interactions]
When they are elongated from the Sun beyond 60 degrees, they are called oriental, going to debility until the beginning of retrogradation. And from the beginning of retrogradation until the opposition of the Sun, they are called oriental retrograde. And from the opposition until direct motion, they are called occidental retrograde. And from direct motion until 30 degrees after direct motion, they are called occidental strong. And from 30 degrees after direct motion until they come within 30 degrees of the Sun, they are called occidental, going to debility. And afterwards, they are called occidental weak until they are combust. Venus and Mercury, when they separate from the Sun by retrogradation, become oriental and are called weak until they come to direct motion; and from direct motion until they are elongated from the Sun as much as they usually are at the beginning of retrogradation, they are called oriental strong. Then they become weak oriental until they are oppressed under the Sun's rays; and afterwards, they are called united with the Sun; then combust, going to appearance; and from their appearance until their elongation from the superior part of the epicycle by 60 degrees, they are occidental strong; and from this place until retrogradation, they are occidental, going to debility; and afterwards until conjunction, they are occidental weak. If you do not understand this, it is false, since it is not possible for them to be elongated from the Sun up to 60 degrees in the zodiac. Afterwards, it says that when a planet emerges from under the Sun's rays and is not conjoined to any other body or aspect, it is in its own light. This is about their interactions with each other. Previously, it discussed what happens to planets in themselves and what happens to planets in relation to the luminaries. Here, it determines what happens to the seven planets in relation to each other. And it can be divided into as many parts as there are modes of interaction that happen to planets with each other. And it can be reduced to 16 modes according to the meaning of the text, which are: conjunction, void of course, swiftness, slowness, translation of light, return of light, prohibition, pulsation of nature, reception, return of nature, refranation, frustration, cutting off of light, veneration, destruction, obsession, love, and hatred. The author explains these in the text in order until the end of this difference. The meaning of the first part is this: Conjunction is when two planets are in two signs that aspect each other with some aspect, and the lighter (i.e., faster in motion) of them has passed fewer degrees from its sign than the heavier (i.e., slower in motion) from its sign, so that this difference is 6 degrees or less. And then it is said that the lighter goes to the conjunction of the heavier. For example: I assume that the Sun is in Aries and has passed 6 degrees from Aries, and Mars is in Leo and has passed 12 degrees from it. These two signs aspect each other with a trine aspect. And the Sun, which is faster in motion than Mars, has passed fewer degrees from Aries than Mars from Leo, and they are within a difference of 6 degrees. In the proposed example, the Sun goes to the conjunction of Mars by trine aspect. And if the Sun were in the 12th degree of Aries, and Mars in the 12th degree of Leo, then the conjunction would be complete. And if the Sun were beyond the 12th degree of Aries, with Mars existing in the 12th of Leo, then there would be a separation between them. And this is called a conjunction of longitude. Conjunction of latitude, however, is when two planets are in one sign, corporally conjoined, and are of equal latitude from the ecliptic, so that the latitude of one is ascending to the north and the other descending to the north, or one ascending to the south and the other descending to the south. Or if there is a conjunction from some aspect, and the latitude of one is northern ascending, and the other southern ascending. For example: I assume that the Moon is conjoined to Saturn in some sign, and in some degree and minute of it, so that Saturn is near its genzabar, going north in latitude, and its latitude is 3 minutes, and the Moon approaches the Dragon's Tail, coming from the north, decreasing its latitude, so that its latitude is similarly 3 minutes. This is a very true conjunction as to longitude and latitude. And in this case, the Moon would eclipse Saturn, unless the diversity of the Moon's aspect were so great as to impede it. Although the author says that the latitude of one should be ascending and the other descending, it seems to me that in a corporal conjunction, in every case where it can happen that the latitudes of both are equal to the same part (I mean that both latitudes are northern or both southern), there will be a true conjunction of latitudes; and in an opposition aspect, if the latitudes are equal in different parts, so that one is southern and the other northern, there will be a true aspect as to latitudes. And when one planet separates from another. Here it places void of course. It says that when a planet has been conjoined to another by body or aspect, and after separating from it, it does not conjoin to any other by body or aspect as long as it is in that sign, then it is said to be void of course. For example: I assume that the Moon joins Jupiter corporally in Sagittarius; and after its separation from Jupiter, there is no other planet in Sagittarius to which it can be conjoined, nor the rays of any other that it can aspect. In this case, the Moon is void of course until it leaves Sagittarius and joins another by body or aspect. And if a planet is in some sign. It says that when a planet is in some sign where no other planet is, nor the rays of any other, that planet, as long as it remains in that sign in such a state, is said to be feral, or wild, in the likeness of a man having no society with anyone. And when it has separated. It says that when a faster-moving planet has separated itself from a slower-moving planet, and in separating from it, it joins another, then it transfers the nature of the first to the second. For example: I assume that the Moon separates from a corporal conjunction of Jupiter; and before the separation is complete, it conjoins Saturn by some aspect, or corporally. The Moon then transfers the nature of Jupiter to Saturn. Translation also occurs in another way, namely, when a light planet conjoins a heavier one, and that heavier one conjoins another still heavier one, then the middle one transfers the nature of the light one to the heavier one. For example: I assume that the Moon aspects Jupiter with some aspect, and Jupiter aspects Saturn. Jupiter in this case transfers the nature of the Moon to Saturn. But if it does not conjoin two planets. It says that when they are in this way...

[Return of Light]
Suppose that one of them is not joined to the other, but both are joined to some third planet. Then, if that third planet aspects some place in the circle, it projects the light of those two to that place. And if any planet is in the place of its rays, it returns to it the light of those two. For example, I assume that the Sun is in Capricorn and Venus in Pisces, so that they do not aspect each other. Then I assume that Mars is in Cancer, aspecting the Sun by opposition and Venus by trine. In this case, Mars receives the light of the Sun and Venus, and returns their lights to the places of the circle where the rays of Mars are. This is called the return of light. The return of light also occurs in another way when two planets do not aspect each other, but a third planet transfers the light of one to the other, so that it separates from one and joins the other. Then it is the same as translation. Next follows prohibition. It says when three planets are in one sign, but in different degrees, and the one that is slower in motion has traversed more degrees of that sign than either of the other two, then the middle one prohibits the conjunction of the lighter with the heavier. For example, I assume that Saturn is in the 12th degree of Virgo, and I assume that Mars is in the 5th degree of the same Virgo. In this case, Mars seeks the conjunction of Saturn. But I assume that the Moon is in the 8th degree of the same Virgo. In this case, it would not be judged that Mars would be conjoined to Saturn, because the Moon is in the middle and prohibits its conjunction. Prohibition also occurs in another way: so that two planets are in one sign and the lighter one joins the heavier one, and another planet aspects the same heavier one, and its aspect is as close as the bodily conjunction of the other. Then the one that is corporally joined prohibits the aspecting planet from aspecting. And if in this case one of them is closer than the other, the one that is closer obtains and is said to join the heavier. For example, I assume that Saturn is in the 12th degree of Virgo, and Mars in the 8th degree of the same. And I assume that Jupiter projects its rays to the 8th degree of Virgo. In this case, Mars prohibits the aspect of Jupiter. But if Jupiter projected its rays to the 9th degree, it would be judged that Jupiter would aspect Saturn, and with this, it would prohibit the conjunction of Mars. And if Jupiter projected its rays to the 7th degree, it would be judged that Mars would be joined to Saturn, and with this, it would prohibit the aspect of Jupiter. And if a planet joins the lord of that sign, it says when any planet is joined by aspect to the lord of that sign in which it is, or to the lord of exaltation, or triplicity, or term, or face, it is said to send the nature of the lord of that dignity to the one whose dignity it is. For example, I assume that the Sun is in Capricorn, aspecting Saturn existing in Virgo. In this case, the Sun is in the house of Saturn and sends the nature of Saturn itself to Saturn. And if a light planet is in some place where it has some dignity, for example, that it is its house or exaltation, etc., and it aspects some heavier planet that has no dignity in its place, it says the light one sends its strength to the heavier. For example, I assume that the Moon is in Taurus, that is, in its exaltation, and aspects Saturn existing in Virgo by trine. In this case, the Moon sends its nature, which is virtue, to Saturn itself, although Saturn has no dignity in the place of the Moon. But if Saturn has dignity in the place of the Moon, for example, I assume that the Moon is in the 24th degree of Taurus, in its exaltation and in the term and face of Saturn, and aspects Saturn, it sends its own nature and the nature of Saturn by reason of its term and face. And when there are some of its dignities, it says a lighter planet aspects a heavier one, and the lighter one has dignity in the place where it is, and the one it aspects also has some dignity there, then the light one sends both natures to the heavier, that is, its own and that of the one it aspects. And this sending is called reception. For example, I assume that the Sun is in Aries in its exaltation and in the house of Mars, and aspects Mars by some aspect. In this case, the Sun sends its own nature to Mars, and with this, the nature of Mars by reason of its house, and Mars receives the Sun from its house. And if it happens that the inferior is in the dignity of the superior, and the superior in the dignity of the inferior, that is the best reception that can be. For example, let the Sun be in Aries in the house of Mars, and Mars in Leo in the house of the Sun, and the Sun aspects Mars by a trine aspect. Such reception is complete and perfect. Hence follows the return. Here it is affirmed that the planet that aspects the one it aspects is combust under the rays, or retrograde. In this case, the superior returns to the inferior the virtue it sent to it, because due to its weakness it cannot retain it. And if in such a case both are in an angle or in a succedent house, then the return is with profit. And if the inferior is in an angle and the superior is not, so that the superior receives the inferior, such a return is also with profit. And if the inferior is cadent from an angle and the superior is in an angle, the return is with profit. And if both are cadent, the return is with detriment. For example, I assume that the Moon is in Taurus and aspects Mercury existing in Capricorn, combust. In this case, the Moon sends its nature to Mercury. But because Mercury is combust, it cannot retain the nature sent to it, and returns that light which it receives from it. And if in this case both are in angles, the return is profitable, etc. Next follows almuten. It wants to join the superior, but before the conjunction is completed, the inferior becomes retrograde. This is called refranation. For example, I assume that Saturn is in the 2nd degree of Virgo, and Venus is at the beginning of Virgo, going to the conjunction of Saturn. But when Venus reaches the 8th or 9th degree, that is, before it reaches Saturn, it begins to retrograde. In such a case, Venus is refranated so that it does not join Saturn. And understand the same for an aspect if it were going to an aspect, but before the aspect was completed, it began to retrograde. Next follows alchoborad, that is, contrariety. It says that contrariety is when three planets are in one sign, of which one is heavy, and the other two are light, so that one of the two light ones has passed the heavy one, and the other seeks the conjunction of the heavy one. But before it joins the heavy one, the one that has passed the heavy one becomes retrograde, and joins the heavy one by retrogradation, and meets the other light one, and being retrograde, it destroys the conjunction of the one it meets with the heavy one. For example, I assume that Saturn is in the 8th degree of Virgo, and Mars is in the 12th degree of the same, and Jupiter is at the beginning of Virgo, seeking the conjunction of Saturn. But before it joins it, Mars begins to retrograde and joins Saturn by retrogradation and meets Jupiter.

[Frustration and Abscission of Light]
In this case, Mars destroys the conjunction of Jupiter with Saturn. This is followed by 'alphariz', that is, frustration. Frustration is when a light planet seeks a conjunction with a heavy planet, but before the conjunction is completed, the heavy planet enters another sign, and there are rays of some other planet at the beginning of that sign. Then, when the light planet, wanting to conjoin with the heavy one, enters that sign, it conjoins with the rays of that planet aspecting there, and thus the first conjunction is annulled. For example, I assume that Saturn is in the 29th degree of Leo, and Mars is in the 24th degree of the same sign, seeking a conjunction with Saturn. But before Mars conjoins Saturn, Saturn enters Virgo, and I assume that Jupiter aspects the first degree of Virgo. In this case, Mars, leaving Leo, conjoins with the rays of Jupiter, and thus the conjunction of Mars and Saturn is annulled. This is also followed by the abscission of light. It is said that the abscission of light occurs when a light planet seeks a conjunction with a heavy planet, and in the second sign from the heavy planet's sign, there is another planet. But before the light planet can conjoin with the heavy one, the planet in the second sign becomes retrograde and conjoins with the heavy one. In such a case, the retrograde planet cuts off the light of the heavy planet from the planet that wanted to conjoin with it. This is almost the same as 'prietas', but it differs in this: in 'prietas', the retrograde planet not only conjoins with the heavy one but also conjoins with the light one that wanted to conjoin with the heavy one by opposition, and it can be exemplified as was said there. Abscission of light also occurs in another way, namely, when a light planet seeks a conjunction with a heavy planet, and that heavy planet seeks a conjunction with another heavier planet and conjoins with it before the light planet conjoins with the first heavy one. For example, I assume that Mars seeks a conjunction with Jupiter, and Jupiter seeks a conjunction with Saturn, and before Mars conjoins Jupiter, Jupiter conjoins Saturn. In such a case, Saturn cuts off the light of Jupiter from Mars. There are also these planets. Planets are strengthened and in some places weakened, and in some places they become fortunate, and in some places unfortunate. They become fortunate in a sextile or trine aspect of benefics, and they are fortunate when they are cadent from them, according to what is to be understood: that when any planet is in the same sign as another, or in the fourth, seventh, or tenth from it, it is said to be in an angle from it. And if it is in the second sign from it, or in the fifth, eighth, or eleventh, it is said to be in a succedent from it. And if it is in the third sign from it, or in the sixth, ninth, or twelfth, it is said to be cadent from it. They also become fortunate when they separate from one benefic and conjoin with another, or when they are between the rays of two benefics, and this is called 'veneratio' by some. They also become fortunate when they are united with the Sun in the same degree, or when they are in its trine or sextile aspect, or in the trine or sextile aspect of the Moon, and also when they are increased in number and light, and when they are in any of their dignities or in their hayz. And planets become stronger when they ascend in the circle of their apogee, and when they are northern or ascend in the north. Similarly, they are strengthened when they are in the second station, going direct. Similarly, when they emerge from under the Sun's rays, when they are in angles or succedents. And the three superior planets are strengthened when they are oriental. And if they aspect the Sun with a sextile aspect, their strength increases. Similarly, when they are in masculine quarters or in masculine signs. The strength of the Sun also increases in masculine quarters and in masculine signs, except in Libra. For there it is not strengthened because of its fall from exaltation, even though Libra is a masculine sign and also in a masculine quarter. And the three inferior planets, namely those existing below the Sun, are strengthened when they are occidental to the Sun and in feminine quarters and in feminine signs. And the Moon is strengthened when it is above the earth at night, and below the earth during the day, and when it is in a feminine sign and place, and when it is in the exaltation of the Sun, namely in Aries. Regarding the misfortune of planets, know that planets are unfortunate, that is, they are made unfortunate, when they are in the aspects of malefics, and when they conjoin with malefics by body or by aspect, so that between them and the body of the malefic, or between them and the rays of the malefic, there is less than the term of one planet. And they are made unfortunate when they are in the terms of malefics or in the houses of malefics. For example, Jupiter or Venus is made unfortunate in the terms of Saturn and Mars, and in their houses. And they are made unfortunate when malefics are elevated above them, so that the malefics are in the tenth or eleventh sign from them. According to what is to be understood, a planet existing in the tenth sign from another is said to be elevated above it, just as one existing in the tenth house is elevated above the ascendant; and if this happens without reception, it is worse. For example, I assume that Jupiter is at the beginning of Sagittarius and Saturn is at the beginning of Virgo. In this case, Saturn is elevated above Jupiter. For Virgo is the tenth sign from Sagittarius. They are also made unfortunate when they are in conjunction with the Sun, or in opposition to the Sun, or in its quartile aspect. They are also made unfortunate when they are in the heads of their 'genzabar', that is, in the intersections of their deferents with the ecliptic, whether in the head or tail of the dragon, or near these places by 12 degrees or less, especially if in these places the Moon is impeded by them, or the Sun, that is, if the Moon or Sun conjoins them in these places or aspects them with a hostile aspect. The reason why they are made unfortunate in these places is because they can be eclipsed there. They are also made unfortunate when they are distant from the Sun by four degrees before or behind. And when they are between the bodies or rays of two malefics, so that they separate from one malefic body or aspect and conjoin with another malefic; or if a malefic or its rays are in the sign before it, and another malefic or its rays are in the sign after it. Then it is said to be besieged. For example, I assume that Jupiter is in Virgo and in the second degree, and Mars or the rays of Mars are in the tenth degree of the same sign, and Saturn or Mars are in the twelfth degree of the same sign. In this case, Jupiter would be said to be besieged by two malefics. In the same way, it is said of signs that they are besieged when one malefic is at its beginning and another at its end. But if the Sun, as a benefic, aspects a besieged planet or sign with a sextile or trine aspect, so that the aspect is within 7 degrees or less, then by such an aspect the siege is resolved. They are also made unfortunate when they are retrograde or combust or cadent from angles. And they are weakened when they are slow in course, so that they move less than their mean motion. And when they are in the first station, going to retrogradation; or when they are in dark degrees; or masculine planets in feminine signs or degrees, and during the day below the earth and at night above the earth; or feminine planets in masculine signs and in degrees.

[Debilitation of Planets]
Masculine planets are debilitated when they are above the earth during the day and below the earth at night. This is contrary to their nature and similarity. They are debilitated or unfortunate if they are in places opposite to their dignities, or if they are in southern latitude from the ecliptic, especially if they are descending in the same latitude, or if they are in via combusta (from the middle of Libra to the middle of Scorpio), or if they are conjoined with a retrograde planet, or a falling planet, or if they are not received. The three superior planets (Saturn, Jupiter, and Mars) are debilitated when they are occidental to the Sun, or in feminine quarters. The Sun is debilitated in feminine signs and quarters, unless it is in the ninth house, which it enjoys. The three inferior planets (Venus, Mercury, and the Moon) are debilitated in masculine signs and quarters. It is said of the planets that some of them love each other, and some hate each other, as will be shown below. Thus is completed the exposition of the third difference of Alchabitius's Introduction to Judgment. The fourth difference is the exposition of the names of astrologers. In the differences of this book, the author determined the essential and accidental being of the circle of signs in the first difference, and the natures of the seven planets in this difference, and what happens to the seven planets in themselves and to each other in the third difference. The fourth difference follows, in which he explains the names used by the masters of judgments and teaches how to apply them to practice. This entire difference can be divided into 16 parts, according to the 16 chapters he places in it. In the first chapter, he speaks of the great conjunctions, enumerating them. In the second chapter, he teaches how to investigate the ascending degree of a nativity. In the third chapter, he teaches how to choose the place of life in nativities. In the fourth chapter, he teaches how to choose the giver of years of life in nativities. In the fifth, he teaches how to choose the planet ruling the nativity, which presides over the native after hyleg and alcochoden. In the sixth, he treats the perfection of the years of the nativity and the world. In the seventh chapter, he teaches how to direct any significator to any place of the circle. In the eighth, he teaches how to direct the ascending degree in nativities. In the ninth, he teaches how to find the duodenaries of the planets and houses. In the tenth, he teaches how to find the novenaries. In the eleventh, he teaches how to find the decans. In the twelfth, he teaches how to find the half-orbits or hours. In the thirteenth, he teaches how to find the years of the firdaria in nativities. In the fourteenth, he teaches how to know which planet is elevated above another. In the fifteenth, he teaches how to find when the opening of the gates occurs. In the sixteenth, he speaks of fortunate and unfortunate men, where the beginning will be evident in the text. Therefore, in the first chapter, he speaks generally of the great conjunctions, saying that great conjunctions are things signifying destructions or changes that occur in the world, and there are six in number. The first, greater than all conjunctions, is the conjunction of Jupiter and Saturn at the beginning of Aries, and this occurs once every 960 years. The second conjunction is the change of the conjunction of Jupiter and Saturn from one triplicity to another, and this occurs once every 240 years. And when their conjunction comes to another triplicity, before it occurs twelve times, they conjoin. For example, the conjunction of Jupiter and Saturn is now in the airy triplicity and begins in the sign of Gemini in the year of the Lord 1325. From that time, in 20 years (the year of the Lord 1345), they will conjoin in Aquarius, and from that time, in 20 years, they will conjoin in Libra, and then in Gemini, and so on in this order until they conjoin twelve times in these three signs. If you multiply 20 by 12, you will find 240 years, after which the conjunction will change and enter the watery triplicity and remain there similarly for 240 years, and so you should understand for the other triplicities. And understand that just as it is said that the great conjunction returns in 960 years to the beginning of Aries, that is, to the fiery triplicity, a conjunction entering the beginning of any other triplicity does not return to its beginning until after 960 years. It will therefore remain, as stated above, in each triplicity for 240 years. There are four triplicities. Therefore, multiply 240 by four, and you will find 960 years. The third conjunction is of Mars and Saturn in Cancer in any 30 years. The fourth conjunction is of Jupiter and Saturn in whatever sign it may be, and this occurs once every 20 years. The fifth conjunction is the entrance of the great luminary into the first minute of the vernal equinox, that is, Aries. The sixth conjunction is of the Sun and Moon and their opposition. And when the ascendant of a great conjunction is mentioned, it refers to the ascendant, namely, the entrance of the Sun into Aries in that year in which that conjunction is to occur. For example, the conjunction of Jupiter and Saturn was in Gemini in the year of the Lord 1325. And the ascendant of the Sun's entrance into Aries in that year was Taurus, 20 degrees. Therefore, Taurus is the ascendant of that conjunction. These conjunctions that have been mentioned are called great conjunctions. There are many other conjunctions among the planets, the number of which is 120, according to Ptolemy in the 50th proposition of the Centiloquium. For he says there, "Do not forget that there are 120 conjunctions that occur in the erratic stars." For in them is greater knowledge than in those that occur in this world, receiving increase and decrease. Daly there in the commentary enumerates them and says that some are binary conjunctions, some ternary, some quaternary, some quinary, some senary, and some septenary. A binary conjunction is when only two planets conjoin, and this can vary in 21 ways. A ternary conjunction is when three planets conjoin, and this can vary in 35 ways. A quaternary conjunction is when four planets conjoin, and this can vary similarly in 35 ways. A quinary conjunction is when five planets conjoin, and this can vary in 21 ways. A senary conjunction is when six planets conjoin, and this can vary in 7 ways. A septenary conjunction is only one, namely, the conjunction of all seven planets. And if you compute or add these predicted numbers to each other, you will find 120. Those who wish to enumerate them individually will find them enumerated in the commentary on the aforementioned proposition. The text here indicates that in this chapter, the author teaches how to investigate the ascending degree of a nativity, assuming that the ascending sign is known but the degree is unknown. He teaches this according to Ptolemy's opinion, not according to his own intention. For Ptolemy says in the 34th proposition of the Centiloquium, "The almuten over the place of conjunction or prevention is in the first degree of the angle from the angles of every human nativity that was in that conjunction or prevention. And every degree that is not similar to the degree of the almuten over the place of conjunction or prevention is not an angle of any human nativity." The meaning of the letter is here.

[Finding the Ascendant for a Nativity]
This is how you find the ascendant degree of someone's nativity. Consider the conjunction of the Sun and Moon that preceded the nativity, or the opposition if an opposition preceded it. If a conjunction preceded it, the nativity is called 'conjunctional'; if an opposition or 'prevention' (which is the same) preceded it, the nativity is called 'preventional'. If the nativity is conjunctional, consider the degree in which the luminaries conjoined, that is, the degree of the zodiac where the conjunction preceding that nativity occurred. See which planet is strongest in that degree by the multitude of testimonies. This planet is the almuten over the place of the conjunction. Then equate it to the hour of the nativity. Once it is equated, establish the ascendant for the hour of the nativity according to estimation, so that you are certain of the ascendant sign. For if you were to err in the sign, this rule would not be valid for you. Therefore, with the ascendant sign of the nativity's hour known, consider whether the place of the planet you equated, given its disposition, is closer to the ascendant degree or to the degree of the tenth house. Whichever of these it is closer to, you will make that angle similar to the planet's degree. That is, place as many degrees of the sign existing in the angle as the planet has traversed of the sign it is in. And so that the meaning of the letter may be more evident, I provide an example here. I assume that at the hour of someone's nativity, the ascendant was Libra, but I do not know its degree. And I assume that the nativity was conjunctional, and the preceding conjunction was in the 6th degree of Aquarius. I see that Saturn is stronger in that degree; therefore, I will equate Saturn to the hour of the nativity, and let us assume I find it in the 20th degree of Virgo. I see that Saturn in this case is closer to the ascendant than to the midheaven according to the estimated ascendant. Therefore, I will make the ascendant angle similar to Saturn's degree. That is, I will place the twentieth degree of Libra in the ascendant. If it had been closer to the midheaven, I would have made the midheaven angle the twentieth degree of the sign existing there. However, if the nativity is preventional, you will work with the degree of the opposition, just as I have now told you about the degree of the conjunction. That is, you will consider the planet that has more strengths in the degree of the opposition. But there is doubt about the degree of prevention, since in a prevention or opposition, the Sun is in one degree and the Moon in the opposite. Which degree, then, should we take as the degree of prevention? The degree of the Sun or the degree of the Moon? The author says, according to Ptolemy's intention, we should take the degree of the luminary that is above the earth. But even then, doubt remains. Suppose one luminary is rising and the other setting, and thus neither will be above the earth nor below the earth. The author says that some wise men have said we should work with the degree of the luminary that is in the east. Then the author says that Ptolemy said if several planets agreed in the lord of the place of conjunction or prevention, that is, if two or three planets had equal strengths in that place, meaning one had as many strengths there as another, then we should take the one that is in its own 'baim'. And if each of them is in its own 'baim', then we should take the one that would change for the better more quickly, that is, the one that will enter a sign where it has more strengths more quickly than in the sign it is currently in. And if they are oriental to the Sun, choose the one that is closer to the Sun, provided it is not combust. In addition to this part, it should be noted that there is another method of investigating the ascendant degree of a nativity, and that method is taken from Ptolemy's Centiloquy, where it says: The place of the Moon in the nativity is the degree itself.

[Duration of Gestation and Hyleg Selection]
The ascendant of the circle at the hour of conception in the womb, from the Moon's place at the hour of conception, is the ascendant at the hour of birth. It is also to be understood, for the clarity of what is to be said, that the durations of infants in their mothers' wombs are not equal, according to what Daly says in the commentary on the opposition already cited. Moreover, they are distinctly divided into three durations: a greater duration, a medium duration, and a lesser duration. The lesser duration contains 258 days. The medium duration contains 273 days. The greater duration contains 288 days. And the difference between the greater and lesser is 30 days. This is to be understood for those born according to the natural course. For abortions and those born in the seventh month, this rule does not hold. The quantity of the infant's duration in the womb is taken from the Moon's place in the figure at the hour of birth. For if at the hour of birth the Moon was at the beginning of the seventh house above the earth, that is, above the western horizon, then the infant was in the mother's womb for the lesser duration, that is, for 258 days. And if the Moon was at the hour of birth in the ascendant degree, then the infant remained in the womb for the medium duration, that is, for 273 days. And if the Moon was at the hour of birth in the degree before the western degree, then the infant remained in the womb for the greater duration, that is, 288 days. And note that when the Moon at birth is in the western part near the horizon, if the astrologer believes it to be above the earth when it is below the earth, or vice versa, he will err in the hour of conception by 30 days. But if the Moon was above the earth, elongated from the west, that is, between the east and west, the duration in the womb is greater than the lesser duration and less than the medium. I say that it is greater than the lesser duration according to the quantity of the Moon's elongation from the west. And if the Moon was below the earth, elongated from the ascendant, the duration in the womb is greater than the medium and less than the greater, and it is greater than the medium according to the quantity of elongation from the ascendant. When you wish to investigate the ascendant degree of someone's birth by this method, establish the ascendant at the hour of birth according to the closest possible estimation to the truth, and equate the Moon to that hour; and see in what place it falls in the figure: if it falls at the beginning of the seventh house, subtract 258 days from the hour of birth. And the hour of conception will remain. But if it falls between the seventh house and the ascendant, that is, above the earth, see by how many degrees it is elongated from the western degree, and for every 12 degrees, take one day, and for every degree beyond 12, take two hours. Add these days and hours to the lesser duration, that is, to 258 days. And subtract the total from the hour of birth, and the time of conception will remain. But if it falls in the ascendant, subtract 273 days from the hour of birth, and the time of conception will remain. But if it falls between the ascendant and the seventh, that is, below the earth, consider how much it is elongated from the ascendant degree, and for every 12 degrees, take one day, and for every remaining degree, two hours. Add the resulting number of days and hours to the medium duration, and subtract the total from the hour of birth. But if the Moon falls at the end of the sixth house, subtract the greater duration from the hour of birth, and the hour of conception will remain. Therefore, knowing the hour of conception, equate the Moon to that hour, and the degree in which it is found was the ascendant at the hour of birth. Although this method is true according to the intention of almost all wise men, it seems to me, and I am certain, that it is not sufficient for investigating the degree in a case where I do not have the ascendant degree except by estimation. For it assumes that I know the Moon's elongation from the western degree or from the ascendant; and if I ignore the ascendant degree, and consequently the western degree, how can I know the Moon's distance from any of them? I do not know. For if my estimation errs by 12 degrees, the Moon's distance from the west or from the ascendant will also err by 12 degrees, and for those, one day should be taken, and thus the hour of conception will err by one day, and the ultimate error, that is, in the ascendant degree, will be as much as the Moon moves in one day. In this chapter, the author teaches how to choose the hyleg, that is, the significator of life in nativities. The meaning of the letter is this: In choosing the significator of life, we must begin with the Sun if the nativity was in the day, and if I find it before the ascendant degree by 5 degrees or less, that is, if we find the Sun in the 5 degrees that have risen above the horizon, that is, at the end of the 12th house, or if we find it in the 10th house or 11th house, we will take the Sun as the hyleg, whether it is in masculine signs or feminine signs. But if it is not in these signs, we must look if it is in the 7th, or 8th, or 9th house in masculine signs, we will still take it as the hyleg. But if in these three places already mentioned, that is, in the 7th house, or 8th, or 9th, it were in feminine signs, it would not be suitable to be the hyleg. Therefore, if the Sun is not a suitable hyleg, we will look to the Moon. If we find it in the ascendant, or in the 2nd, or in the 3rd house, or in the 7th, or 8th house, it will be the hyleg, whether it is in a masculine sign or a feminine sign. But if it is not in these places, we will look if we find it before the degree of the ascendant sign by 5 degrees or less, or in the 10th house, or 4th, or in the 5th in a feminine sign, it will still be the hyleg. But if in these places it were in masculine signs, it would not be a suitable hyleg. But if the nativity was at night, we must begin first with the Moon. If we find it before the western degree by 5 degrees or less, that is, in those 5 degrees that are below the earth on the western side, or in any of the other aforementioned places according to the said manner, it will be the hyleg. And if it is not suitable, we will look to the Sun, which, if it is before the degree of the seventh house by 5 degrees or less, that is, below the earth, or if it is in the 4th or 5th house, it will be a suitable hyleg, whether the signs are masculine or feminine. And if it is in the ascendant or in the 2nd house in a masculine sign, it will be a suitable hyleg, but not in a feminine sign. But if the luminaries are not suitable to be hyleg, we will look whether the conjunction preceded the nativity or the opposition: if the conjunction preceded, we will look at the degree of the conjunction, that is, that degree in which the luminaries were conjoined before the nativity; and if we find that degree in any of the four angles or in any of the succedent houses, we will take it as the hyleg. And if we do not find it in any of the angles nor succedent houses, we must look at the degree of the Part of Fortune, which, if it is in any of the angles or succedent houses, we must take it as the hyleg. But if it is not in any of these places, we must finally take the ascendant degree of the nativity. But if the opposition preceded the nativity, we must look at the degree of the opposition as was said about the degree of the conjunction, and then to the Part of Fortune, and finally to the ascendant degree of the nativity; nor is it necessary in the degree of conjunction or opposition or Part of Fortune to look whether the signs are masculine or feminine. And thus it is clear that the Sun can be hyleg by day and night, above the earth and below the earth, in 11 places. For it can be hyleg above the earth in six places and below the earth in 5. And the Moon can likewise be hyleg in 11 places. For it can be hyleg below the earth in six places and above the earth in 5. But if the Moon in any of the aforementioned places is combust under the Sun's rays, it will not be a suitable hyleg. And when the houses are calculated according to the doctrine handed down in the canons of the astrolabe and the tables of the first mobile, every planet that is before the ascendant or before the beginning of any other house by a few degrees or less will have strong fortitude in the succeeding house. And no place from the aforementioned places can be hyleg unless some planet having dignity in that place aspects it, that is, if it is the lord of the house or the lord of exaltation or triplicity or term or face. Note that the meaning of the letter can be reduced to a few words. There are five places from which the hyleg, that is, the significator of life, is taken, which are these: the Sun, the Moon, the degree of conjunction or opposition, the Part of Fortune, the ascendant degree of the nativity. If the nativity is by day, one must begin with the Sun. And if it is not in suitable places as aforesaid, the Moon is to be taken. And if it is not suitable, the degree of conjunction or opposition is to be taken, which, if it is not suitable, the Part of Fortune is to be taken. And if it is not suitable, the ascendant degree of the nativity is to be taken. Ptolemy says that the hyleg should not be taken from any place existing below the earth. For he says that it is not fitting that we operate in such a noble matter as this through anything that is below the earth, but always through that which ascends and appears above the earth. Nor is it fitting for us to operate through a sign that does not aspect the ascendant.

[Determining the Hyleg and Alcochodon]
nor through the sign that ascends before the ascendant, which is called the house of labor, i.e., the 12th house, which is also cadent from the 7th angle, even more so: because the fumes that rise from the humors of the earth disturb the virtue that comes from it to the earth with their thickness and gloom: and they damage it because the colors and magnitudes of the stars existing in this house appear of a different kind than they are by their nature. Daly Abenragel says that the wise men are very discordant in this; however, that in which the greater part of them agree is that they begin first in diurnal nativities with the Sun, and they begin if it is in any of the angles or succedent, and in a masculine sign, and in a masculine quarter, and if it aspects any of its dignities, it will be the hyleg. If it is not so, and it does not aspect any of its dignities, it will not be suitable for the hyleg; and then you will seek the hyleg from the Moon, and if you find it in an angle or succedent, and in a feminine sign, and in a feminine quarter, and if it aspects any of its dignities, take it for the hyleg, otherwise it will not be suitable. Then look at the nativity; if it is conjunct, take the hyleg from the ascendant degree; and if any lord having any dignity there aspects that degree, you will take him for the hyleg. And if the ascendant is not suitable, you will seek the hyleg from the Part of Fortune. And if the Part of Fortune is not suitable, you will seek the hyleg from the place of the conjunction or opposition preceding the nativity. And if they are not suitable, the nativity will not have a hyleg. And it will be necessary to return to directing the places of the hyleg to the places of the fortunes and to their rays by athazir, and there you will find the place of the end. And if the nativity is nocturnal, you will first seek the hyleg from the Moon, just as you began to seek from the Sun by day. And if you find it in an angle or succedent, in a feminine sign, and in a feminine quarter, and if it aspects any of its dignities, it will be the hyleg. Otherwise, you will seek the hyleg from the Sun, and if you find it in an angle or succedent, in a masculine sign, and in a masculine quarter, and if one having dignity there aspects it, you will take it for the hyleg, otherwise it will not be suitable. And then if the nativity is preventional, you will seek the hyleg from the Part of Fortune, just as you sought from the Moon and the Sun. And if the Part of Fortune is not suitable, you will seek the hyleg from the ascendant degree. And if none of them is suitable for the hyleg, you will seek the hyleg from the degree of conjunction or prevention preceding the nativity. And if it is in an angle or succedent: and there is an aspect from one having any of the five dignities there, take it for the hyleg. And when the Sun is the hyleg and does not have an alcochodon, you will seek the hyleg from the degree of the Moon. And if that, i.e., the degree of the Moon, is the hyleg and does not have an alcochodon, you will seek the hyleg from the ascendant degree if the nativity is conjunct; and if that degree is the hyleg and does not have an alcochodon, you will seek the hyleg from the Part of Fortune. However, if the nativity is preventional, begin first with the Part of Fortune: if it is the hyleg and none of these has an alcochodon, you will seek the hyleg from the degree of conjunction or opposition preceding the nativity: and if none of them has an alcochodon, because the native did not have a hyleg nor an alcochodon, it is a signification of a short life and durability. And know that in the hyleg sought from the ascendant and from the Part of Fortune and from the degree of conjunction or prevention, the masculinity or femininity of the signs nor of the quarters is not considered. And the greater part of the wise men say that the Moon in the third house is suitable to be the hyleg: because it rejoices in it, and they similarly say that the Sun in the ninth house is suitable to be the hyleg because it rejoices there. The alcochodon. In this chapter, the author teaches how to choose the alcochodon, who is the giver of the years of life. The meaning of the letter is this: when you want to know which of the planets is the giver of the years of life, we must look at which planet has more dignities or strengths in the place of the hyleg. For example: if the Sun is the hyleg, we must look at the stronger planet in the place of the Sun. And if the Moon is the hyleg, we must look at the stronger in the place of the Moon, and so on for other places. And if such a planet aspects the place of the hyleg from any aspect, we must take it as the alcochodon. If, however, it does not aspect, we must look at another after it, i.e., the planet that has some strengths in the place of the hyleg, but not as many as the first degree. For example: if one has six strengths in the place of the hyleg and another has 5 or 4 strengths there, and the first does not aspect the place of the hyleg, it cannot be the alcochodon. Then if the second aspects the place of the hyleg, we must take it as the alcochodon; and if it also does not aspect, we must look again at another having fewer dignities, and so we must proceed: until we find one aspecting the place of the hyleg who has some dignity in the place of the hyleg: and if we find no planet aspecting the place of the hyleg that has dignity or dignities there, that place could not be the hyleg: therefore, in this case, it is necessary to seek another hyleg according to the previously stated method. For example: if the nativity is diurnal and the Sun is in a suitable place to be the hyleg: if no one has dignity in the place of the Sun aspecting it, the Sun cannot be the hyleg: because it does not have an alcochodon: therefore, it is then necessary to seek the hyleg from the Moon. And if it is in a suitable place for the hyleg and no one having dignity in its place aspects it, then seek the hyleg from the Part of Fortune or from the degree of conjunction or prevention or the ascendant degree according to the order stated above. And it seemed to some that one should begin with the lord of the house, so that if the lord of the house of the hyleg aspects the hyleg, they took him as the alcochodon and did not look at any other. But if the lord of the house did not aspect, they looked at the lord of the exaltation, who, if he aspected, they placed him as the alcochodon. And if he did not aspect, they looked at the lord of the triplicity, then at the lord of the term, then and finally at the lord of the face. Dorotheus first looked at the lord of the term and preferred him to the lord of the house: but this does not seem consistent with the truth. And some said that if two or three or more planets agree in dignities so that they have equal essential strengths in the place of the hyleg and all aspect that place, the one who aspects closest is to be taken: and if they also agree in this, which rarely happens, the one who is in a praiseworthy state is to be taken, provided that it is conjunct with the Sun in one degree and is not distant from it by 16 minutes. Or the one who is closer to an angle or the one who is at the beginning of the morning lord, i.e., who begins to appear in the morning before sunrise, or the one who is in its station, standing and going direct, or who is in another praiseworthy state from the Sun, i.e., who is oriental if it is one of the three superior planets or occidental if it is one of the three inferior planets. If, however, it happens that the Sun is the hyleg and is in Leo or Aries, i.e., in its house or exaltation, it will be the hyleg and alcochodon. And if the Moon is the hyleg and is in Cancer or Taurus, it will be the hyleg and alcochodon, and it is not necessary to consider any other. Ptolemy says that he is the alcochodon who has more strengths in the place of the hyleg, whether he aspects that place or not. But none of the wise men agrees with him. Therefore, it seems safer to me to follow the way of the wise men. Regarding the years that the alcochodon gives, although the author says nothing, I want to narrate a few things according to the opinion of Balhy Abenragel, which are more consistent with the truth. Balhy Abenragel says that the greater part of the wise men of this science say that when the alcochodon is in the angles, it gives its greater years; and when in the succedents, it gives its middle years; and when in the cadent houses, it gives its lesser years, and it does not give improvement to one succedent over another, and this is an error, says Balhy Abenragel. Know that among the hidden secrets and signals of this science is that when the alcochodon is in the degree of the tenth house, it gives its greater years. And when it is in the degree of the eleventh house, it gives its middle years. And when it moves from one of these two places to another, look at how many degrees there are from one to the other and divide by them the years that are between the greater years and the middle years. For example: I assume that the degree of the 10th house is the third degree of Pisces: and I assume that Venus is the alcochodon and is in the 12th degree of Pisces: it is therefore distant from the point of the 10th house by 10 degrees. And I assume that from the beginning of the 10th house to the beginning of the 11th are 30 degrees. I know that if it were at the beginning of the 10th house, it would give the greater years, which are 82. And if it were at the beginning of the 11th house, it would give its middle years, which are 45. But now in

[Planetary Conditions and Life Expectancy]
neither of these two points is. Therefore, I will subtract 45 and a half years from the greater years, which are 82. 37 years remain, which I will multiply by the distance of Venus from the beginning of the tenth house, which is 7. This results in 370. I will divide this by 30, which is the length between the tenth and eleventh houses, and 12 years will result, with a remainder of 10 after the division. I will multiply this by 12 and divide by 30, and four months will result. Therefore, I will subtract 12 years and four months from the greater years of Venus, and 69 years and 8 months will remain. These will be the years that Venus gives in this case. You can apply this example to other angles and houses. Balya Abenragel says that when the Alcochoden is combust and it is going towards the Sun so that it does not appear, it loses all its given years. For that which is in this state gives only days or hours or things that have no name. And the term of combustion is this: After Saturn is occidental to the Sun and the Sun is towards it, and there are 15 degrees between them until it remains and is oriental, and there are 10 complete degrees between them. And Jupiter is the same. Mars, however, after there are 15 degrees between it and the Sun in the west, until it is oriental and there are 9 degrees between them. Mercury, however, does its deeds and gives its complete gifts as long as it is direct, provided that it is not approached by the Sun by less than 7 degrees. And from 7 degrees to 5 degrees, it gives, but not completely. But from the beginning of 7 degrees until it passes the Sun by 5 degrees, it loses all its given years. And from 5 degrees until the completion of 7 degrees, it gives little. But after it has passed 7 degrees, it gives its complete given years. And Venus does the same, except that when it appears visibly at less than 5 degrees, it then gives its complete given years. The Moon, however, when it applies to the Sun by going towards it and there are 15 degrees between them, weakens its action and gives a small thing, that is, days or something similar to this. And when it applies to the Sun at 12 degrees, it loses all its given years until it has passed the Sun's degree by 10 degrees, and then it gives a small given, that is, days or something similar to it, until it has passed the Sun by 12 degrees, and then it will give its complete given years. The fall of a planet, which is contrary to its exaltation, takes away half of the given years, and the term of this fall is such that the Sun, when it is in the 5th degree of Libra until it passes the 25th degree of the same, is in its fall. The remainder of the sign will be judged as detriment. Saturn is in its fall from the beginning of the 12th degree of Aries until it passes the 26th degree of the same, and the remainder of the sign will be judged as detriment. Jupiter is in its fall from the 8th degree of Capricorn until the completion of the 20th degree, and the remainder of the sign will be judged as detriment. Mars is in its fall from the beginning of the 19th degree of Cancer until the end of Cancer, and at the beginning of that sign, it is judged as detriment. And Venus is in its fall after it has passed the term of Jupiter until the 21st degree of Virgo. What is said about Venus cannot stand unless you understand it according to Ptolemy's terms. For according to those terms, the 14th degree of Virgo is the end of Jupiter's term. But according to the terms in Alchabitius, it is not so. For there, Jupiter's term ends in the 21st degree of Virgo. Either the text of Balya is corrupt, or his statement cannot be understood except according to Ptolemy's terms. And Mercury is in its fall from the beginning of the 8th degree of Pisces until the completion of the 10th degree of the same, and in the remainder of the same sign, it is judged as if it were in its detriment. The retrogradation of the three superior planets from the beginning of their retrogradation until the opposition of the Sun, that is, until the middle of the retrogradation, takes away half of the given years, and the other half remains. And when it has passed the opposition of the Sun, see how many degrees and minutes it will go retrograde from the opposition of the Sun, and how many there are, see what proportional part it will have to all the degrees it has to retrograde from the opposition until the direction, and add that much to half of the given years, and direct those degrees correctly with their minutes in such a way that the planet that is at the beginning of its direction will give its complete given years correctly. I will give an example here: I assume Mars is the Alcochoden and its total given years are 60, according to the proportion previously made between the angle and the succeeding house, and I assume it is retrograde in the middle of its retrogradation. It has therefore lost half of these years in the middle of its retrogradation and before the middle of its retrogradation, and 30 years remain. And I assume it has gone beyond the middle of its retrogradation, that is, the opposition of the Sun, retrograding by 2 degrees. And I assume that from the opposition until the direction, it should go retrograde by 10 degrees. Therefore, I will multiply 2 degrees by half of the given years that it lost, that is, by 30 years, and 60 will result. I will divide 60 by 10, and 6 years will result. I will add these years to half of the given years, that is, to 30 years, and 36 years will result. This is the given of Mars in the proposed case. In Venus and Mercury, after each of them begins to retrograde, it loses half of the given years that it gives when it is direct. And afterwards, see how many degrees and minutes remain until its occultation, as accurately as you can, because Venus may appear when there are less than 5 degrees between it and the Sun. And when it has appeared, it will give half of the given years, unless it appeared when there were less than 5 degrees between it and the Sun, in which case that appearance does not harm it in this state. Afterwards, direct those degrees and minutes after it began to retrograde until it occults itself subtly and correctly, and divide by this half of the given years that remained in the aforementioned manner. For that which is occulted loses all its given years, as we said, and nothing remains for it. And it can be exemplified in a similar way to the example given for the retrogradation of the three superior planets. Balya says that Jupiter and Venus, when they are corporally conjoined or when they aspect the Alcochoden from a trine or sextile, add to the number of years that the Alcochoden gave according to the number of their own years, months, days, or hours, according to their strengths or weaknesses. And when both malefics, Saturn and Mars, are corporally conjoined with the Alcochoden or aspect it from an opposition or square, they diminish its number of years by their lesser number. But when Mercury is with the benefics, adding to the Alcochoden, it also adds its lesser number of years. And when it is with the malefics, diminishing the Alcochoden, it also diminishes its part. And when Mars and Saturn aspect from a trine in signs of short ascension or from a sextile in signs of long ascension, they diminish. And I say that the Sun in a square and opposition diminishes its lesser number of years, and adds from a trine and sextile. Many ancient and modern astrologers say that a fortunate Moon adds from a trine or sextile. And all the wise men of this science confess that when a native does not have a Hyleg and has one of the two benefics in the ascendant or midheaven, it is possible that he will live according to the quantity of the lesser years of that benefic that signified life, unless the ascending degree and the Moon are unfortunate, or the same benefic is the lord of the house of death, which signifies a short duration and life. And the Almuten who presides over the nativity.
