This author teaches how to choose the Almuten, that is, the giving planet in the figure from which the native's being begins after the Hyleg and Alcochoden. The meaning of the text is clear.

[Calculating the Perfection of Conjunctions]
But one year for one sign according to the method previously stated: and we will begin from Virgo. And I will give an example, applying it to our computations according to the years of our Lord Jesus Christ. When you wish to know to which sign the year of the conjunction applies, which signified the law of the Saracens, subtract from the years of Christ 621 years, 6 months, and 14 days. For so many years passed from the beginning of the years of Christ until the beginning of the years of the Arabs. And divide the number of perfect years that remain by 12, and cast out what remains from Virgo, giving to each year one sign according to the method previously stated. And the imperfect year following the perfect years you divided remains in Virgo. For example: the years of Christ are now 1330 completed, and 22 days. From these I will subtract 621 years, 6 months, 14 days. There remain 708 perfect years, 6 months, and 8 days. These are the years that have passed from the beginning of the years of the Arabs until now. I will divide these perfect years by 12, and the total number arises so that no perfect year remains. Therefore, I say that the perfection of the great conjunction, which signified the sect of the Saracens, is now in Virgo, according to the author's opinion. Just as an example was given for the sect of the Saracens, so it can be done for other sects, if the sect is to be spoken of, if the conjunction signifying that sect and the ascendant of the year of the conjunction are known. But it is not expedient to speak much on this matter, for it is a thing that does not accord with our faith. But if anyone delights in these things and wishes to reduce the changes that occur in laws to the motions of the superior bodies, let him read the books on great conjunctions; there he will find it. Then he says, if you wish the perfection from the sign of the conjunction that signified the aforesaid sect, cast out the aforesaid years from Scorpio, because that conjunction, according to him, was in Scorpio. But if you wish the perfection from the ascendant of the kingdom, see how many solar years have passed from the beginning of that kingdom. He gives an example of one kingdom, but I do not know of which kingdom he speaks, and I do not care, for the letter can be understood without his example. But just as it is said of the ascendant of the kingdom, so it is to be understood of the ascendant of the foundation of any city or castle or even of any building, so that the perfect solar years that have passed from the beginning of that foundation are taken and cast out from the ascendant of the beginning of the foundation in the manner previously stated. Then he says, if you wish the perfection from the ascendant of the mutation of the conjunction of Jupiter and Saturn from the watery triplicity to the fiery triplicity, subtract from the years of the Persians 176 perfect years, and convert those that remain into solar years, and cast out from Leo. He means that the conjunction of Jupiter and Saturn at the beginning of the years of the Persians was in the watery triplicity, and after the beginning of the years of the Persians, by which they computed for 176 years, the conjunction changed to the fiery triplicity. And he orders to subtract 176 years from the years of the Persians, and the years that remain are those that have passed from the year of the mutation of the conjunction to the fiery triplicity. And he orders to convert those remaining years into solar years, because the Persians do not have bissextile years, but solar years do. And the perfection is according to solar years. And he orders to cast out from Leo, because according to him, Leo was the ascendant in the year of the mutation of the conjunction to the fiery triplicity. From this it appears that this author was and composed this book at a time when the conjunction was in the fiery triplicity. But now this conjunction is in the airy triplicity. Therefore, I will give an example of the triplicity in which we are. When you wish to know the perfection from the year of the mutation of the conjunction of Jupiter and Saturn to the airy triplicity, subtract from the years of Christ 1324 years, 71 days, and 20 hours. For so much time has passed from the beginning of the years of Christ until the beginning of the years of the mutation of the conjunction to the triplicity in which we are. And cast out the remainder from the 13th degree of Taurus, for that was the ascendant of the aforesaid year. And where your number reaches, there will be the perfection of the year. For example: the years of Christ are 1330 completed, and 22 days. From these I will subtract 1324 years and 71 days. And there will remain 5 perfect years and 316 days of the imperfect year. I will give the first year to Taurus, beginning from its 13th degree. The second sign to Gemini, beginning from its 13th degree. The third to Cancer. The fourth to Leo, beginning from its 13th degree. The fifth to Virgo, beginning from its 13th degree. Therefore, the perfection of the 6th perfect mundane year comes to Libra, to the 13th degree. And if you wish the degree in which is the perfection of the last day from the days that have passed of the imperfect year, multiply the number of days of the perfect year by 30, and divide the product by 365. And the number of times will be the degrees. But if anything remains after the division, multiply it by 60, and divide by the same as before, and the number of times will be the minutes. For example, in the proposed example, 316 days remained from the imperfect year, which I will multiply by 30, and 9480 will result. I will divide this number by 365, and 25 degrees will result. And 355 remains after the division, which I will multiply by 60, and 21300 will result. And I will divide by 365, and 58 minutes will result. Therefore, I will add to the 13th degree of Libra 25 degrees and 58 minutes, and the number will reach the 8th degree and 58 minutes of Scorpio. Therefore, there is now the perfection from the ascendant of the year of the mutation of the conjunction to the airy triplicity. This is about direction. In this chapter, the author teaches how to direct any significator to any place of the circle. It must first be understood that direction, or directing a significator to any place of the circle, is nothing other than finding the equinoctial degrees that revolve from the place of the significator to the place to which it must be directed. If the place of the significator is in the midheaven or in the angle of the earth, then to direct is to find the equinoctial degrees that revolve from the place of the significator to the place to which it must be directed in the right horizon. But if it is in the ascendant or in the descendant, then it is to find those degrees in the oblique horizon. But if it is not in any of these places, then ascensions are taken mixed, that is, mixing the ascensions of the direct circle with the ascensions of the region, proportionally according to the distance of the place of the significator from the angles. And the degrees of direction signify years, which days, which other times. In nativities, each degree signifies a year. In the revolutions of the years of the world and nativities, each degree signifies a day. And some wish that in the revolutions of years, 59 minutes and 8 seconds, that is, the motion of the sun in one day, signify one day. In the conjunctions of the sun and moon and in oppositions, according to some, each 13 degrees and 10 minutes, that is, as much as the moon moves in a day by its mean course, signifies a day. Therefore, when you wish to direct any significator to any place of the circle, if that significator is in the degree of the midheaven or in the angle of the earth, subtract the ascensions of the direct circle of the degree of the significator from the ascensions of the direct circle of the place to which you wish to direct, and the degrees of direction remain. But if the significator is in the ascendant or descendant, subtract the ascensions of the oblique circle of the degree of the significator from the ascensions of the oblique circle.

[Calculating Directions]
to which you wish to direct it, and the degree of direction remains. Example when it is in the Midheaven: I assume that the Moon is in the Midheaven in the 5th degree of Aquarius, and I assume that the opposite rays of Saturn are in the 6th degree of Pisces. I will assume that I want to direct the Moon to the opposite rays of Saturn. I therefore sought the ascensions of the Moon's degree in the direct circle and found 37 degrees, 23 minutes. I also sought the ascensions of the sixth degree of Pisces, where the opposite rays of Saturn are, in the same direct circle, and found 67 degrees, 48 minutes. Then I subtracted the ascensions of the Moon from the ascensions of Saturn's rays, and 30 degrees, 25 minutes remained. These would be the degrees of direction in this case. Example when it is in the Ascendant: I assume that the Moon is in the same 5th degree of Aquarius and the rays of Saturn in the 6th of Pisces. I sought the ascensions of the Moon's degree in the oblique circle in a region whose latitude is 48 degrees, and I found 90 degrees, 22 minutes. I also sought the ascensions of the sixth degree of Pisces and found 348 degrees, 31 minutes. I subtracted the ascensions of the Moon from the ascensions of the degree of Saturn's rays, and 18 degrees, 9 minutes remained. These would be the degrees of direction in this case. In this same way, the ascending degree is directed to any place in the circle. If, however, the significator to be directed is outside these places, then if it is between the Midheaven and the Ascendant, see its distance from the Midheaven by subtracting the ascensions of the degree of the Midheaven in the direct circle from the ascensions of the degree of the significator, which distance you should keep. Then know half of the diurnal arc of the significator's degree by the method described in the chapter on radiations, and keep it. Then subtract the ascensions of the direct circle of the significator's degree from the ascensions of the direct circle of the place to which you wish to direct it, and what remains will be the significator of the direct circle; keep it. Then subtract the ascensions of the significator's degree in the oblique circle from the ascensions of the place to which you wish to direct it in the same oblique circle, and what remains is the significator of the region. Then subtract the smaller significator from the larger, and multiply the difference by the distance from the angle of the Midheaven, and divide the product by half of the diurnal arc, and the proportional part will come, which you add to the significator of the direct circle if it is smaller than the significator of the region, or subtract if it is larger, and what results will be the degree of direction. But if you wish to direct against the succession of signs, just as parts and retrograde planets are directed, that is, proceeding from the Ascendant towards the Midheaven, then you must take the distance of the significator from the Ascendant by the ascensions of the region, and you must add the proportional part of the two significators to the significator of the region if it is smaller than the significator of the direct circle, or subtract from it if it is larger; in other respects, the work does not differ. But if the significator to be directed is between the Ascendant and the angle of the Earth, see the distance of the significator's degree from the Ascendant by subtracting the ascensions of the Ascendant's degree of the region from the ascensions of the significator's degree of the region, and keep the distance. Then know half of the nocturnal arc of the significator's degree by the method described in the work on radiations, which you also keep. Then subtract the ascensions of the significator's degree in the oblique circle from the ascensions of the place to which you wish to direct it in the same oblique circle, and what remains is the significator of the region, which you keep. Then subtract the ascensions of the significator's degree of the direct circle from the ascensions of the direct circle of the place to which you wish to direct it, and what remains will be the significator of the direct circle. Then subtract the smaller from the larger, and the difference of the two significators will remain, which you multiply by the distance of the significator's degree from the Ascendant, and divide the product by half of the nocturnal arc of the significator's degree, and the proportional part will come, which you add to the significator of the region if it is smaller than the significator of the direct circle, or subtract from the significator of the region if it is larger than the significator of the direct circle; what results after addition or subtraction will be the degree of direction. If, however, you wish to direct the succession of signs, that is, proceeding from the angle of the Earth towards the Ascendant, then you must take the distance of the significator from the angle of the Earth by the ascensions of the direct circle, and multiply that by the difference of the two significators, and divide by half of the diurnal arc, as was said before; and you must add the proportional part to the significator of the direct circle if it is smaller than the significator of the region, or subtract if it is larger; in other respects, the work does not differ. But if the significator to be directed is between the angle of the Earth and the occidental degree, you must operate with the opposite degree of the significator and with the opposite degree of the place to which you wish to direct it, and by the distance of the opposite degree of the significator from the Midheaven, and by half of the diurnal arc of the opposite degree of the significator. For the opposite degree of the significator is as distant from the meridian line as the significator's degree is from the angle of the Earth, and half of the diurnal arc of the opposite degree is as great as half of the nocturnal arc of the significator. And then the operation is the same as that between the Midheaven and the Ascendant. If, however, the significator to be directed is between the occidental angle and the Midheaven, you must operate similarly by the opposite degree of the significator and by its distance from the Ascendant, and by half of the nocturnal arc of the same opposite degree, and by the opposite degree of the significator's place to which it is to be directed; and the operation is the same as that between the Ascendant and the angle of the Earth. If it happens that the significator to be directed is in one quadrant and the place to which it is to be directed is in another quadrant, for example: the significator is between the Midheaven and the Ascendant, and the place to which it is to be directed is between the Ascendant and the angle of the Earth, then you must direct up to the angle, and afterwards direct the angle up to the place to which it is to be directed, and join these directions together. You will direct the significator as previously stated, so that you take the distance of the significator from the angle that is behind it in the order of the signs; for example, if it is between the angle of the Midheaven and the Ascendant, you will take its distance from the angle of the Midheaven. And if it is between the Ascendant and the angle of the Earth, you will take its distance from the Ascendant. You will also take half of the diurnal or nocturnal arc of the significator's degree or its opposite by the method previously stated; and you will take the angle to which you wish to direct as the place to which it is to be directed; and you will observe the order previously stated. After that direction is made, you will direct the angle, by the method previously stated, which was the significator in one of the angles, up to the place to which the significator is to be directed, and you will add one direction to the other, and the degrees of direction will result. The author in the text says that the distance of the significator from the angle should be taken, and that should be divided by the parts of the hours of the significator's degree, and the hours of the significator's distance from the angle will result. And he says that one must take the sixth part of the difference of the two significators, which part he orders to be multiplied by the hours of the significator's distance from the meridian, and he orders the result to be added to the significator of the direct circle or subtracted by the method stated. But the method I have presented is easier and clearer. For in the author's method, one must take the distance from the angle by the same method that I have presented, and beyond this, one must seek the parts of the hours of the significator's degree.

[Calculating Directions with Latitude]
Then divide the distance from the angle by the parts of the hours of the degrees of the significator, and hold what results. Afterwards, according to his method, seek the significator of the direct circle and the significator of the region by the same method I have set forth, and also the difference between the two significators. Beyond this, it is necessary to divide that difference by six so that it has six parts. Since error easily occurs in a multitude of operations, the method I have set forth seems more certain to me. For example, when the significator is between the Midheaven and the Ascendant, and the place to which it should be directed is in the same quadrant, namely between the Midheaven and the Ascendant. I assume that the Moon is the Hyleg and is in the fifth degree of Aquarius, and I assume that the opposite rays of Saturn (the same would apply to bodies) are in the sixth degree of Pisces, and I assume that the angle of the Midheaven is the 20th degree of Capricorn. To direct the Moon to the rays of Saturn, I first sought the ascensions of the degree of the Midheaven in the direct circle and found 21 degrees and 39 minutes. I subtracted the ascensions of the degree of the Midheaven from the ascensions of the degree of the Moon, and the distance of the Moon from the Midheaven remained: 15 degrees and 44 minutes. Then I sought the ascensions of the degree of the Moon in the oblique circle and found 330 degrees and 22 minutes, which I also sought from the ascensions of the degree opposite the Moon's place, 104 degrees and 30 minutes, from which I subtracted the ascensions of the degree of the Moon. But because I could not subtract, since the ascensions of the degree of the Moon were greater than the ascensions of the opposite degree, I added 360 degrees to the ascensions of the degree opposite the Moon, and 464 degrees and 30 minutes resulted. Then I subtracted, and 134 degrees and 8 minutes remained, and this was the entire diurnal arc of the degree of the Moon, which I bisected, and the half was 67 degrees and 4 minutes. Therefore, I kept the distance of the Moon from the Midheaven and half of the Moon's diurnal arc. Then I subtracted the ascensions of the degree of the Moon in the direct circle, which were 37 degrees and 23 minutes, from the ascensions of the degree of Saturn's rays in the same circle, which were 67 degrees and 48 minutes, and 21 degrees and 25 minutes remained, and this was the significator of the direct circle, which I therefore kept. Then I subtracted the ascensions of the degree of the Moon in the oblique circle, which were 330 degrees and 22 minutes, from the ascensions of Saturn's rays in the same oblique circle, which were 348 degrees and 21 minutes, and the significator of the region remained, which was 8 degrees and 9 minutes. Then I subtracted the significator of the region from the significator of the direct circle, and the difference between the two significators remained, which was 12 degrees and 16 minutes. Then I multiplied this difference by the distance of the Moon from the Midheaven and divided by half of the diurnal arc of the degree of the Moon, and the proportional part resulted, which was 2 degrees, 52 minutes, and 38 seconds. I also subtracted this proportional part from the significator of the direct circle because it was greater than the significator of the region, and the degrees of direction remained, which were 27 degrees, 32 minutes, and 21 seconds. For each degree, I took one year, and for every 5 remaining minutes, one month, and for every minute, 6 days, and for every second, 6 minutes of a day. When this time is completed from the time of birth, for whom the figure was thus disposed, the native will die. When the significator is between the Ascendant and the angle of the earth, you will work with the distance from the Ascendant and with half of the nocturnal arc, and it does not differ in anything else. When you wish to direct against the succession of signs, if the significator is between the Midheaven and the Ascendant, you will work with the distance from the Ascendant and with half of the diurnal arc. If the significator is between the angle of the earth and the degree of the West, you will work with the opposite of the degree of the significator and the degree opposite the place to which you wish to direct, and then your work is between the Midheaven and the Ascendant. And if the significator is between the degree of the West and the Midheaven, you will similarly work with the opposite degrees, and then your work is between the Ascendant and the angle of the earth. Note, however, that in the manner described, significators are directed when they have no latitude. When significators have latitude, the method is more difficult, and for this reason, an instrument was made to direct planets having latitude, and that instrument is called a directorium. It seemed to the composer or inventor of that instrument that a significator having latitude could not be directed by tables of ascensions, or not without great difficulty. But I say that his instrument is not sufficient unless it is of maximum size so that it can receive minutes, and such an instrument can hardly be made. For in directions, for the most part, one year is taken for each degree. If, in the directions of the instrument, it is not divided except by degrees, certainty up to a year will hardly be found in it, and this if the instrument is well made so that there is no error in dividing; but this is not sufficient. And I tell you that a significator having latitude can be directed to a place having latitude by tables of ascensions, and I have not seen the method explained in any book. But the method is this: when you wish to direct a significator having latitude from the ecliptic to the body of some planet having latitude, or to the rays of some planet having latitude, first seek the degree with which the significator culminates according to the doctrines of the canons of the primum mobile. Then seek the degree with which the place to which you wish to direct culminates according to the same doctrine, and you will take the degree with which the significator culminates as the place of the significator, and by this, you will know the distance of the significator from the Midheaven or from the Ascendant by the method previously stated, neither more nor less. And you will take the place with which the place to which it should be directed culminates as the place to which it should be directed. With these two, you will seek the significator of the direct circle by the method previously stated. Then seek the degree with which the significator rises in its region according to the doctrine of the canons of the primum mobile. Also seek the degree with which the place to which it should be directed rises according to the same canons. Then, with the degree with which the significator rises, you will seek half of the diurnal or nocturnal arc by the method previously stated, and you will seek the significator of the region with these two degrees, namely with the degree with which the significator rises and with the degree with which the place to which it should be directed rises; in other respects, the work does not differ. I also tell you briefly that it is necessary to seek the degree in which the significator culminates and the degree with which the place to which it should be directed culminates. With the first two, it is necessary to seek the significator of the direct circle. With the other two, it is necessary to seek the significator of the region. With the degree with which the significator culminates, it is necessary to seek the distance from the Midheaven if it is between the Midheaven and the Ascendant. With the degree with which the significator rises, it is necessary to seek half of the diurnal or nocturnal arc. If the significator is between the Ascendant and the angle of the earth, it is necessary to seek the distance of the significator from the Ascendant with the degree with which the significator rises and with the same half of the nocturnal arc. In all other respects, the work is the same as the work previously stated. There is also another case that can occur in directions when the significator and the place to which

[Direction of the Ascendant]
which must be directed by latitudes, or one of them has latitude. For it can happen that the significator to be directed and the place to which it must be directed come simultaneously to the meridian line, so that both mediate the sky with the same degree, but are not in the same degree in the ecliptic. If any of these cases occurs, then you will operate in the same way as I will say. If the significator and the place to which it must be directed come with the same degree to the midheaven, and there are no ascensions in the direct circle between them, you will put 0 for the significator of the direct circle. Afterwards, you will seek the significator of the region by taking the ascensions in the oblique circle from the place with which the significator rises to the place with which the place to which it must be directed rises, and you will multiply all that, that is, the significator of the region, by the distance of the significator from the angle, and you will divide the product by half of the diurnal or nocturnal arc, and the proportional will result, which you will hold for the degrees of direction. But if the significator to be directed and the place to which it must be directed rise with one and the same degree, you will put 0 for the significator of the region, and you will multiply the significator of the direct circle by the distance of the significator from the angle, and divide by half of the diurnal or nocturnal arc, and the proportional will result, which you will hold for the degrees of direction. To give examples of all these would be too long, but I intend, God willing, at the end of this exposition, to put the equation of one nativity in which the method of investigating the ascendant and choosing the hyleg and alcochoden will appear, and I will put there some projections of rays and some directions; let this suffice concerning the work of directions. The author says in the text, having known the years of direction, if you wish to know the place of this direction in the zodiac, add the years of direction to the ascensions of the direct circle of the significator's degrees if the significator was in the midheaven or in the angle of the earth, and reduce to equal degrees in the direct circle; and where the number leads you in the circle of signs, there is the place of direction; and it is called the place of division, and the lord of the term of that place is called the divisor. If the significator was in the ascendant, add the years of direction to the ascensions of the region of the significator's degrees, and reduce to equal degrees in the oblique circle; and where the number leads you in the circle of signs, there is the place of division, and the lord of the term of that place is the divisor. And this is the same work as the work of the projections of rays; and when you have made the direction and you have made this work, you will find at the end the same place to which you directed, unless the significator had latitude. And from this, the algebutar in nativities. In this chapter, the author teaches how to direct the ascendant degree in nativities. The meaning of the text is this: Consider in whose planet's term the ascendant degree is, and consider the end of that term. Then seek the ascensions of the ascendant degree in the oblique circle by the table of your region and keep them; also seek the ascensions of the end of that term by the same table, from which subtract the ascensions of the ascendant degree, and the degrees that remain are the degrees of direction. Take for each degree one year, and for every five minutes one month, and for each minute six days, and for each hour two hours and twenty-four minutes of an hour; and the planet that is the lord of the term is the disposer of the years or the divisor. Afterwards, consider the end of the immediately following term, and subtract the ascensions of the preceding term's end from the ascensions of the end of that term; and the degrees of direction will remain. Take thus for each degree one year, and so on. And the lord of that term is the disposer or divisor; and in this way you will proceed to the end of each sign according to the order of the signs until the end of life. And if there is in any term any planet or rays of any planet, that planet will be the ruler in the division. An example I put here: the ascendant of a nativity was the fourth complete degree of Virgo. To direct this degree, first consider in whose planet's term this degree is. And it appears first that it is in Mercury's term, and the term lasts until the end of the seventh degree of Virgo. I sought the ascensions of the ascendant degree in the oblique horizon in the region whose latitude is 48 degrees, and I found 44 degrees and 27 minutes. I also sought the ascensions of the end of the term, namely the end of the seventh degree of Virgo, and I found 48 degrees and 33 minutes. I subtracted the ascensions of the ascendant degree from the ascensions of the end of the term, and 4 degrees and 6 minutes remained. I gave one year to each degree, and one month to every five minutes, and six days to each minute: there were four years, that is, one month and 26 days. And Mercury, the lord of the term, was the disposer of these years. Then I considered the immediately following term, which is Venus's, and it lasts until the end of the 17th degree of Virgo. I sought the ascensions of the end of that term, namely Venus's, and I found 62 degrees and 15 minutes. From these I subtracted the ascensions of the end of the preceding term, Mercury's, and 13 degrees and 44 minutes remained, which made 12 years, 8 months, and 12 days. And Venus disposed these years. At the end of this term, the native's age was 17 years, 9 months, and 18 days. Then follows Jupiter's term, which lasts until the 21st complete degree of Virgo. I sought its ascensions and found 67 degrees and 93 minutes. From these I subtracted the ascensions of the end of the preceding term, and 5 degrees and 28 minutes remained, which made 4 years, 3 months, and 18 days. Jupiter was the disposer of these years. The native's age at the end of these years was 23 years, 3 months, and 6 days. Then follows Mars's term, and it must be done as before: according to this order, the direction is continued until the end of life. As often as the direction reaches the body or rays of an infortune, illness or impediment will come to the native in his body according to the nature of that infortune, unless fortunes aspect that place. Then they will diminish the evil. And from this, the duodenaria of planets and houses. In this chapter, the author teaches how to find the duodenaria. It must be understood for the clarity of this chapter that each sign is understood to be divided into twelve parts, and each part is two degrees and 30 minutes. Dyfpalensis places this chapter and the two following chapters among the dignities of planets. The lord of the duodenaria is the lord of that sign. The lord of the second duodenaria is the succeeding planet descending, and so on according to order. For example: the lord of the first duodenaria of Aries is Mars, the second the Sun, the third Venus, the fourth Mercury, the fifth the Moon, the sixth Saturn, the seventh Jupiter, the eighth again Mars, and so on according to order. The author's meaning is this: When you wish to know the duodenarias of planets or houses, see how much the planet has traversed of the sign in which it is, or of the house in which it is, and multiply the number of those degrees by twelve; and to the product, add the number of degrees you multiplied. Whatever is collected, project it from the beginning of the sign.

[Finding the Lord of the Novenary]
in which the planet is, giving to each sign 3 degrees and 20 minutes. Where the number ends, there will be the novenary. And from this, Alchabitius teaches how to find the lord of the novenary. The meaning is this: When you wish to know the novenary or the lord of the novenary of any planet, see how many degrees the planet has traversed in the sign in which it is, or in the house in which it is. And divide that whole sign into 9 divisions. And each division will be of 3 degrees and 20 minutes. Then see in which part of that division the planet is. And you will give the first division to the lord of the movable sign of the same triplicity. And the second division to the lord of the following sign. And so on, according to the order of the signs, until you come to that novenary in which the planet is whose lord of the novenary you seek. For example: I assume that the Sun is in the 24th degree of Aquarius. To know the lord of the novenary of the Sun's degree, I first gave 3 degrees and 20 minutes of Aquarius to the lord of the movable sign of the same triplicity. Now Aquarius is of the airy triplicity. The movable sign of that triplicity is Libra; its lord is Venus. Therefore, Venus is the lady of the first novenary of Aquarius, that is, of the first 3 degrees and 20 minutes. Then I gave the second novenary to Mars, the lord of the following sign, that is, Scorpio. And then 6 degrees and 40 minutes were completed from the beginning of Aquarius. Then I gave the third novenary to Jupiter, that is, the lord of Sagittarius, who succeeds Scorpio. And then 10 degrees were completed from the beginning of Aquarius. I gave the fourth novenary to Saturn, the lord of Capricorn, who succeeds Sagittarius. And 13 degrees and 20 minutes were completed from the beginning of the sign. I gave the fifth novenary to Saturn, the lord of Aquarius. And 16 degrees and 40 minutes were completed. I gave the sixth novenary to Jupiter, the lord of Pisces. And 20 degrees were completed from the beginning of the sign of Aquarius. I gave the seventh novenary to Mars, the lord of Aries. And 23 degrees and 20 minutes were completed from the beginning of the sign. I gave the eighth novenary to Venus, the lord of Taurus. That, then, is the division of the Sun's novenary in the assumed case. And then 26 degrees and 40 minutes of Aquarius were completed. Therefore, when you find in books of judgments about the lord of the anaubarach of the luminaries, if it is by day, it refers to the lord of the Sun's novenary. If by night, to the lord of the Moon's degree novenary. Other things that the author says are clear by reading the text. This teaches how to find the decans. Its meaning is this: Divide the ascending sign into three parts. And each division will be of ten degrees. And you will give the first division to the lord of the ascendant. The second to the lord of the second sign. And the third to the lord of the third sign. He means that the first division is of the lord of the same sign that ascends. And the second division is of the lord of the following sign of the same triplicity. The third division is of the lord of the third sign of that triplicity. So that the three decans are the lords of the three signs of one triplicity. The author gives such an example in the text. Suppose that the first face of Aries is ascending, its decan is Mars. If the second face is ascending, its decan is the Sun, the lord of Leo, the second sign of the same triplicity. And if the third face is ascending, its decan is Jupiter, the lord of Sagittarius, which is the third sign of that triplicity. And if the first face of Leo is ascending, its decan is the Sun, the lord of the same sign. If the second face is ascending, its decan is Jupiter, the lord of the sign that succeeds Leo in the same triplicity. If the third face is ascending, its decan is Mars, the lord of the third sign from Leo in the same triplicity, that is, Aries. Understand this method for other triplicities.

[Lord of the Orb and Horary Lords]
And from this, the lord of the orb. In this chapter, he sets the order for the lord of the hours in nativities. The meaning of the text is this: Look at what hour the native emerges from the womb and the lord of that hour. Give it to the first year of the native's life, and through it, it signifies the state of the native's body, whether healthy or infirm, in that year, just as through the lord of the ascendant. And you will give the lord of the following hour to the second year, and through it, it signifies the state of substance in that year, just as through the lord of the house of substance. You will give the lord of the third hour to the third year from the hour of birth, and through it, it signifies the state of brothers in that year, just as through the lord of the third house. And in this way, you will proceed with the other lords of the hours, following the order of the hours and houses, until the end of life. And what it says in the text is clear. An example in this: Suppose someone was born on a Sunday, in the fourth hour. That fourth hour is the hour of the Moon. Therefore, the Moon will be the lord of the first year, and from it, the state of the body is taken. The following hour is of Saturn. Therefore, Saturn will be the lord of the second year, and from it, the state of substance in that year is taken. And so on, in order. And from this, the disposition of the firdaria. This chapter discusses the years of the firdaria and the governance of the planets in nativities. The meaning of the text is this: If the nativity was by day, the firdaria begins with the Sun, and the Sun governs the native according to the quantity of its firdaria years, which are ten. After the Sun, Venus governs for the quantity of its firdaria years, which are eight. After Venus, Mercury governs for 12 years. Then the Moon for nine years. Then Saturn for 11. Then Jupiter for 12 years. Then Mars for 7 years. Then the Head of the Dragon for three years. Then the Tail of the Dragon for two years. Then the disposition returns to the Sun and proceeds through the order of the planets as before. The total number of years is 75. And whoever exceeds this number of years returns to the first disposition as far as possible. If, however, the nativity is by night, the firdaria begins with the Moon, and the Moon disposes its years. Then Saturn. Then Jupiter. Then Mars. Then the Sun. Then Venus. Then Mercury. Then it returns to the Moon and proceeds according to the order of the planets as before. And when any planet disposes the years of its firdaria, it alone disposes the seventh part of those years. In the second seventh part, the planet that succeeds it participates with it. In the third, the third planet participates. In the fourth, the fourth. And in the fifth, the fifth. And so on, up to seven sevenths and seven planets. For example: I assume that someone was born by day. Therefore, the firdaria begins with the Sun, and the Sun governs him according to the quantity of its firdaria years, which are 10 years. And the Sun alone governed the seventh part of these ten years, that is, for one solar year and 156 days and 12 hours. For this is the seventh part of ten years. In the second seventh part of these ten years, Venus had participation with the Sun in the disposition of the firdaria for one year, 156 days, and 12 hours. And then two years and 313 days were completed for the native. Then Mercury had participation with the Sun in the disposition of the firdaria for one year and 156 days and 12 hours. And at the end of this disposition

[Planetary Firdaria and Elevation]
of the division, 4 solar years, 104 days, 6 hours passed for the native. Then the Moon had a participation with the Sun through the same seventh part for 10 years. At the end of this division, 260 years, 18 days, 18 hours passed for the native. Then Saturn had a participation with the Sun through the seventh part for 10 years, and at the end of this division, 52 complete years passed for the native. Then Jupiter had a participation with the Sun in the disposition of the firdaria through the same seventh part. At the end of this division, 8 solar years, 208 days, 12 hours passed for the native. Then Mars had a participation with the Sun in the disposition of the firdaria in the last seventh part of ten years, and at the end of this division, 10 complete years passed for the native. This is how it should be done for the firdaria of all planets. However, the Head and Tail of the Dragon, each disposes of the years of its firdaria or the participation of the planets by itself. To narrate the events contingent to the native in any of these divisions would be too long. But Abenragel in his great book completely set forth all divisions and the judgments of each division. Therefore, those who wish for these judgments should read that book. In this chapter, he teaches from this almanac. His intention is that the planet which was higher in its short circle, i.e., in the epicycle, is said to be elevated above the other by an elevation of which he speaks here. And this is what Ptolemy says in the 63rd proposition of the Centiloquium: He says that one must look at the conjunction of Saturn and Jupiter in the same minute for the elevation of one above the other and judge with the strength of its nature in this world. And similarly, do this in the remaining 21 conjunctions. He says there in the commentary: the elevation of a planet above a planet is that its distance from the apogee of its short circle is such that it is said to be elevated above the other. But the author in the text orders to look at the mean place of the planet and the true place of the planet. And if the true place of the planet is less than the mean motion, the planet is descending from the upper part of the epicycle towards the lower part. But if the true place of the planet is greater than the mean motion, the planet is ascending from the lower part of the epicycle towards the upper part. To put it briefly, if the argument of the planet is less than six common signs, it is descending. And if it is more, it is ascending. Then the author orders to subtract the mean motion of the planet from its true motion if the mean motion is less than the true motion; or conversely if it is greater, that is, the smaller is subtracted from the larger, and he orders to multiply the remainder by seven. And he orders to divide the resulting number by 22, and he orders to take the quotient as the elevation when it ascends or as the depression when it descends. For Venus and Mercury, he orders to look at the difference between the place of each of them and the place of the Sun, and he orders to do as in the others. The method previously stated according to Ptolemy's opinion seems better and more certain to me. Then the author says that the stronger signification of the planets is when one of them is elevated above the other in conjunction. In opposition, however, and in the fourth aspect, the signification will be less apparent. And if one planet is ascending and the other descending, the one that is ascending goes above the descending one. If both are ascending, the one that has the greater ascension goes above the other. And if both are descending, the one that has the lesser ascension goes above the other.

[Elevation and Aperture of the Gates]
Descent. It also says that a planet is elevated above another planet's rising to a northern latitude, going above the meridian. And if both are northern, the one that is more northern goes above the one that is less northern. If both are southern, the one with the lesser latitude goes above the one with the greater latitude. If any planet is in the ecliptic lacking latitude, then the northern planet goes above it, and the one lacking latitude goes above the meridian. And from this comes the opening of the gates. The opening of the gates is said to occur when an inferior planet conjoins a superior planet, and their houses are opposite. For example, when the Moon conjoins Saturn or aspects it, then there is an opening of the gates. Similarly, when the Sun conjoins Saturn, for the houses of the Sun and Moon are opposite the houses of Saturn. Similarly, there is an opening of the gates when Mercury conjoins Jupiter, because the houses of both are opposite. Similarly, when Venus conjoins Mars, there is an opening of the gates because their houses are opposite. Hyspalensis says that Venus signifies humidity, Mercury signifies winds, Saturn signifies clouds and cold, Mars signifies winds from the right, i.e., from the south, and heat, Jupiter signifies temperance and winds from the left, i.e., from the north. The same Hyspalensis says that when the Moon separates from the conjunction of any planet or from its aspect and conjoins another planet, and the houses of those planets are opposite, this is a great opening of the gates, in which it is necessary for winds or rains to come, as is from the nature of those planets. For example, when the Moon, separating from Venus, conjoins Mars, or separating from Mercury, conjoins Jupiter, or separating from the Sun, conjoins Saturn, this is a great opening of the gates. And from this, Albumazar speaks of fortunate and unfortunate hours. They found 12 hours after the conjunction of the Sun and Moon and give them to the Sun, and divide them into three parts, and they judge the first four hours according to the judgment of the first lord of the triplicity of the Sun's place. And they judge the second four hours according to the judgment of the second lord of the triplicity of the Sun's place. And the last four hours according to the judgment of the third lord of the triplicity of the Sun's place at the hour of conjunction. Afterwards, they give the next 12 hours to Venus and divide them similarly into three parts, and they judge each four hours according to the judgment of the lords of the triplicity of Venus's place at the hour of conjunction. Afterwards, they do similarly with Mercury and the Moon and with the other planets in the order of the planets until the circle returns to the Sun after 84 hours. And then they receive from the Sun in the same order. And this continues until the second conjunction. And some say that after the conjunction there are 12 hours which are called combust, in which it is not good to begin any work. And after these 12 combust hours, there are 72 incombust hours, in which the beginning of works is useful. After these 72 incombust hours, there are again 12 combust hours, and again after those, 72 incombust hours, and after those, 12 combust hours, and so on until the next conjunction. And to put it briefly, all 12 hours that are given to the Sun according to the order of the planets are combust, and the 72 hours that are of the other planets are incombust. Then the author says, and they divide these 12 combust hours into three divisions, and each division will be of four hours. And some say that if one begins a war in the first four combust hours, the perdition of his soul is to be feared. The author does not understand the perdition of the soul after this life, so that after the soul's separation from the body, devils seize it and lead it to hell. But he understands the perdition of the soul, that is, the loss of present life, and he understands this in all places of astrological judgments. For it pertains to them to speak of this perdition. But of the first perdition, it pertains to theologians. And he who begins a war in the second four hours, the detriment of his body is to be feared, i.e., without loss of life. And he who begins a war in the last four hours, the loss of all that he possesses is to be feared, and the loss of those things that pertain to him. And thus is completed the exposition of the introduction of Alchabitius to the mastery of astrological judgments. Fifth difference in the commemoration of all parts. This is the fifth difference of this book, in which the author teaches the projection of parts, and it can be divided into two parts: because in the first part he places the parts that fall in nativities. And in the second part he places the parts that fall in the revolutions of the years of the world. The second part begins there: and with God's help. The first part is divided into two parts: because in the first part he gives the method of projecting parts in general and exemplifies with the part of fortune. In the second part he places the parts specifically, i.e., of the houses. The second part begins there. Let us begin after the part of fortune. The meaning of the first part is this. The method in the projections of parts is that equal degrees are taken which are between one place and another, and that number is projected from the ascendant or another place. Or the degrees that were from the beginning of the ascendant sign are added to the equal degrees that were between both places, and the product is computed from the beginning of the ascendant sign, giving to each sign 30 degrees. And where the number ends, there is the part of fortune. For example: I assume that the Sun is at the end of the sixth degree of Pisces, and the Moon is at the end of the 14th degree of Gemini, and the ascendant degree is the 10th degree of Aries. I subtract the true place of the Sun from the true place of the Moon, and 98 degrees remain, to which I add 10 degrees, which are from the beginning of Aries to the ascendant degree, and 108 degrees result. I begin to project from the beginning of Aries, giving to each sign 30 degrees, and this number ends in the 28th degree of Cancer. There, then, is the part of fortune in the example given. Let us begin, therefore, by placing in each house the parts pertaining to it. And it can be divided into as many parts as there are houses where the parts begin, as is clear in the text. First, he places the parts of the first house, and there are six. The first is the part of life. The second is the part of Hyleg. The third is the part of future things or the part of divination. The fourth is the part of affection and concord. The fifth is the part of stability of duration. The sixth is the part of animosity and audacity. He says in the text, when you wish to know the part of life, take the degrees that are from Jupiter to Saturn by day, and by night the degrees that are from Saturn to Jupiter, and project from the ascendant. Albumazar says in his great introduction that this part signifies natural life and the being of the body and sustenance, which if it is in good condition, signifies length of life and health of body and joy of soul. If, however, it is impeded, it signifies shortness of life and a multitude of infirmities of soul and sadness and sorrow. Then the author says, the part of Hyleg is taken from the degree of the conjunction that preceded the nativity if the nativity was conjunctal, or from the degree of prevention, i.e., opposition, if the nativity was preventional, to the degree of the Moon, and projected from the ascendant of the nativity, and where the number ends, there is the part of Hyleg. Albumazar says that this part directs as Hyleg directs by degree, and its perfection is led through the signs as is done with Hyleg. When its direction or perfection comes to malefics, it signifies impediment and danger. And there were many wise astrologers who, when they found a man suffering great dangers at certain times and did not find at the same time that his Hyleg had come to places of malefics, nor did they find the same impediment suffering signification in the revolution of the same year, they did not know the cause of this thing. And therefore this was hidden from them: because they did not direct this part, and if they had directed it, they would have found this evil to happen at the same time that this part had come to certain places signifying the danger itself. The part of future things is taken by day from the Moon to the Sun, and by night the opposite, and projected from the ascendant. And the properties of this part, according to Albumazar, are to signify the soul and the body and their being. And it signifies faith and prophecy and region and the worship of God and secrets and thoughts and intentions and hidden and concealed things: and everything that is absent from things, in this way you will apply judgments in others, and from what place to what place each is taken and from what place it is projected is clear in the text. Second house. Here he places the parts of the second house, and there are three. The first is the part of substance. The second is the part of poverty and meanness of spirit. The third is the part of blessedness, triumph, and victory. Albumazar says that the part of substance signifies profit and sustenance and food by which bodies are sustained, which if it is in a good place, signifies good being in substance, food, and sustenance. And if it is impeded, it signifies evil being in these things that we have said. But the other species of fortune appearing from substance, if they are treasured and kept and acquired, signify the other significators of substance and the part of fortune. Third house. Here he places the parts of the third house.

[Parts for the Duration of a Kingdom]
where the strength is to the place where the planets conjoin. And unless this is understood, it is impossible. For it assumes that one knows the degree of the ascendant at the hour of the conjunction of the superior planets. But this is impossible, as Abraham Avenezra says, for he says it is impossible to know the day on which the conjunction should occur; and this would be a great thing. It is also done in another way, namely, it is taken from the degree of the Midheaven of the revolution of that year in which the conjunction occurred, up to the Sun, and projected from the degree of Jupiter. The second part, by which it is known how long the king's reign should last. Here, the hour of the king's election is taken from the Sun in the 15th degree of Leo. And it is projected from the Moon. It is also taken from the Moon in the 15th degree of Cancer and projected from the Sun. This part is about the time of the king's election. Here, the hour of the king's election is taken on the day from Jupiter to Saturn, and at night the opposite, and projected from the ascendant of the revolution of the year in which the king rose. And if Jupiter is in a common sign and the revolution is diurnal, and with this Jupiter is cadent from an angle, then it is taken from Saturn to Jupiter, and 30 degrees are added above, and it is projected from the ascendant. If, however, Jupiter and Saturn are opposite each other and both are cadent from the ascendant, half of the degrees between them are taken and projected from the ascendant. And if Jupiter is in its exaltation and the revolution is at night, it is counted from it to Saturn and projected from the ascendant. Then the author says that there are two main parts from which the election of the king and its duration are extracted. The first of these is that you look at the hour of the king's election and see where the perfection of the year comes from the conjunction of the triplicity that signified that sect in which that kingdom is, giving to every 30 degrees a year, and to every two and a half degrees a month. And thus, the mixed proportion is to the hour of the election. And when you know in what degree of the sign it is, keep that degree, for from it you will go to the first part. And when you want to calculate it, you will apply the ascendant of the revolution of the year in which the elected one rose. Afterwards, look at Saturn and Jupiter, and whichever of them is oriental from the Sun, take from that one up to the degree of the equation of the first part that you kept, and project from the ascendant of the revolution, and where the number comes, that is the place of the first part. And note, the author says, take from the planet oriental from the Sun, either Saturn or Jupiter, and does not say what should be done when both are oriental. I believe that then it should be taken from the one closest to the Sun. Also, it does not say what should be done if neither of them is oriental. To be brief, I do not know what should be done, as I have not seen these two parts set out in this way in any other book. The second part is known in this way: Look at the conjunction of Jupiter and Saturn in which the king rose or began to reign, to what sign and degree the perfection of the year comes, giving to each year 30 degrees, and to each month 2 and a half degrees, up to the day on which the king rose, and that is the place of the equation of the first part, keep it. After this, take from Saturn or Jupiter, whichever is oriental, up to the place of the second part, and project from the ascendant of the revolution of the year, and where the number comes, that is the place of the second part. These are the parts that signify the strength of the king and his duration. Balya Abenragel says: Look at the revolution of the years of the world for the enthronement of the enthroned. First from Saturn, which is the first part, and from Jupiter, which is the second. And how many degrees and how many minutes are between them, and note this. Afterwards, consider in what sign the lord of the Midheaven is, and reduce those degrees to the ascensions of that sign in which it is, and what comes out from there will be what lasts for years or months or days. And if it is in its houses or exaltations, it will be years; and if they are peregrine in succedent houses, it will be months; otherwise, it will be days. Similarly, when the Sun applies to Mars, and Mars is void of course, not applying to Saturn, it signifies that soldiers will move against the enthroned one and will come upon him with raised weapons, and because of this, sadness and anxieties will befall him, and perhaps they will capture him. But if Mars with this applies to Saturn, their natures conjoin, and no one will move against him. Here, there are also other excetutory parts of the world by which it is known which things will be expensive and which cheap. The meaning of the natal letter. When you want to know whether a thing will be very expensive or cheap, or little, consider the part of that thing and see in which planet's house or exaltation or term or triplicity that part falls. If that planet is combust or retrograde or in some malignant place, that thing will become cheap and of little value. But if it is in a place of strength or in an angle, and especially in the Midheaven, that thing will be expensive and of greater value. And if the lord of that house comes to the place of its descent, that thing will become cheap. He means to say that if the planet has more strengths in the place of the part, in any of its dignities, and especially in its exaltation, or if it is in any of the angles, and especially in the Midheaven, that thing will be expensive. And according to the quantity of the planet's strength in its dignities or in angles or succedent houses, will be the quantity of the dearness. But if the planet itself is in its fall from its house or exaltation, or is in a cadent house from an angle, that thing will become cheap and of little value. Look also at the aspect of the benefics and malefics to it, that is, to the part and to the Moon, and who its lord is and how it aspects that part. If a benefic and the Moon aspect that part, the price of that thing will multiply. And if malefics aspect them, that thing will suffer detriment and will be cheap and of little value. I tell you that if the planet has more strengths in the place of the part in the revolution of the year, and is retrograde, and with this is in any of its dignities or in an angle, it signifies that that thing will be expensive, but not at the beginning of the year, as long as the lord of the part is retrograde. And when that planet begins to become direct, then that thing will begin to be expensive. In the same way, if the planet lord of the part is in its fall and is direct, it signifies the cheapness of the thing, but that cheapness will be greatest when the planet begins to be retrograde. Then he sets out the projections and begins with the part of wheat and says that the part of wheat is taken from the Sun to Mars and projected from the ascendant: from which places they are taken and from which places they are projected is clear in the text. And so that the method may be clearer, I will give an example of the part of wheat in the figure of the preceding conjunction of the Sun's ingress into Aries, and in the figure of the revolution of this year, that is, 1331. I say that in Paris, according to the truth of Alfonsine tables, at the hour of the conjunction of the Sun and Moon preceding the Sun's ingress into Aries, the ascendant will be the first degree of Cancer. The Sun's place at that hour will be 5 signs, 6 degrees, 42 minutes, 36 seconds. The true place of Mars was 1 sign, 44 degrees, 17 minutes, 28 seconds. I will see what is between the Sun and Mars by subtracting the Sun's place from Mars's place, and I find 1 sign, 47 degrees, 34 minutes, 52 seconds, which number I will compute from the ascendant, and the number terminates in Libra, 18 degrees, 10 minutes, 6 seconds. Then I will see what is strongest there, and I find Saturn stronger in that place, which is its exaltation, by virtue of which it has four strengths there. It is its triplicity, by virtue of which it has three strengths. It is also its face, by virtue of which it has one strength. Therefore, Saturn has 8 strengths in the place of the part of wheat. After Saturn is Venus, which is its house, and it has 5 strengths there. And Jupiter has its term there. I will look at the state of each of these in the figure, and according to their state, I will see about the fate of wheat. First, I will look at Saturn, what state it has in the figure, and I find it in the angle of the earth, not distant from the angle by 4 degrees. This signifies that wheat should be expensive, but not too much, because the angle is not strong, for the strongest of the angles in this regard is the Midheaven, then the ascendant, then the angle of the earth, and finally the western angle. But because Saturn is retrograde and peregrine in its place, having no dignity in its place, it signifies that wheat will be of little value at the beginning of the year. And when Saturn begins to become direct, its price will rise and it will be more expensive. This is the signification of Saturn. Then I will look at the state of Venus, and I find it in the 2nd house, its own house. This similarly signifies that wheat will be somewhat expensive. I will also look at the same part in the figure of the revolution of the same year. I say that the ascendant of the revolution in the aforesaid tables will be the fourth degree, 15 minutes, 26 seconds of Libra. The distance between the Sun and Mars will be 1 sign, 45 degrees, 3 minutes, 59 seconds. I will compute this number from the ascendant, and the number terminates in Capricorn, 19 degrees, 19 minutes, 25 seconds. Mars has its exaltation and triplicity in the place of this part, so it has seven strengths there. Saturn has its house and face there, so it has six strengths there. Mars is stronger in the place, and it is in the angle of the Midheaven. This signifies that wheat should be expensive, but because Mars is in its fall from its exaltation, it will not be expensive until it leaves its fall. This writing on Alchabitius, ordered by John of Saxony in the town of Paris, in the year 1331, is finished and corrected.
